## Welcome to the Grim Darkness of the Far Future

**Warhammer 40,000** is a tabletop game where you command an army of mighty warriors. It is also a wide-ranging hobby that includes collecting, building, and painting **Citadel Miniatures**. This book serves as a launching pad for all of these activities – and much more!

The **Warhammer 40,000 hobby** offers a unique window into a world of excitement and adventure set in the **Dark Imperium**, where the empire of **Mankind** is beset from all sides. **Daemon-worshipping heretics** and myriad alien horrors surge from the darkness between the stars, intent upon bringing ruin and discord to the **Emperor’s realm**.

Against them stand the resolute armies of the **Imperium**, from the superhuman **Space Marines** and the pious **Sisters of Battle** to the innumerable ranks of the **Astra Militarum** and the towering war engines of the **Knight households**. A million worlds burn with the fires of war even as they echo to the monstrous laughter of the **Dark Gods**.

This apocalyptic setting provides endless opportunities for collecting, building, painting, and gaming.

### Ways to Enjoy the Hobby

- Collect vast armies and fight epic battles described in the background.
- Paint beautiful display figures and build scenic snapshots of strange alien worlds.
- Build amazing war machines.
- Spend time with like-minded friends, painting or gaming together.

There is no right or wrong way to engage with the Warhammer 40,000 hobby – it’s best to find what you most enjoy and pursue it.

From gaming tournaments and campaign events to world-class painting competitions, from dining table warfare to exciting battles at local clubs, the Warhammer 40,000 universe offers a world of fun. Strap on your armour, load your bolter, and get ready for war!

---

## Collecting Citadel Miniatures

The range of **Warhammer 40,000 Citadel Miniatures** is incredibly vast and varied, from ground-shaking war engines to scuttling xenos swarms, heavily armed combat aircraft to brave infantrymen and courageous heroes.

Grand armies surge into battle across war-torn worlds. Regiments of infantry dig in behind corpse-shored barricades. **Space Marine Drop Pods** streak down from orbit through burning skies to disgorge armoured warriors into the heart of the foe. Artillery pieces roar as they fling megatonne explosives into enemy ranks, while hurtling xenos skimmers and rumbling, spike-studded tanks duel through blazing ruins of once-glorious cities.

Everywhere, storied heroes and black-hearted villains lock blades, screaming praise to their uncaring gods as they battle to the death.

### Reasons to Collect

A big part of the hobby is collecting warriors and war machines, building and painting them to create an exciting and diverse collection.

- Many hobbyists collect armies to play games of Warhammer 40,000, including heroes, warriors, vehicles, and monsters.
- Some collect and paint mightiest heroes or assemble collections around themes like tanks, aerial armadas, or elite specialist teams.
- Others base collections on stories from **Games Workshop’s novels** and gaming supplements.

Whatever your inspiration—display, tabletop wargaming, or both—the hobby is exceptionally rewarding. Watching your collection grow from a handful of models to a fully realized army brings pride and achievement.

Most collections begin with a few miniatures like a squad of warriors, a character model, or a **Start Collecting!** box.

Examples include:

- A **Genestealer Cult army** growing to encompass a variety of unit types.
- A **Blood Angels army** that is mobile and resilient, with transports, fast-moving infantry, tanks, heavy troops, and mechanized walkers.

---

## Building and Painting

Constructing and painting **Citadel Miniatures** is a tactile and satisfying experience. Whether following instructions or creating custom conversions and bespoke colour schemes, this part of the hobby lets you personalise your collection!

The **Citadel Paint System** works layer by layer, building from basecoats and washes to highlights and special effects, creating jaw-droppingly impressive models. It's a straightforward system with highly rewarding results.

### Assembly

Most **Citadel Miniatures** do not come pre-built. They are assembled using modelling tools and glue, then painted in colours and schemes that you choose.

**Games Workshop** produces specialist tools and a huge selection of **Citadel Paints**, which include the Citadel Paint System to easily and enjoyably build and paint miniatures.

Many enjoy the creative process, taking pride in making the best-looking miniatures possible. A well-painted army brings Warhammer 40,000 to life, making you almost hear the tank engines roar and bolters boom.

Adding **Citadel terrain**, built and painted to complement your army, adds to an epic tabletop narrative that can live on as a war story among your gaming group for years.

### Building Skills

Initially, building and painting may seem daunting, but with a few easy techniques such as **basecoating**, **washing**, and **drybrushing**, and some practice, you will be amazed by your results.

Information on the Citadel Paint System is widely available from:

- Games Workshop staff
- Internet tutorial videos
- Citadel publications

Whether crafting a single, beautiful model for competitions or batch-painting companies and squadrons ready for battle, the only limit is your imagination. Your skills will grow with every project until you become a master artisan.

### Assembly Process

- Citadel Miniatures are provided unassembled and unpainted.
- Using **Citadel Fine Detail Cutters** and assembly instructions, you clip components from plastic frames.
- Models are assembled piece by piece using plastic glue.
- Model customization through head swaps and re-posing allows creating unique army additions.

### Painting

- After assembly, miniatures are painted in chosen colours.
- Games Workshop provides painting guides, walkthroughs, and instructional videos.
- Possible colour schemes inspire creative efforts.
- Visit [games-workshop.com](https://games-workshop.com) for the entire range of paints, products, books, and step-by-step videos.

---

## Warhammer 40,000 Gaming

Mighty armies advance across tabletop battlefields to bring ruin to their foes. Desperate last stands and heroic duels unfold amidst blasted cityscapes and carnivorous alien jungles. Every game tells a dramatic tale, immersing players deeper in the war-torn galaxy of the far future.

### The Warhammer 40,000 Universe

The universe is vast and home to many factions vying for dominance.

- The **Imperium of Man** opposes **Chaos-tainted traitors** and heretics.
- Vile **xenos** seek to invade whenever possible.

Battlefields are grand and fantastical, including:

- Grim fortress monasteries
- Gothic hive cities the size of continents
- Arid crystalline deserts
- Volcanic death worlds
- Ancient alien techno-crypts
- Any landscape your imagination can conjure

### Battles and Warfare

- Range from elite commando raids and assassination missions to immense battles between millions of warriors.
- Include deadly dogfights through city spires.
- Crashing tank battles over fiery plains.
- Thunderous firefights between demigod war engines.
- Desperate battles to banish **Daemons** back to their hellish origins.

Warhammer 40,000 offers limitless possibilities.

### Types of Gameplay

For many hobbyists, playing tabletop wargames is the desired outcome of gathering and painting an army.

- Game types vary from friendly storytelling to highly competitive tournament play.
- The hobby offers opportunities for narrative play, head-to-head deathmatches, and ongoing campaigns of conquest.

### Learning and Growing

Many start small, learning rules by battling with a handful of squads. As collections grow, options expand.

Soon you will plunge into the grim darkness of Warhammer 40,000 and fight battles remembered for years.

Example: Steve and Natalie use their **Death Guard** and **Ultramarines** in battle. A game this size can last a couple of hours.

Numerous missions to play and enjoy are included later in this book.

---

## Open Play

Totally unrestricted, **open play** is the quickest and easiest way to play Warhammer 40,000.

- Requirements: some models, a copy of the rules, a few dice, a tape measure, and an opponent.
- Fun and friendly, open play lets you use any models.
- Often involves players using their entire collections to see what happens.
- Results are spectacular, providing memorable war stories for post-game discussion.

---

## Narrative Play

Although impromptu battles are quick and fun, many prefer to forge carefully thought-out narratives.

- Develop strong themes for armies with unifying colour schemes and backgrounds.

## Narrative Play

**Narrative play** involves players using their games and battlefields to tell exciting **stories**, often creating an overarching **narrative** to bind several games into a **campaign**. It’s a fantastic way to take your hobby to the next level.

## Matched Play

Many players enjoy the more competitive element of the **Warhammer 40,000** hobby, playing games to see who can come out on top. **Matched play** facilitates this by bringing an extra level of **balance** to players’ armies.

- Places restrictions upon the **units** they can take
- Allows an even number of **points** to pick their forces
- Most commonly seen at **gaming tournaments** and events
- Guarantees a close-run and nailbiting battle regardless of armies or players

---

## 19 DARK MILLENNIUM

> “We are beset on all sides by vile predatory aliens and sedition gnaws at us from within; in this dark hour the best we can do is look to our wargear and pray to our gods.”  
> — **Skolak a’Trellar IV, Imperial Commander**

### Thought for the Day: Beware the Enemy Within!

---

## The Imperium of Man

After more than **forty thousand years** of war and strife among the stars, **Humanity** stands on the brink of **extinction**. Beset on all sides by hostile aliens and threatened from within by **traitors**, Humanity’s survival rests with the cruel and bloody regime known as the **Imperium**.

Few amongst Mankind’s untold population realise the full truth of their situation or the horrible fate looming beyond the stars. If there is any future at all, it is a **grim one**…

The **Imperium** stretches across the galaxy. At its heart is **Holy Terra**, the cradle of Humanity and starting point of an empire containing countless **trillions** of souls.

Despite its size, the Imperium is spread thinly; its worlds are scattered and often divided by thousands of light years. It is a **sprawling** and disconnected domain, expanding despite isolation and unexplored regions.

---

## Lost Ages of History

Some **four hundred centuries** (forty thousand years) have passed since man first stepped into space. An age so long that almost all its history lies shrouded in **legend**.

- Origins of Mankind's scattering across worlds remain unknown
- Wars that split Terra and reduced Humanity to brutal savagery are forgotten
- Names of ancient ruins, nations, and peoples long lost to dust remain mysteries

Only **whispers** remain of the **Age of Technology**, the **Realm of Night**, the **Empire of Blood**, and the long **Age of Strife**.

---

Now is the **Age of the Emperor**, the **Age of the Imperium**, dark days indeed. This age is already ten thousand years old, steeped in myth and ignorance.

- Great and unfathomable technologies enslaved by mysticism and madness
- Era of constant war, where **survival** is hailed as victory
- Defeat leads to the **end of Humanity**

---

## The Emperor

When the **Emperor** led Mankind across the galaxy over a hundred centuries ago, an age of regression and isolation ended. It marked the launch of the **Great Crusade** and a brief enlightenment before the horror of the **Horus Heresy**.

Ancient records are sparse; legends tell of the creation of the **Space Marines** and the brutal history now half-remembered. Some secrets may be locked away in hidden Imperial libraries, but exposure would mean heresy and death.

---

Once, the **Emperor** lived as a mortal man, but his physical life ended crushed by **Horus, the Arch-traitor**, in the final battle for Terra. 

Today the Emperor survives only by his **supreme will**, preserved by the **Golden Throne**, a machine of stasis fields and psi-fusion reactors.

- His broken body is kept alive artificially
- His immense **psychic powers** protect Humanity across the galaxy
- Must hold back the forces of **Chaos**, preventing Daemons and destruction

If he fails, reality itself will be consumed by **the Warp**, a realm of terror and madness where only **Chaos** remains.

---

## The Imperium Lives

The Emperor has neither spoken nor moved since his imprisonment in the Golden Throne. His body is effectively dead, but his mind wages an eternal battle against the horrors of the Warp.

- His consciousness is divorced from material reality  
- He is incapable of ordinary communication  
- He gave everything so the Imperium could endure  

Now worshipped as a **god**, the Emperor’s name guides the Imperium through superstition and blind obedience. 

- The **High Lords of Terra** rule in his name  
- The vast bureaucracy of **Adeptus Terra** enforces laws, collects taxes, commands armies  
- No individual is free from its influence  

Despite constant war and threats from **xenos** and **Chaos**, the Imperium persists, fueled by fear and faith.

---

## The Cogs of the Empire

The Imperium’s organisations wield shifting power, their agents and armies sometimes cooperating, often clashing.

- Civil wars erupt frequently over ideological differences  
- Innovation is often suppressed, fearing heresy  

---

## Orbits of Power

The many organisations of the Imperium are so complex that detailing all would take a lifetime. The main pillars remain, their influence waxing and waning according to the dictates of **Holy Terra**.

---

### Hierarchy of the Imperium

#### High Lords of Terra

- Twelve individuals who govern Mankind’s destiny  
- Rule in the **Emperor’s name**  
- Command Imperial fleets and armies  
- Interpret the Emperor’s will through his psychic presence  
- Nine seats are sacrosanct, including Master of the **Administratum**, Paternoval Envoy of the **Navis Nobilite**, and Fabricator General of the **Adeptus Mechanicus**

#### Adeptus Terra

- Known as the **Masters of the Earth**  
- The central bureaucratic organisation of the Imperium  
- Comprised of many autonomous departments  
- Pass orders from the High Lords down through various branches  

#### Adeptus Administratum

- The largest organisation within Adeptus Terra  
- Divided into countless branches  
- Manage daily Imperial governance  
- Responsible for **tithes**, administration, records, and archives  
- Tasked to perform duties without requiring understanding  

#### Adeptus Ministorum

- Also called the **Ecclesiarchy**  
- Promulgators of the **Imperial Creed** throughout the Imperium  
- Spread the **Imperial Cult** and enforce religious doctrine

## Ecclesiarchy

The **Ecclesiarchy** is not part of the **Adeptus Terra** but is a separate institution that hosts numerous subgroups of its own. The best known of these are:

- Its military wing: the **Adepta Sororitas**
- Orthodox training orphanages: the **Schola Progenium**
- Missionaries who often accompany Imperial exploratory vessels: the **Missionarus Galaxia**

---

## The Inquisition

Known as **"The eye that sleepeth not,"** the **Inquisition** is a highly secretive organisation. It is bound by no authority save its own and that of the **Emperor**. 

The sole mission of the **Inquisition** is the protection of **Humanity**. **Inquisitors** are empowered to investigate any potential threat to Mankind and take any measures necessary to destroy the danger. The end justifies any means.

---

## Navis Nobilite

Known as **Passage-makers** and **Bearers of the Third Eye**, the **Navis Nobilite** or **Navigator Houses** are led by the **Paternova** and form the Terra-based organisation from which all **Navigators** come.

- Navigators are one of the few sanctioned breeds of mutant.
- They use their **third eye** to pilot human starships through the dangerous warp space.

---

## Adeptus Mechanicus

The **Lords of Mars** and **Disciples of the Omnissiah**, the **Tech-Priests** of the **Adeptus Mechanicus** are keepers of ancient knowledge and arcane technology.

- They preserve the **Emperor’s Golden Throne**
- Operate the forge worlds supplying weapons, armour, munitions, spaceships, and war machines
- Contain many subdivisions, including fleets and military wings
- Follow the **Cult Mechanicus** worship of the **Omnissiah**
- Use intricate invocations to assemble and maintain machines
- Headquartered on **Mars**, not Terra

---

## Adeptus Astra Telepathica

Their voices pierce the darkness and cross the stars. The role of the **Adeptus Astra Telepathica** is to:

- Recruit, identify, and classify **psykers**
- Train those found worthy

This organisation is divided into two main bodies:

- The **League of Black Ships**
- The **Scholastica Psykana**

The **Master of the Adeptus Astra Telepathica** presides over both. Many grades of psyker are classified, with acceptable grades serving the Imperium in various roles. Those unable to pass stringent tests are assigned less savoury duties.

The Imperium's colossal size and vast distances between planets mean communication is often impossible. Despite this, labyrinthine Imperial organisations struggle to maintain an increasingly dystopian order.

---

## Adeptus Astronomica

They fuel the guiding light of the **Emperor**. The **Adeptus Astronomica** trains psykers to provide the raw psychic power to fuel the **Astronomican** — the psychic homing beacon enabling Navigators to steer through the warp.

- This requires a choir of at least ten thousand psykers.
- The role quickly destroys the psykers.
- There are always more trained to replace them.

---

## Rogue Traders

The **hand that draws the map**, **Rogue Traders** are licensed and equipped to explore uncharted galaxy portions.

- They are **Emperor’s emissaries** to the unknown.
- Hold full authority to negotiate, barter, subjugate, or destroy
- Their pursuit feeds the Imperium’s appetite for information, territory, alien artefacts, and raw materials

---

## Planetary Governors

They rule in **His name**. Individual planets are ruled by local leaders who:

- Must provide troops for the **Astra Militarum**
- Maintain order
- Carry out all Imperial decrees
- Pay all tithes levied by the **Administratum**, especially the **tithe of psykers**

Planetary governors may rule as they wish if quotas are met.

---

## Adeptus Arbites

They are the **Keepers of the Great Book of Judgement**. The **Arbitrators** and **Judges** of the **Adeptus Terra** enforce law across the Imperium.

- Maintain absolute and unforgiving order
- Rigidly adhere to the letter of the law
- Breed fanaticism

---

## Adeptus Astartes

They know no fear, the **Angels of Death**. The **Adeptus Astartes**, or **Space Marines**, are the most powerful and feared warriors of Humanity.

- Approximately one thousand **Chapters**, each with one thousand warriors
- Maintain their own identity and traditions
- Autonomous from the Ecclesiarchy
- Highly mobile shock troops trained for rapid deployment and combat anywhere

---

## Astra Militarum

The **Hammer of the Emperor**, the **Imperial Guard** is the largest fighting force of the Imperium.

- Relies on vast numbers of soldiers, armoured tanks, and artillery
- Crushes foes through attrition and overwhelming firepower
- Provisioned by the **Departmento Munitorum**, the **munitions and supply wing** of the **Adeptus Administratum**

---

## Imperial Fleet

They who ply the stars and bear the biggest guns. All shipping in the Imperium falls under the **Imperial Fleet**, except that operated by the **Adeptus Astartes** and few other organisations.

- The largest segment is the **Imperial Navy**
- Composed of battleships, cruisers, escort squadrons, transports, messenger craft, orbital defences, and patrol vessels
- Serve as first line of defence, escort cargo, and project Imperial war across the stars

---

## Officio Assassinorum

The **dagger in the dark** and **silent answer**, this mysterious agency trains elite killers operating in utmost secrecy.

- Different temples make up the agency
- Only deployment allowed by the **High Lords of Terra**
- Assassins strike unseen and complete deadly missions by any means necessary

---

## Questor Imperialis

The **Glorious Households** and **Defenders from the Old Night.** An **Imperial Knight** is a giant armoured walker guided by a single Noble pilot.

- Many pilots trace bloodlines back to Terra
- Pilots swear oaths of fealty: 
  - **Imperial Knights** to the Golden Throne of Terra
  - **Mechanicus Knights** to the **Adeptus Mechanicus** of Mars
- Knights who forsake their households become **Freeblades**, adopting new heraldry and fighting independently

---

## Adeptus Custodes

The **Bodyguards of the Emperor** and **Protectors of the Sanctum Imperialis**, the **Adeptus Custodes** or **Custodian Guard** have an elite role.

- Ten thousand strong, genetically engineered superhumans
- Capable of besting even Space Marines in combat trials
- Serve as the Emperor’s personal guardians
- Answerable only to the **Master of Mankind** and their own leaders
- Occasionally seen off Terra during dire emergencies

---

## Empire Lost Among the Stars

For **ten thousand years**, the Imperium endured one hundred centuries of constant war. Then a great darkness descended: the **Cicatrix Maledictum – the Great Rift**.

- Warp storms of unprecedented scale and power struck the galaxy
- Hundreds of thousands of planets were lost or rendered silent
- Scribes and curators sought answers in neglected records and ancient vaults
- The **Ruinstorm** had split the galaxy during the **Horus Heresy**, but the current division surpassed all prior disruption; this age is known as the **Age of Strife**
- The Age of Strife marked the end of civilisation, with Mankind enslaved or reduced to barbarism

Despite crises:

- The Imperium remained the galaxy’s largest empire
- It survived civil wars, loss of the Emperor’s direct leadership, and the **Age of Apostasy**
- Corrupt ideologues subverted the Emperor's word to gain power
- Wars, schisms, betrayals, and a religion outlawing reason tested the Imperium
- Planets and star systems were lost continuously to sedition, xenos invasion, and cosmic phenomena
- Communication failures and bureaucracy obscured losses, but the Imperium grew

Explorator fleets relentlessly sought new colonies and systems to exploit even as others fell away.

---

## The Great Rift and Its Effects

The **Great Rift** shocked reality, cracking the galaxy asunder:

- A tidal wave of dread and psychic agony swept sentient beings
- Psychically attuned suffered most as warp energies poured into realspace
- Billions perished, their pain a psychic cacophony
- A turbulent scar of raw, pulsing **Chaos** ran from the **Hadex Anomaly** in the **Jericho Reach** to the farthest reaches of the **Segmentum Obscurus**
- This scar severed the galaxy on a massive scale, rupturing the seams of reality in unimaginable ways

## The Eye of Terror and the Great Rift

The **Eye of Terror**—the largest and most dreaded of all **warp rifts** previously known—became but a small fraction of a massive new rent. The **warp storms** issuing forth from the gaping void swept to every corner of the galaxy, severing all **astrocommunication** from millions of Imperial planets.

- Only worlds sharing a **solar system** remained in contact, and even that failed during the height of the tempests.
- The number of **Imperium planets lost** remains unknown.
- The **Astronomican**, the Emperor’s guiding beacon, blinked and then vanished.

Psychic aftershocks washed the galaxy as reality struggled to recover from the horrific trauma. Eventually, some worlds discovered that **Astropaths** could once again transmit interstellar messages, despite the risk of deadlier **daemonic incursion**.

Crusades were launched to re-establish contact and retake lost systems. The most successful was the **Indomitus Crusade**, led by **Roboute Guilliman**, the returned **Primarch** and **Lord Commander of the Imperium**. Wherever he traveled, faith returned.

Despite efforts, few messages or spacecraft could cross the hellish new barrier that split the galaxy: the Great Rift. The fractured **Imperium of Mankind** became broken and isolated but persisted. The banners of the myriad armies of Mankind still flew high across countless worlds.

---

## Warhammer 40,000 Mottoes

- **"DEATH BRINGS NO PEACE TO THE UNFAITHFUL."**  
  Let every blade, bullet, step, and word be aimed at Chaos's downfall.

- **"HERESY GROWS FROM IDLENESS."**  
  The galaxy rightfully belongs to **Mankind**, and the Emperor’s works will endure by the might of the **Adeptus Astartes**.

---

## Mankind and the Immaterium

The history of Mankind’s greatest successes and tragedies is directly linked to **warp space**, also known as the **immaterium** or simply the **warp**. 

- The discovery of warp space enabled the first **human colonizations** by achieving **faster-than-light** travel.
- The warp allowed Mankind's expansion but was also the source of collapse at the end of the **Age of Technology**.
- The warp is an infinite and incomprehensible realm inhabited by **malignant entities**, including the four **Great Gods of Chaos**: **Khorne**, **Tzeentch**, **Nurgle**, and **Slaanesh**, and their legion of **Daemons**.
- These forces seek the galaxy's destruction and to possess every living soul.

Daemons cannot easily leave the immaterium; they require gateways such as the unprotected mind of a **psyker**. Psykers draw power from the immaterium but risk **daemonic possession** without proper training or exceptional will.

**Warp storms**—violent, sudden outbursts from the immaterium—cause brief Daemon incursions. Such storms plagued the galaxy irregularly, especially during the **Age of Strife**, when vast storms raged unchecked for centuries.

The **Emperor** rose to power on Terra during the decline of these storms. He led the **Unification Wars** and then the **Great Crusade**, reclaiming lost colonies and ending Mankind’s greatest darkness.

---

## The Astronomican and the Great Crusade

The Emperor ordered the construction of the **Astronomican**, a beacon broadcast from Terra by a choir of psykers and focused by the Emperor's will. This beacon:

- Shone through warp space, allowing **Navigators** to plot courses through the warp’s chaotic currents.
- Enabled Mankind to expand from Terra, founding the **Imperium**.
- Its light defined the Imperium’s borders for nearly ten millennia.

Navigators could travel within a radius of the Astronomican, but many distant sectors lay beyond its reach, such as the **Eastern Fringe** or the **Ghoul Stars**. Rogue Traders sometimes explored these blind spots by conventional travel.

Warp anomalies such as **warp rifts** (e.g., the Eye of Terror) created regions where travel was limited or impossible. These rifts stirred fierce warp storms, dimming or blotting out the Astronomican. Without its signal, navigators faced madness, mishaps, or worse.

---

## The Great Rift and Imperium Nihilus

A chain reaction of tears in the warp divided the galaxy, leaving a massive scar of pure Chaos known as the **Great Rift**. The **Noctis Aeterna** followed—a period when the Astronomican was swallowed by the storm.

- For some time, only intermittent flashes of the beacon were visible, as if the Emperor battled the storm.
- Half the galaxy’s beacon returned but with interruptions.
- The **galactic north**, called **Imperium Nihilus**, lost the beacon entirely, leaving worlds blinded and isolated.

---

## Navigators

**Navigators** are a stable breed of human mutants existing long before the Imperium. Originating during the **Age of Technology**, the **Navis Nobilite** (Navigator Houses) have persisted through the **Age of Strife**.

- Navigators are physically unique, all possessing a **third eye**, key to their power.
- This eye allows them to see warp currents and safely pilot spacecraft through the immaterium’s maelstrom.
- Their mutation is the result of ancient **genetic experimentation**.
- Without Navigators, the Imperium would be fragmented like the Imperium Nihilus, forced to risk blind warp jumps.

Although Age of Technology beacons are lost, the **Astronomican** provides a steering reference for their navigation.

---

## Worlds of the Imperium

The Imperium claims over a **million planets**, a vast number yet only a tiny fraction of the galaxy’s stellar systems. Data on these worlds is contradictory or outdated.

### Civilised Worlds

- **η-class [Hive Worlds]**  
  Host huge urban conglomerations spanning continents and miles high. Hive worlds have immense populations ideal for recruiting **Imperial Guard** if anarchy is contained.

- **μ-class [Feudal Worlds]**  
  Societies have regressed to medieval states, some maintaining **Knight worlds** with reverence for **archeotech** relics.

- **фλ-class [Feral Worlds]**  
  Populations have devolved into savagery, some unable to use tools. These worlds pay the lowest **tithe grade** due to their primitiveness.

Many worlds were settled during the **Age of Technology** and reclaimed in the **Great Crusade**. Lost worlds continue to be rediscovered, but an exact count is impossible due to distances, poor communication, and galactic volatility.

The Imperium is divided into **five segmentums**, which are further broken into sectors and sub-sectors. Some worlds cluster near stable **warp translation points**, forming tightly-knit alliances such as the **Realm of Ultramar** or systems near **Terra**.

Most inhabited worlds are separated by vast voids, producing diverse cultures and technology levels. Worlds largely self-govern as long as the **Imperial Tithe**—a levy on manpower, manufacturing, and psykers—is paid.

---

## Exterminatus

**Exterminatus** is a dire order calling for the complete annihilation of life on a planet. Such orders arise only from the highest Imperium authorities:

- **Space Marine Chapter Masters**
- **Lord High Admirals** of the Imperial Navy
- **Lord Commanders** of the Astra Militarum
- **Inquisitors**

Exterminatus is issued only when no other solution or redemption exists.

## Exterminatus: Ultimate Sanction

**Exterminatus** is used to combat **planetwide heresy**, **rampant mutation or disease**, to prevent the opening or widening of **warp rifts**, or when **xenos** are so entrenched that the resources (including population) are beyond salvation.

- Methods vary but are uncompromising:
  - **Adeptus Astartes** deploy **Exterminatus devices** on the planet’s surface with kill teams to ensure absolute death.
  - The **Imperial Navy** uses sustained bombardment by battleships to hammer the world until it collapses.
  - The **Inquisition** uses **cyclonic torpedoes** and atmospheric incinerators.

---

## Planet Classifications in the Imperium

### 33α-class: Agri Worlds

Many planets, especially **hive** or **forge worlds**, cannot produce enough food. So, some worlds are wholly dedicated to agriculture.

- Managed by the **Adeptus Administratum** to maximize food production.
- Workers are often exploited or worked to death to meet hourly quotas.

### ф-class: Forge Worlds

Forge worlds belong to the **Adeptus Mechanicus**, planets dedicated to heavy industry and the **Cult Mechanicus** religion.

- The greatest forge world is **Mars**, home of the **Fabricator General**.
- These worlds are wreathed in pollution from massive machines that produce weapons for the Imperium’s armies.

### ρ-class: Research Stations / Fortress Worlds

- This classification overlaps between research stations and heavily garrisoned fortress planets.
- Some may be asteroid bases serving as surveillance posts or defensive strongholds for protecting shipping lanes or watching for **xenos** invasions.
- Often protected by orbital guns and fortified bunkers.

### δτ-class: Death Worlds

Death worlds are too dangerous for conventional human settlements.

- Example: **Catachan**, known for vast jungles and deadly flora and fauna.
- Despite the dangers, survivors make excellent recruits for the Imperium’s armies.

### ю-class: Mining Worlds

Planets rich in materials valuable to manufactorums and forge worlds.

- Workers, often enslaved or penal, harvest **ore**, **promethium**, gas clouds, or minerals.
- Found on barren or inhospitable worlds (e.g., lava oceans of Trollix, electro-clouds of Zeutus).
- The Imperium values materials over miners' lives.

### Chapter Planets

A **Chapter Planet** is the headquarters for an **Adeptus Astartes Chapter**.

- Exempt from normal Imperial Tithes.
- Can be a death, feral planet, space station, moon, or asteroid.
- The **Chapter Master** governs the planet, often recruiting locally.

---

## The Vastness of Space and Imperial Defenses

The Imperium's reach extends beyond planets and star systems:

- Defensive emplacements and man-made stations guard inhabited systems from **xenos** threats.
- **Battle stations**: planet-sized ports for fleets.
- **Starforts**: large forts acting as lynchpins of Imperial expansion.
- Artificial moons, doomsday bastions, and asteroid hazard zones bolster defenses.
- Arrays of listening probes and exploratory fleets search for new claims.
- Mining stations harvest resources even in remote regions.

---

## The Perils of Space Travel

Space is unforgiving, and many ships face numerous challenges:

- Malfunctions, mutiny, pirate raids, and accidents leave many derelict ships adrift.
- Ships using **warp space** face even greater hazards.
- Abandoned wrecks form gigantic **space hulks**, drifting unpredictably.
- Space hulks contain relics, xenos artifacts, and dangerous passengers.
- The **Noctis Aeterna** (the Blackness) unleashed thousands of dead fleets into realspace, bringing relics and horrors.

---

## Warp Storms and The Noctis Aeterna

The **warp** is highly volatile, and when its energies escape into realspace, catastrophic storms occur.

- Warp storms isolate sub-sectors, block travel and communications, and cut off the **Astronomican**.
- The **Blackness** during the Age of the Imperium was the most severe warp storm event.
- The **Cicatrix Maledictum** cracked the galaxy, severing the Emperor’s Light.
- Ships and fleets were buffeted, torn apart, or taken by **Daemons**.
- Entire planets and defense stations were displaced or destroyed.
- The warp storms caused time distortions and long-lasting devastation.
- Warp shockwaves appeared as multihued nebulas or monstrous forms.
- Communications failed, and **Astropaths** sending messages often died horrifically.
- Daemon legions, **Traitor Legions**, and **Chaos Renegades** resurged.
- Major wars decimated bastion planets like **Sabatine** and **Dhorthan**.

---

## In the Depths of Space

- The Imperium is held together by more than planets — **faith** played a unifying role from the beginning.
- The **Ecclesiarchy** grew from a small cult of disciples into the state religion.
- The **Emperor** was venerated as a living god particularly on primitive planets during the **Great Crusade**.
- After the **Horus Heresy** and the Emperor’s physical incapacitation, faith became a source of reassurance.
- Many cults arose, worshipping the Emperor in different ways but universally advocating for the survival of Humanity.
- Mutants, psykers, and aliens were to be destroyed without mercy.
- These sects were absorbed into the **Ecclesiarchy**, led by the **Ecclesiarch**, which became the **Adeptus Ministorum** in the early 32nd Millennium.

---

## The Official Founding of the Adeptus Ministorum

- First steps involved tightening control and persecuting dissenting cults.
- The **Ecclesiarchy** became the aggressive, dominant religious force in the Imperium.

---

## The Ecclesiarchy

**"There is no cowardice in faith."**

- With weaponry and warriors, a city or world may be conquered.
- But with **faith**, it is possible to conquer the galaxy itself.

## 36

Refused were declared **unbelievers** and the population was stirred to violence against them. The might of the **Ecclesiarchy** was such that it could call for **Wars of Faith** – military campaigns capable of overturning planets or whole systems.

Often this was done to further the **Imperium’s** goals, ridding it of **heretics**, **seditious unbelievers**, or **alien subversion**, but history is equally replete with examples of the Ecclesiarchy instigating bloody wars for its own gain. These wars secured enough wealth through falsely declared crusades to build the first of the **shrine worlds**.

Lavish **cathedrals**, massive statues, and monolithic triumphal arches heaped praise upon the **Emperor** but, more importantly to many, those pivotal hub planets granted vast political sway and were often rich in **mineral resources**.

The Ecclesiarchy’s influence spread, and few dared to question its motives. By the end of the **33rd Millennium** there was practically no open worship in the Imperium save for that condoned by the **Adeptus Ministorum**. The only exceptions were the domains of the **Adeptus Astartes** and the **Adeptus Mechanicus**, who were begrudgingly allowed to keep their unique traditions.

In the long ages since, this has led to distrust, and occasionally even open war, between the differing parties.

### THE HOLY MISSION

The servants of the Ecclesiarchy are fanatical in their quest to spread their religion. Given the size of the galaxy, the random nature of **warp storm isolation**, and the widely varied levels of cultural and technological advancement within the Imperium, the **Adeptus Ministorum** has found many belief systems already established on planets they visited for the first time.

This was not an impediment, for the Ecclesiarchy had become adept at assimilating all manner of creeds into the **Cult Imperialis** – the worship of the Emperor. This might mean erecting great cathedrals to impress hardened hive-dwellers, or teaching hunting tribes on feral worlds that the sun god they worshipped was in fact the glorious light of the Emperor.

The nuance of how the people bowed before the Master of Mankind was not as important as the act itself. For many centuries the Ecclesiarchy was content to play the long game. Their strategy, over time, reined in the more barbaric customs and gradually they usurped complete religious control.

Any local religions that resisted were ruled **heretical** and actively crushed by political or military means, whichever proved the most prudent.

As the **Age of the Imperium** grew darker, the fervour of faith became ever louder. To the superstitious masses, the **hellfire that cracked the stars** and the plethora of **warp-fuelled phenomenon** were clear signs of the **Time of Ending**.

In desperation, vast populations isolated and besieged by nightmare creatures called upon their Emperor to protect them. For most, the only answer was more carnage rained down from the stars.

**THERE IS NO FEAR IN CONVICTION.**

There are those amongst Humanity who cry out for hope, for freedom and an escape from duty and toil. Decry such traitors! There can be **no hope** in times such as these, save that which the **Emperor** offers. There can be **no freedom**, save that which the **Emperor** grants. There can be no cessation of toil, save that which **death** bestows, and even that final gift is the **Emperor’s to give – as He will**.

**LIFE IS A PRISON, DEATH A RELEASE.**

### A DEADLY EVOLUTION

Since the prolific **warp storms** of the **Age of Strife**, the rate at which humans develop **psychic powers** has steadily increased. Psychic minds appear as bright flames in the **immaterium**, ripe sweetmeats for the pandemonium of **planeshifters**, **Enslavers**, and **Daemons** that dwell there.

Recognising the substantial risk for **daemonic possession** and the spread of **Chaos**, the **Emperor of Mankind** attempted to control the growing epidemic. By his decree, the use of psychic powers was banned save for those sanctioned by the Imperium itself.

The ruler of every Imperial planet was to set aside a levy of young **psykers** for transport to Terra aboard the **Black Ships**.

Every day of the Age of the Imperium, the vast armadas of the **League of Black Ships** have plied the void, racing to collect their precious cargo across the galaxy before rushing homeward to Terra, their holds crammed full of frightened psykers.

Even with **psychic dampeners**, such journeys are fraught with danger. The threats are constant, as **warp travel** can unhinge unwary minds, sometimes causing psykers to release untold horrors.

An untrained psyker’s only chance of surviving the threats of the warp is to go unnoticed by the powers that stalk there. Without the discipline taught by the **Adeptus Astra Telepathica** and its **Scholastia Psykana**, a psyker has no chance of defending themselves against a hungry warp presence.

Many psykers are innocent of any malign intentions and the implications of their abilities, although this makes them no less dangerous. Others, far fewer in number, are aware of what hunts them and actively court the dreadful attention of warp entities, tempting a terrible fate for morsels of knowledge or power. When discovered, such tainted psykers are quickly eliminated.

Many psykers die en route to Terra, but those who survive are rigorously tested to work out their best use. Upon reaching the Imperial home world, the psykers are sorted, graded and assigned to various duties.

The vast majority are sent to the **Astronomican** to serve the great beacon – their lives are short, painful and culminate in an agonising death. A goodly number are deemed too unstable even for that duty. Most of these are lobotomised, becoming mindless **servitors**, but a few are spirited away to the **Obsidian Keep** in the heart of the Astra Telepathica palace complex where an unknown fate awaits them.

A very few are deemed fit for more active service. Of these, the main part are sent to the **Imperial Palace** to undergo the **Soul Binding** ritual. More die there, but the maimed survivors are inducted into the ranks of the **Astropaths**.

Others are sent to various departments – one in ten million may be mind-scrubbed and sent to serve the military as a sanctioned psyker, one in a hundred million may be mind-scrubbed and sent to a **Space Marine Chapter** to be reborn as a **Librarian**, and one in a billion may be worthy of serving as an **Inquisitor** or other high-status official.

Since the eruption of the **Great Rift**, the supply chain of the Black Ships has been severely interrupted. Planets cut off from their Imperial Tithe are forced to implement their own restraints upon their populations of untrained psykers.

---

## 39

**THOUGHT FOR THE DAY:**

**IT IS BETTER FOR A MAN TO BE AFRAID THAN HAPPY.**

---

## AGES OF MANKIND

Knowledge of the long ages of human history has been wreathed in **shadow**, buried beneath the aeons or simply lost over the expanse of time. Some **Historitors** continue to seek knowledge, but their work can be compared to holding a candle against the dark abyss.

The Historitors of the **Adeptus Administratum** seek, gather and dutifully collect the history of each planet within the Imperium. Once, perhaps, this was done with purpose. Now, however, it is most often an indiscriminate compilation of data, a process where scribes unthinkingly copy content onto scrolls, preserving complete records in constant fear of missing a single inconsequential letter.

The ability, or even desire, to translate what these facts mean in any larger sense is almost entirely absent, found only in a few individuals who are eyed suspiciously, or perhaps punished for their enthusiasm.

The largest and most complete collection of such records exists beneath the surface of **Terra**, where the colossal under-halls stretch out of sight – endless vistas of **datascrolls** tower upwards like mountains.

With flickering candlelight provided by floating **servo-skulls**, processions of curators, scriveners, and ciphers wind through the valleys, attempting to illuminate that which was.

Over the years, old truths have been lost to the adjustments and redactions made by revisionists of the **Adeptus Ministorum**, the **Inquisition**, and even the **High Lords of Terra** themselves.

---

## AGE OF TERRA: M1-M15

Little is known of this period save that, during this time, **Mankind** made its first forays from Terra into space.

**Mars** became the first planet to be terraformed when it was settled by industrial cartels. The red planet soon became synonymous with technical expertise and scientific advancement.

Colonies had to be self-sufficient, as many were isolated from Terra by long, dangerous journeys.

---

## AGE OF TECHNOLOGY: M15-M25

This era is referred to as the **‘Dark Age of Technology’** so often that its original title might seem incomplete.

There are few reliable records dating back to this epoch and even they seem to contradict themselves with regularity. What is known is that from roughly **M18** onwards, Mankind discovered the **warp** and how to enter it.

Slowly, through many disasters, Humanity learned to use the warp to make faster-than-light journeys out of their own star system.

It was during this time that the first alien races were encountered. Soon after, Mankind embarked upon the discovery, development and cultivation of the human **Navigator gene**, a controlled mutation that allowed human pilots to make longer warp jumps than previously thought possible.

Navigator families, initially controlled by industrial and trade cartels, had become individual forces in their own right by **M19**.

By **M20**, Humanity had proliferated and settled many of the countless star systems.

It was a golden age for scientific achievement; technology provided all the answers. Thinking machines aided civilian and military production, allowing enormous labours to be accomplished at a frenetic pace.

Perfection of the **Standard Template Construct (STC)** system permitted an explosion of colonisation that reached the furthest limits of the galaxy. This was the zenith of technological development and knowledge-sharing, for even the most far-flung colony had access to the entire inventory of human invention.

For the rest of the age, Mankind spread across the stars, becoming widely dispersed and divergent.

Evidence exists of many wars, but none that threatened the stability of human space. Amongst the records are lists of **xenos enemies** that have long since gone extinct, along with more familiar names such as **Aeldari** and **Orks**.

During this time period, interplanetary trade was established and great fleets carried goods to and from the ends of the galaxy.

*‘We endure an age of darkness, it is true, but still we shall be the lucky ones who do not live to see its end.’*  
– **General Valtor**, IV Drovian Dragoons

As planets became overpopulated, the recently invented construction mediums of **plasteel**, **plascrete**, **ferrocrete**, and **rockcrete** were used to build colossal cities, which became the **proto-hives**.

As quick as the expansion of Mankind’s domain had been, it was eclipsed by the speed of its collapse. The decline was so rapid and so nearly complete that little of those colonies, or the civilisations they spawned, remain.

Speculation is rampant, but there are few facts. What is known is that **human psykers** were first mentioned towards the end of **M22**, making a sudden appearance on almost every human world within a relatively short span of time.

By the end of **M23**, there was widespread anarchy, descriptions of what must be **daemonic possessions**, and great turbulence in the warp.

Some records also cite betrayal by the machines and a great war with robotic armies.

Whether factual or allegorical, the histories leave no doubt on one point: the golden age had come to a spectacularly swift and brutal end.

---

## AGE OF STRIFE: M25-M30

Marked by terrible wars and massive invasions that tore **Humanity** apart, this age was a time of collapse.

**Warp storms** of unprecedented ferocity isolated Mankind’s colonies.

## The Age of Strife and the Rise of the Emperor

The great distances prevented almost all contact between **colonised planets**, and those close enough to remain in communication often became embroiled in internal battles for control. The separated **human cultures** rapidly diversified. Humanity itself began to evolve, with **mutations** regularly appearing on most planets and, on some worlds, altering into something new: the first of the **abhuman races**.

Civilisations that persecuted recently developed **psykers** fared the best. Worlds where such abilities were encouraged seem to have been destroyed altogether. Some wonders of the **Age of Technology** were lost or destroyed in flames of conflict, while others fell into neglect. **Mankind** was brought to its knees, and this horrific state continued for nearly **six millennia**.

When humanity finally emerged from the long darkness, it was **forever altered**. **Science** was no longer the answer but something to be feared. As legends tell, late in the Age of Strife, a force slowly reconciled old grudges between the warring factions of Terra and Mars. The long campaign called the **Unification Wars** was ended. This new leader was known only as the **Emperor**.

Even as he prepared to reclaim the wider galaxy, a final mighty surge of the Age of Strife’s **warp storms** lit up the skies. This phenomenon was recorded by planets all across the galaxy. When the scintillating burst died, it left the **warp somewhat becalmed** and the galaxy scarred by what would later be known as the **Eye of Terror**.

With the quelling of the warp storms, the **Emperor** and his newly formed Legions of **Space Marines** turned their attention to the stars, beginning the **Great Crusade**.

## The Great Crusade and the Emperor's Campaign

Using the psychic beam of the newly created **Astronomican**, **Navigators** could plot courses through the warp to cover vast distances of realspace quickly. The Great Crusade advanced outwards in many directions at once, driving back **xenos** and creatures of the warp alike.

Over hundreds of battles, the Emperor reclaimed many of the earlier colonies and was reunited with the lost **Primarchs** — his superhuman creations whose **geneseed** had been used to make the Space Marine Legions. The Primarchs had been stolen by the **Dark Gods** while still in their gestation pods.

The Emperor’s crusade brought an end to the despair of the Age of Strife and began a new period of human history.

> **“DIVEST YOURSELF OF MERCY, FOR MERCY IS A WEAKNESS. DIVEST YOURSELF OF COMPASSION, FOR COMPASSION IS A WEAKNESS. DIVEST YOURSELF OF HOPE, FOR HOPE IS A WEAKNESS. WHEN NOTHING REMAINS WITHIN BUT HATE, AND THE PURITY OF YOUR PURPOSE, THEN YOU WILL BE STRONG.”**  
> — Sergeant Golgaar, Iron Hands Clan Company Raukaan

## Age of Darkness and the Horus Heresy

A new era had begun, but the bright dawn envisioned by the Emperor was not to be. The fledgling **Imperium** was torn asunder by the great betrayal of the **Horus Heresy**. Human pride and ambition opened the door for the treacheries of the **Dark Gods**.

The **Great Crusade** was spearheaded by the newly formed **Space Marine Legions**, armed by the factories of **Mars** and supported by the **Imperial Army**. Forces of the Emperor were unstoppable, driving back **xenos** and warp creatures, reclaiming planet after planet in the name of Humanity.

One by one, the twenty missing **Primarchs** were found and reunited. During the Great Crusade, the Emperor preached three great truths:

- Genetic corruption must be **sought out and eradicated**  
- Psykers were to be uncovered, controlled, and evaluated by Imperial agents  
- Destructive xenos were to be rendered powerless  

The Imperium was re-established as the largest single empire in the galaxy.

Deciding it was time for the next phase of enlightenment, the Emperor handed control of the new Space Marine Legions to his sons, the **Primarchs**, while he returned to **Terra**. In his stead, **Horus**, Primarch of the **Luna Wolves** (later the Sons of Horus), was named first amongst equals and given the title **Warmaster**.

### The Great Betrayal

At the dawn of this new era, great sacrifice was demanded. Turning his back on the Emperor, the Warmaster **Horus**, the Emperor’s most trusted commander, committed the ultimate betrayal. Embracing the will of the **Dark Gods**, he led a rebellion that set the galaxy aflame with bitter civil war.

A full third of the Imperium’s forces joined Horus, including half of the Space Marine Legions. Brother fought brother, creating myths and grudges that still echo throughout the galaxy. Warriors of legend clashed and planets were cracked beneath their titanic struggles.

Horus carved a bloody path to Terra, invading the Emperor’s Palace amidst slaughter and war. Yet, heroically, the tide turned and Horus was struck down — but not before dealing the Emperor a mortal blow.

The shattered body of Mankind’s leader remained intact, held by his indomitable spirit until interred within the **Golden Throne**. Deep within the Imperial Palace, arcane technology sustains the Emperor’s spirit so he can continue to watch over Humanity. Bound physically, his **psychic powers** remain unfettered; he is still the **Master of Mankind**.

> **“No being is more accursed, more hateful and despised, than the traitor. Show neither mercy nor compassion to such heretics; they deserve only your hate.”**

## Victory’s Heavy Toll

The Emperor’s survival is paramount because only his mind is powerful enough to direct the **Astronomican** — the psychic beacon guiding space travel.

However, generating this mental energy destroys the psykers who serve in the **Adeptus Astronomica**, reducing them to empty husks. Many die daily for the Imperium’s survival.

The Emperor cannot sustain himself by normal means; he requires **human life force**—specifically, **souls of psykers**. The Imperium’s **Black Ships** scour for emergent psykers across the galaxy.

Some psykers serve in the Adeptus Astronomica, but many are sacrificed to feed the Emperor’s mighty spirit slowly and agonisingly. Hundreds or even thousands must die daily for the Emperor, the Imperium, and all Humanity to survive.

The Emperor’s dream of enlightenment turned into an oppressive, harsh rule carried out in his name. Mankind regressed into religious obfuscation while the Emperor sat immobile and silent, a creature whose will extended over a million worlds but unable to act physically.

## Repercussions and the Age of Fear

The bitter fighting of the Horus Heresy marked the beginning of a new age founded in blood. After Horus’s death, the traitors splintered, but many wars remained.

The **Scouring** demanded countless victories to restore the Imperium from the brink of destruction. During this turmoil, the Imperium’s hierarchy transformed from direct rule by the Emperor to rule by a council in his name.

Suspicion and paranoia grew as betrayals were uncovered on more planets than first thought. Distrust became rampant, ushering in an era of fear and mistrust.

### Changes in Military and Government

- The **Legiones Astartes** were broken down into many smaller **Chapters** to prevent misuse of power.  
- **Roboute Guilliman**, Primarch of the **Ultramarines Legion**, oversaw this transition.  
- The **Imperial Army** was divided into the **Imperial Fleet** and the **Astra Militarum**.  
- The **Adeptus Administratum** spawned many separate branches, often with overlapping responsibilities.  
- The **Inquisition** was formed — a secretive organisation outside normal hierarchies, tasked with relentless vigilance to root out threats to Humanity.

> **“PERSEVERANCE AND SILENCE ARE THE HIGHEST VIRTUES.”**

## Aftermath of the Horus Heresy

Mankind became trapped within the bureaucracies of the Imperium. The Emperor, having reached the end of his natural life, survives only by the **Golden Throne** and continual human sacrifice.

Psykers continue to emerge in growing numbers and are barely controlled through constant suppression and vigilance.

There is only **war and constant battle**, and the menace from the **warp** looms ever larger.

## The Scouring: M31

The entire millennium was marked by the sprawling campaign of vengeance against heretic traitors scattered across the galaxy.

- **Loyalist forces**, led by the **Ultramarines** and **Space Wolves**, drove back surviving traitors.  
- Thousands of fallen regiments, star fleets of the Imperial Army, entire **Titan Legions**, and the **Dark Mechanicum** fought alongside the Traitor Legions.  

Many foes were purged, but the conflicts raged on, shaping the turbulent galaxy.

## The Scouring and Aftermath

The core of the **corrupted Space Marines** fell back and found refuge within the swirling chaos of the **Eye of Terror**. They were declared **Excommunicate Traitoris**, and all records and memory of the **Traitor Legions** were to be expunged from **Imperial archives**. The **Scouring**, however, was far from over.

It was a time of grim realisation for the **Imperium**, as the war-torn aftermath revealed the true scope of the **Horus Heresy’s betrayals**. Many more planets had been lured into helping the traitors than initially known. Some embraced their **corruption**, while others were misled or beguiled.

The search for the disloyal took on epic proportions. In the midst of the **Scouring** came the **Second Founding** and the formation of the **Adeptus Astartes**, one of many precautionary moves to prevent such a great betrayal again. Henceforth, suspicion, guilt, and recrimination became rife in the **Imperium of Man**.

---

## Xenos Rising: M32

With strength siphoned off by the countless battles of the previous millennium, the **Imperium** was ill-equipped to face the growing threat from myriad **xenos races**. These enemies became ever bolder and more predatory, closing in on all sides.

Even star systems once thought impregnable were besieged. Tragedy struck as **Roboute Guilliman**, **Primarch of the Ultramarines** and **Lord High Commander** of the Imperium, was mortally wounded by the **Daemon Primarch Fulgrim**.

---

## The Forging: M32-34

During this golden age of the **Imperium**, the **Adeptus Terra** began to bind important star systems under tighter control. **Astropath choirs** were set in relay positions across the galaxy, with major hubs on highly garrisoned worlds such as **Armageddon**, **Bakka**, and **Macragge**.

The **Imperial Cult** became the official religion, and the **Ecclesiarchy** increased control over the masses. Without the **Emperor’s guidance**, the Imperium’s direction was left to interpretation. Strict rules were imposed to avoid dissension, with fear ruling authority and ignorance among the lower menials.

The Imperium’s reign became ever harsher and uncompromising.

---

## Nova Terra Interregnum: M35-36

Also called the **Time of the Two Emperors**, the **Ur-council of Nova Terra** denounced the **High Lords of Terra** and claimed rule of the entire **Segmentum Pacificus**. For nine centuries, the Imperium was split in two, leading to civil wars, trade disputes, and wavering allegiances.

**Chaos cults** were behind many uprisings. The corruption was so prolific the **21st Founding of Space Marines** disastrously failed, requiring the **Grey Knights** and **Inquisition** to intervene and expunge the threat.

---

## Age of the Imperium

### The Age of Apostasy: M36

Following the **Nova Terra Interregnum**, a new age of dissent and power struggles erupted. This included the **Reign of Blood**—a conflict between the ruling **Ecclesiarch** and other **High Lords of Terra**—and the **Plague of Unbelief**, a galaxy-wide uprising of corrupt demagogues.

Only the **Horus Heresy** saw more bloodshed in internal strife.

### The Age of Redemption: M37-41

The sins of apostasy were purged in blood through systematic culling commanded by the **High Lords of Terra**. The **Imperial Cult** spread more widely than ever, leading to the burning of heretics on hundreds of thousands of planets.

Countless faith crusades were launched, depleting both **Imperial Guard regiments** and **Space Marine Chapters**. A famous event early in this period was the judgement of **Saint Basillius**, which found thirty Space Marine Chapters lacking in faith. The guilty chose to embark on crusades into the **Eye of Terror** over instant death, all opting for the dangerous mission.

### The Macharian Conquests: M41

Considered by many historians as the last of the Redemption Crusades and their zenith, **Lord Commander Solar Macharius** mustered the greatest army since the **Great Crusade**. In seven years, his armies reconquered a thousand worlds on the galaxy’s western fringes.

His glory led him into dark sectors never before touched by the Emperor’s light. Upon his death, the Imperium mourned deeply, but the territories he conquered soon fell into internal rivalry and war. The ensuing **Macharian Heresy** lasted seventy years, ended only by over one hundred Space Marine Chapters fighting together.

### The Waning: M41

Exhausted by the Redemption Crusades, many outlying worlds fell to **Ork invasions**, **Chaos insurgencies**, and other **xenos** threats. To combat growing anarchy, the **Adeptus Terra** imposed stricter rules and harsher punishments.

Portents of doom became incessant. The prescient foretold great ripples in the warp, like a swell disturbed by some colossal unseen menace.

### Tyrannic Wars: M41

The **Tyranids** entered the galaxy, initiating the **Tyrannic Wars**. **Hive Fleet Behemoth** destroyed the planet of **Tyran** and the **Thandros System** before being halted in the **Realm of Ultramar** at great cost.

Other Hive Fleets, including **Hive Fleet Kraken**, ravaged the **Aeldari craftworld of Iyanden**.

### The Great Rift: M41

A galaxy-spanning tear in reality, known as the **Cicatrix Maledictum** (also called the **Crimson Path**, **Mouth of Ruin**, **Warpscar**, and others), was ripped open. It brought terrible darkness that enveloped the galaxy and ushered in a new epoch.

---

## The Long War: M31-41

The great rebellion begun by the arch-heretic **Horus** has never ceased. The **Long War**—a term by the **Traitor Legions** reflecting their desire to complete Horus’ goal—continues across every segmentum.

The **Traitor Legions**, along with cults and rebellions, repeatedly assail the worlds of the **Emperor**. Thirteen times **Abaddon the Despoiler** has launched **Black Crusades**, massive invasions where Chaos powers unite against the Imperium.

The Long War is not only open combat. Plagues, anarchic iconoclasts, and covert cults are woven deep within the Imperium’s bureaucracy.

---

## Hope Rekindled

When the **Cicatrix Maledictum** tore through the galaxy, it brought darkness across the Emperor’s realm. Amid this gloom, a few heroes fought to keep hope alive.

Key to this time was the world of **Cadia**, a crux point of fate. By uniting factions in the **Eye of Terror**, **Abaddon the Despoiler** shattered the world that had resisted him for millennia.

The Imperium’s mightiest heroes—including **Belisarius Cawl**, **Saint Celestine**, and **Inquisitor Katarinya Greyfax**—bled defending Cadia but were ultimately forced to retreat to the ice world of **Klaisus**.

On Cadia, Abaddon destroyed mysterious geometric pylons that held back **Chaos** from the material dimension. With these lynchpins broken, **warp storms** ravaged the galaxy.

Meanwhile, the **Aeldari civilization** underwent massive upheaval. From the **craftworlders** and **Drukhari** rose the **Ynnari**, followers of the newborn deity **Ynnead**. They sought to defeat Chaos and restore the Aeldari.

The **Ynnari** allied with Cawl, Celestine, and Greyfax, and together they forged a path to **Ultramar**. Despite confused records, all agree the greatest miracle happened on **Macragge**, at the **Fortress of Hera**.

Here, **Roboute Guilliman**, **Primarch of the Ultramarines**, was reborn. Clad in war raiment, he drove heretics from his star system and pursued them into retreat. His desperate pilgrimage through the warp led him finally to **Terra**, where he communed with the **Emperor**.

From this meeting, Guilliman emerged with a grim new purpose.

---

## Imperium Structure and Major Regions

The galaxy holds an estimated **four hundred thousand million stars** and countless planets. About **one million worlds** are claimed by the **Imperium**, ruled by the **Emperor of Mankind**.

To govern and protect this expanse, the **High Lords of Terra** divided the galaxy into five major control zones known as the **Segmentae Majoris**:

- **Segmentum Solar** (home of Terra)
- **Segmentum Obscurus**
- **Ultima Segmentum**
- **Segmentum Tempestus**
- **Segmentum Pacificus**

The **Cicatrix Maledictum** (the **Great Rift**) necessitated the addition of the **Imperium Nihilus**, the region cut off from the light of the **Astronomican**.

Each **segmentum** is further subdivided into sectors and sub-sectors.

---

## Important Locations in the Imperium

- **Holy Terra**
- **Imperial Primus Palace**
- **Hall of the Astronomican**
- **Cathedral of the Emperor Deified**
- **The Halls of Judgement**
- **Scholastica Psykana**
- **Orbital Defence Systems**
- **Ecclesiarchal Palace**
- **Imperial Record GHR**

Notable worlds include:

- **Armageddon**
- **Macragge**
- **Bakka**
- **Cadia**
- **Ryza**
- **Mordian**
- **Fenris**
- **Prospero** (Planet of the Sorcerers)
- **Necromunda**
- **Terror & Mars**
- **Nocturne**
- And many others across all sectors and segmentae.

---

**"Prayer cleanses the soul, but pain cleanses the body."**

**"Submit to the will of the Emperor! Fight until your blade is blunted, your armour battered, your flesh bloodied, and your bones are splintered. Fight until your lifeblood spills and only duty sustains you. The Emperor expects no less."**

**"The Inquisitor is the conscience of the Imperium."**

## Galactic Orientation and Astrocartography

Although **space** is **three-dimensional**, the **galaxy** is largely **planar**, and so **Astrocartographers** refer to galactic locations using **cardinal directions** derived from those of **Holy Terra**. 

Thus, the **Eastern Fringe** was so named as it was far to the **galactic east of Terra**.

---

---

## Dark Imperium

**The Victor lives in honour; the vanquished dies in shame.**

Such was the turmoil during the creation of the **Great Rift** and the period following it that there could be no reliable accounts. As limited communications returned, **Historitors** and **Chronotechs** struggled to understand incoming reports.

With the influx of **warp energies**, time passed strangely—speeding up in some sectors and slowing in others.

---

## The Noctis Aeterna

As the chain reaction of the **Great Rift** cracked open the galaxy, **tidal waves of unnatural energies** spilled outward in sporadic fashion.

- **Warp storms** swept across everything.
- Not even the furthest reaches of the galaxy were spared their corrupting touch.
- Over a million planets of the **Imperium** were cut off from the **Light of the Emperor** as the **Astronomican** went out.

During that time, the **Imperium of Mankind** ceased to be – each planet became isolated, a speck of sanity buffeted by a raging tempest.

---

## Warp Storms and Chaos Incursion

The **warp storm** was beyond the ability of any technology in the Imperium to record; it was greater in size and power than anything previously recorded, perhaps since the lost era of the **Age of Strife**.

- Long-range **astrocommunications** proved impossible.
- The warp was in too much upheaval to permit travel.
- Starships in transit were destroyed or subjected to horrific battering.
- Survivors were carried far off course by the insane tides of unnatural energies.

Riding the crest of the warp storms’ shock waves came the forces of **Chaos**:
  
- The **Daemon legions** were the vanguard.
- Fleets of the **Traitor Legions** followed.
- The ragged masses of **Renegades** and their cults trailed behind.

---

## The Defence of Terra

As the first warp storms broke over **Holy Terra**, its pollution-filled skies turned a roiling **crimson**.

- **Khorne**, the **Blood God**, sent **eighty-eight cohorts** of his Daemon legions to assault the **Emperor’s Palace**.
- His aim was the glory of tearing down the **Golden Throne**.

The skies of Terra congealed into **blood clouds** that deployed the **red host** before the **Lion’s Gate**.

The gun batteries of the **Imperial Palace** were second to none, yet could not halt the red tide alone.

- Led by **Roboute Guilliman**, the **Lord Commander of the Imperium**, the **Primaris Space Marines**, **Adeptus Custodes**, and **Sisters of Silence** fought side by side.
- The **Chaos** assault was broken long before reaching the **Eternity Gate**, but the **High Lords** were shaken by the enemy’s boldness.
- Without the beam of the **Astronomican**, arcane machinery and protective devices were insufficient to halt the **fell powers** from materializing on **Holy Terra**.

In rage, **Khorne**’s fortress trembled. The heat of his outburst obliterated the essences of eight **Bloodthirsters** who led the failed attack.

---

## The Gate is Broken

**Cadia** stood proudly as the gate through which the enemy could not pass.

- For the entire **Age of the Imperium**, **Cadia** bore the brunt of countless **Chaos assaults**.
- It was a redoubt against horrors issuing from the **Eye of Terror**.
- In the **Dark Imperium**, there was no assurance where **Chaos** forces would attack, only that they would.

---

## The Cadian System and the Cicatrix Maledictum

Though Cadia was reduced to a burning wasteland by **Abaddon’s** endless assaults, the sister worlds fought hard to destroy the spearhead of the **Despoiler**.

- The **Great Exodus of Cadia** saw Imperial defense redeployed across the system.
- Every realm touched by the **Cicatrix Maledictum** was blighted by intense **Daemon storms**.

These howling tempests carried myriad types of death upon their winds. In these deadly storms, the scions of the **Dark Gods** emerged from the aether to battle the defenders of Mankind.

---

## The Hour of the Damned

Despite all communications being cut, distress calls reached the **Legion of the Damned**.

- When travel was impossible, they appeared unlooked-for.
- They struck on **Baal**, **Armageddon**, **Antagonis**, and hundreds of other planets.
- They spoke only with **bolter and chainsword**, punishing enemies of the Imperium before vanishing without trace.

Truly, the **hour of the damned** had come.

---

## A Light in the Darkness

From blackness came a light—a brief flash, then distant blinks.

- The rays of the **Astronomican** lanced outward from **Holy Terra**, piercing the galaxy’s maelstrom but unable to pierce the **Great Rift**.
- In the **north-eastern galaxy**, little or none of the Emperor’s guiding light penetrated.

Messages could again be sent through the warp, but many planets—on the Terran side of the Great Rift—did not respond.

- Slightly less than half of the 1,000 **Space Marine Chapters** were unaccounted for.
- Twelve **Space Marine Chapter Planets** were reported destroyed during the **Noctis Aeterna** and subsequent campaigns.

Some Space Marines, like the **White Consuls**, escaped destruction. Others, such as the **Sky Sentinels**, perished when **Magnus the Red**, Daemon Primarch of the **Thousand Sons**, overran their home world of **Pranagar**.

Should **Imperium Nihilus** regain contact, known losses may grow, revealing grim truths to the **Lords of Terra**.

---

## The Indomitus Crusade

After defending **Holy Terra**, **Roboute Guilliman** gathered a new armada.

- Included were elements of the **Adeptus Custodes**, **Silent Sisterhood**, and vast numbers of **Primaris Space Marines** from many new Chapters.
- Strike forces from over a dozen pre-existing **Space Marine Chapters**, led by the **Imperial Fists**, joined the fleet.

Thus began many new legends as Guilliman aided beleaguered planets—breaking sieges and sweeping away invaders to restore hope.

Word spread rapidly, hailed by those who received astropathic messages: the return of a **hero out of myth**.

Once more, a **demigod** of the past fought for the **Imperium of Mankind**.

---

## Quotes from the Dark Imperium

> **"The victor lives in honour; the vanquished dies in shame."**  
> — Dark Imperium  

> **"Those who are pure of heart and strong of faith have nothing to fear from the Black Templars, this is true. But who then, amongst the heaving, sinful masses of humanity, can truly count themselves as safe from our wrath?"**  
> — Marshal Gideon, **Black Templars**, Mephistari Crusade  

> **"Butcher your enemy’s warriors without mercy. Crush his armies and leave none alive. But do not stop there. Burn his cities. Bomb his worlds from orbit. Slaughter everything and everyone until he kneels in the ashes of those he sought to protect. Only then will he understand the true fury of the Dark Gods."**  
> — Haakor of the **Black Legion**

---

## The Stand at Armageddon

For much of the millennium, the planet **Armageddon** was a battleground.

- Initially invaded by **Chaos**, it later hosted a massive war between **Ork hordes** under **Ghazghkull Thraka** and **Imperial forces**.
- Though Ghazghkull left to find new stomping grounds, fighting continued.

The **Great Rift’s hellstorms** did not halt the fighting but transformed it.

- During the **Noctis Aeterna**, reinforcements for both sides were cut off or destroyed.
- Defenders had to fight each other and waves of **Daemons**.
- Temporary ceasefires occurred, with Orks and humans sometimes united against a greater threat, but these never lasted long.

When the **Astronomican** returned and warp travel became possible, relief forces found a changed landscape:

- Forces of **Tzeentch** and **Khorne** battled each other.
- Orks and Imperials took cover from dueling **Greater Daemons**.
- Half the planet had warped into a **Daemon world**, a hellish landscape overlaying war-torn hive world terrain.

Imperial forces, including **nine Space Marine Chapters led by the Salamanders**, stopped a ritual that would have brought **Angron** (Primarch of the **World Eaters**) back to the planet.

---

## Devastation of Baal

After sacrificing shield worlds to fend off the earliest **xenos** advance, the planet **Baal** faced an intense attack by **Hive Fleet Leviathan**.

- The **Tyranid fleet** was so vast it blotting out stars.
- **Lord Commander Dante** bolstered defenses of the Blood Angels’ home world and moons.
- He also sent pre-emptive strike forces to delay, mislead, and reduce the tyranid threat.
- Hundreds of splinter fleets were defeated.

The **Flesh Tearers** were the first to respond to Dante’s call for aid, and all successor Chapters except the **Lamenters** answered.

## The Siege of Baal and Hive Fleet Leviathan

Even the **Knights of Blood**, who had been declared **Excommunicate Traitoris** by the **High Lords of Terra**, arrived to bolster the defences. It was still not enough. Learning at an exponential rate, **Hive Fleet Leviathan** could not be thwarted by the same strategy twice.

Advancing steadily, their superior numbers cleared the sector of life before the xenos made planetfall upon **Baal** and her twin moons. The first nineteen waves, each larger than the last, were driven off at great loss to the **Blood Angels** and their successor allies. Five **Chapter Masters** fell in that bitter fighting, three in the Battle at the Dome of Angels alone.

The **Tyranids** began the process of draining Baal and her moons, absorbing even the rad-poisoned deserts of **Baal Secundus**. With their defences in ruin and the moons stripped and broken, the remaining Space Marines retreated back to the rubble of the Blood Angels’ sprawling fortress monastery. There, they prepared for a last stand as the next wave swept downwards.

Doom, it seemed, had at last come to the **Sons of Sanguinius**.

It was then that the **Great Rift** cracked open the galaxy, and the withered Baal System was blasted by the aetheric storms. Although no further attack waves came from the Leviathan fleet, not a single Imperial defender remained alive upon the last moon, **Baal Prime**.

On Baal itself there were already enough Tyranids to destroy the Imperial troops many times over. Even with no chance of victory, **Commander Dante** led his troops, each fighting retreat seemingly more hopeless than the last. 

As the final perimeter was broken, the stars reappeared. Looking skywards, the Tyranids sought contact with their hive fleet, but it was gone, replaced by a newly arrived **Imperial fleet**.

---

## TRUE FAITH IS BLIND AND JUSTIFIED

Like an angel of vengeance came **Roboute Guilliman** and his crusade. After many more battles, Baal was finally cleared of the xenos threat. A great rebuilding of both world and Chapter was undertaken, for the Blood Angels and their successors were sorely needed elsewhere.

What became of Leviathan is a mystery, although a clue was found upon the now-barren moon of Baal Prime. **Xenos skulls** were piled impossibly high in the much-reviled, eight-pillared symbol of one of the Blood Angels’ most terrible and ancient nemeses: the **Bloodthirster Ka’Bandha**.  

---

## TERRA RETALIATES

In an effort to seize the initiative, a strike force was mustered on **Terra**, supported by an entire army of **Adeptus Custodes**.

---

## PLAGUE OF PLAGUES

Something terrible came out of the **warp storms** as they roiled through the southern reaches of **Ultima Segmentum**. Where the seeds of corruption had been planted by the **Plague That Walks**, a new and terrible contamination spread. The diseased dead rose to claim the living.

Previously, the walking corpses could be destroyed, but now doing so only released hordes of **Nurglings** that writhed impossibly out of the withered flesh of the fallen. Hive worlds were toppled, and as the **Blackness** descended, there was no escape.

In the horrific ruins, **Cults of Corruption** slithered out of hiding, summoning forth further aid from the **Realm of Chaos** itself. So did systems fall, creating the **Scourge Stars** – a trio of sickly systems that had fallen to **Nurgle**.

From that power base, the **Death Guard** and Plague legions issued, systematically reaping planet after planet. On they spread.

It was none other than the Daemon Primarch **Mortarion** that brought the fabled **Realm of Ultramar**, gem of the whole segmentum, under siege. Plague bombardments rained down, so severe that once gloried hives became pits and agri worlds became slime-ridden ruins.

Chaos was encroaching on many fronts when **Roboute Guilliman** returned. It was his tactical acumen that first stabilised the many war fronts, and his **Spear of Espandor** counter-attacking campaign that successfully bought the forces of the Imperium still more time.
