Amongst the **Drukhari**, the Haemonculus Covens refuse their vision, desiring the souls of the dead for themselves.

The gladiatorial champion **Lelith Hesperax** has joined the Reborn, along with many of the **Wych Cults**, while the **Kabalites’** reactions to Ynnead’s disciples are varied. **Harlequins**, naturally, fight on both sides.

---

## Necrons

### Necron Awakening

After aeons of slumber, the **Necrons** have begun to awaken. Rising from their **stasis tombs**, the Necrons have returned to complete their terrible purpose.

Long ago, the **Necrontyr** forsook mortal flesh for bodies of near-impervious metal. When their dreams of galactic conquest soured, they sealed themselves inside hidden **tomb worlds**, awaiting a new age.

So long did the Necrons slumber that the galaxy all but forgot their existence. Even in the minds of the **Aeldari**, who once strove against the Necrons for mastery of the stars, did their memory grow dim.

The cold-hearted **Necron Overlords** and their implacable legions awakened to find their once great empire in decay and primitive life forms squatting in their ancient domains. They were not impressed.

### Necron Resilience and Technology

No longer creatures of flesh and blood, Necrons are androids that can survive crippling damage. Once rent, the metal from which they are formed flows back together, and severed limbs scrabble to reattach themselves.

Should irreparable damage occur, the Necron ‘phases out’, its body and consciousness teleported back to the nearest tomb-complex to remain in storage until a new shell can be forged.

The technologies by which this is accomplished are a mystery, and many contingencies, including self-destruct mechanisms, prevent that knowledge from falling into the covetous hands of lesser races.

While their technology is beyond the grasp of human understanding, the Necrons’ purpose seems brutally clear: they seek to cleanse the galaxy of upstart primitives and re-establish themselves as rulers.

### Necrons at War

From vast **crypt-fortresses**, the burnished legions emerge into the dying light of a war-torn galaxy. The Necrons are an implacable foe, a steel sea that ripples with the crackling energy discharge of their **gauss weaponry**.

- They advance remorselessly, unleashing precision volleys while remaining virtually impervious to return fire.
- Even those that fall rise again to join the silent march.
- Amidst the phalanxes drift giant mechanoid arachnids and vehicles of strange, macabre design.
- **Canoptek Scarabs** – metal insects that phase in and out of reality – descend in great swarms.
- Talon-limbed horrors and spectral assassins emerge from the shadows.
- Looming over all are the **Monoliths**, **Obelisks**, and **Tesseract Vaults**, great floating engines of destruction.
- Even shards of old star gods, the **C’tan**, now serve the Necrons.

Beneath the direction of their Overlords, the Necrons remain single-mindedly focused on one purpose – to reclaim the stars.

---

## Sautekh Dynasty

There are many dynasties of Necrons, some of which have not yet reawoken. The greatest of the arisen Necron empires is that of the **Sautekh Dynasty**.

They are led by **Imotekh the Stormlord**, a peerless warrior and pitiless commander. Beneath his tactical mastery, the Sautekh legions have mercilessly carved themselves a new empire.

Under Imotekh’s aggressive strategies, his dynasty has reclaimed dozens of systems and united many disparate Necron worlds under its glorious banner. The crownworld – the **Phaeron’s** seat of power – is **Mandragora**, on the Eastern Fringe.

It has always been Imotekh’s wish to reunite all tomb worlds beneath his rule, and nothing can deter his plans, not even rampant Daemon incursions.

As the **Great Rift** opened, the Stormlord launched his **Absorption Wars**, a many-pronged campaign to seize dozens of tomb worlds awakened by the warp influx. Imotekh sought to conquer them before they could fully rise from their stasis slumber, ensuring the continued rise of the Sautekh.

---

## Necron Dynasties

For millennia, the **Necron dynasties** ruled the galaxy. Time and the **Great Sleep**, however, have taken an inevitable toll.

Those dynasties that have managed to wake seek a new age of Necron domination.

- **Mephrit**  
  The star-killers. Exotic energies are boldly displayed by the ranks of the soldiery of the Mephrit Dynasty. The captive light of suns burns within all of the weapons they unleash upon their foes.

- **Nihilakh**  
  In times of antiquity, this dynasty built treasure worlds filled with wealth plundered from a thousand civilisations. Regal in war, the warriors of Nihilakh wear turquoise and gold as their dynastic colours.

- **Novokh**  
  The crimson armour of Novokh is a legacy of many bloody victories. The dynasty’s symbol reflects the core system cluster of their territory and the six wars of conquest that spread out from its heart.

- **Charnovokh**  
  Ravaged by **Tyranid hive fleets** and with their tomb worlds defiled by the **Imperium**, the legions of Charnovokh cling defiantly to the edges of the Eastern Fringe, their dynasty hanging in the balance.

---

## Necron Wargear

Necron technology is even less fathomable to **Imperial Tech-Priests** than the wonders wrought by the Aeldari.

- **Gauss weapons** are the most commonly carried weapon of the Necron soldiery. Unlike conventional Imperial energy weapons, a gauss projector does not deliver a laser burst or bolt of force, but instead emits a **molecular disassembling beam** capable of reducing flesh or armour to its constituent atoms.
- Other examples of Necron war-tech include **quantum shielding**, **tesla**, and **particle weaponry**—all equally inexplicable in their operation.

---

## Orks: The Enemy Beyond

Over the long millennia, the **Orks** have proven to be the most prolific and frequent threat to the Imperium.

They can be found in warbands, clans, and tribes spread across countless planets and space-borne fleets, sometimes even forming their own volatile empires.

Orks are a barbaric **xenos** race that infests the galaxy. No matter how far Mankind has travelled, they have found that Orks are either already there waiting for them or arrive soon after to launch their characteristically crude but devastating attacks.

Orks are brutal, **green-skinned** creatures that revel in violence. So great is their need for conflict that, without a more obvious opponent, they will gladly fight amongst themselves.

Their species is so numerous that, if the disparate groups were ever to cease hostilities with their own kind, the Orks would swiftly overrun the galaxy.

### Ork Society and Warfare

Size dominates Ork society, and the largest of their kind invariably lead them.

On occasion, an especially hulking **Ork Warboss** will conquer several rival groups, forming the survivors into a massive army. What follows is known as a **Waaagh!** – part invasion and part holy war.

During a Waaagh!, the greenskins will continue to flock to the leader’s banner so long as they have something to conquer. Each new victory calls yet more greenskins from the surrounding region to join.

A powerful Ork can lead a Waaagh! for a while, but to string together many victories and keep finding worthy targets takes an Ork with extreme cunning.

Luckily, the combination of **brawn and brains** is rare in Orks, although when such a leader rises, the whole galaxy trembles.

---

## Ork Clans

### Goffs

Orks of the **Goff Clan** are traditionalists in the greenskin fashion. They respect violence, especially at close quarters, and do not care for any frills or flash.

- Goff warbands are infantry-minded and view other clans as soft.
- They dress predominantly in black decorated with dags or checks.
- They think camouflage fit only for cowards. Why hide from a foe?

### Deathskulls

Plunderers without equal, the **Deathskulls** are noted for their ability to scrounge.

- They’ll fight whole wars just so they can strip the battlefield clean.
- The salvage is then beaten into (or out of) shape by **Meks**, who cobble it back together to create deadly new weaponry.
- A superstitious lot, Deathskulls believe **blue** is a lucky colour.

### Blood Axes

Because of their habits of trading for Imperial wargear, wearing camouflage, and using battle tactics, other Orks often distrust the **Blood Axes**.

- This clan favours the use of **Kommandos**, elite fighters that use dirty tricks like sneaking up on foes.
- Blood Axes ignore this derision, caring only for victory.

### Bad Moons

The richest of the Ork clans, the **Bad Moons** are known for having the best gear of war.

- Bad Moons Nobz tote gaudy back-banners and massive, kustomised weapons.
- They are followed by mobs of scurrying **grot servants**.
- If it is loud and flashy, the ostentatious Bad Moons want it—they bristle with gold-plated firepower and shiny flair.

### Evil Sunz

Orks belonging to the **Evil Sunz Clan** are irresistibly attracted to every conceivable kind of fast vehicle.

- Warbike mobs are especially popular.
- They include jetcraft pilots and super-charged **Trukk** crews.
- Evil Sunz wear **red armour** and often paint their machines red, firmly believing in the old Ork adage that “red ones go fasta.”

### Snakebites

Those Orks in the **Snakebites Clan** scorn technology, preferring ‘da old ways’.

- Other clans consider them backward, but despite their feral, warpaint-wearing ways, the ferocity of the Snakebites’ assaults is second to none.
- No clan breeds more dangerous **squigs** or **grots** than the Snakebites.
- Their camps teem with such creatures.

---

## Ork Specialists

### Mekboyz

**Ork Mekboyz** inherently know how to fix all things mechanical using only the crudest of tools, a few well-placed kicks, and occasionally some mad **gubbinz** of their own invention.

- They are tinkerers extraordinaire, using a method of jury-rigging impossible for non-Orks to decipher.
- Rarely are inventions, war machines, or ramshackle vehicles built the same way twice.
- They go to war clanking with contraptions thought up by the Mekboyz—extra-shooty weapons, kustom force fields, or even the bizarre teleportation weapon known as the **shokk attack gun**.

### Weirdboyz

The most deranged of all the greenskins are the **Weirdboyz**. These Orks are the most psychically attuned of their kind and can absorb the wild mental energies of nearby Orks.

- They must find ways (often quite quickly) to vent the build-up of these volatile forces, resulting in Weirdboyz vomiting dangerous blasts of warp energy.
- It is on the battlefield where Ork emotions run highest, meaning Weirdboyz dragged to battle become infused with power of titanic proportions.
- If they remain coherent (or are pointed in the right direction by their minders), this energy is unleashed upon the foe, bursting them apart.

### Painboyz

Part doctor, part dentist, and part butcher, **Painboyz** are driven to perform exploratory surgery on living creatures.

- Sometimes they even do such operations when it is required.
- It is the Painboyz that ‘fix’ injuries to fellow greenskins, who luckily are quite hardy.

## Ork Doks and Weapons of War

The **‘Doks’**, as they are also referred to, are often called upon to fuse the mechanical contraptions made by **Mekboyz** onto **Orks**. They work with a range of pincers, ‘stabby bits’, crude sawing instruments, and rusty syringes that work as well in close combat as they do in operations. Indeed, most often it is all one and the same.

**DEATH AND DUTY ARE ALL WE MUST GIVE.**

### Ork Weapons of War

- **Slugga**
- **Choppa**
- **Shoota**
- **Power klaw**
- **Rokkit launcha**
- **Big shoota**
- **Big choppa**
- **Bomb squig**
- **Shokk attack gun**
- **Boom bomb**

Orks are not subtle, and nowhere is this more apparent than upon the battlefield. **Ork weaponry** is loud, large-calibre, and prone to belching fire and smoke. If several barrels and a spare rokkit can be welded together, so much the better. Aiming is not a priority, but massive firepower and loud explosions most certainly are.

---

## 131: T’au Empire

**T’au** are an alien race that seeks to carve an empire into the havoc-filled **Eastern Fringe**. They mean to bring a new and enlightened way to a barbaric and unordered universe. Many races have already joined their cause and, in time, even those that resist are shown the benefits of **T’au’va – the Greater Good**.

On the Eastern Fringe of the galaxy, a new empire is growing. Ambitious and united in purpose, the xenos race known as the **T’au** has spread its ‘enlightenment’ across the stars. Although barely registering as a blip against the size of the sprawling **Imperium**, the rapid expansion of the T’au has drawn a predictably brutal response from the **High Lords of Terra**.

As the T’au encroached on Imperial territory, several vast crusades were sent to halt the aggressive xenos colonization. After purging the T’au colonies nearest their worlds, the Imperial forces crossed the **Damocles Gulf**, a space anomaly that had long formed a barrier to T’au expansion, to confront their foes. The relentless T’au, however, surprised the Imperial commanders with the strength of their defence, forcing a retreat.

The **T’au** are a practical people, devoid of religion or psychic ability. Instead, they adhere to a rigid **caste system**, with each of the five castes (**Fire, Earth, Air, Water**, and **Ethereal**) forming a subspecies within the race. Such segregation provides the clarity of purpose that allows each member to fulfil their role within society – be it warrior, worker, pilot, or bureaucrat.

The members of the ruling caste, the **Ethereals**, bind the other castes towards a common goal. It is they who steer the course of the T’au expansions, deciding which planets will be colonised, which aliens will be absorbed and which will be eliminated.

Unlike the Imperium, the T’au attempt to sway other cultures, using diplomatic ploys to show the plentiful benefits of the **Greater Good**. Those who refuse to join the growing T’au Empire are quickly shown the error of their ignorance.

---

## T’au Military and Expansion

The T’au military is fast, flexible, and well equipped with technologically advanced weaponry and agile **battlesuits**. With their organised methods of war and sophisticated weaponry, the T’au believe there is no foe they cannot defeat. Many aliens have already been conquered, and some, like the carnivorous **Kroot** and the insectoid **Vespid**, have been so enlightened they now send troops to assist further T’au expansions.

The T’au hope to bring a progressive new age of light to the dark and savage galaxy.

---

## 132: Quote from Aun’Va, Ethereal Supreme

> “Our conquest is inevitable, our ascension a matter of time. Let none who are wise deny our destiny.”  
> — **Aun’Va, Ethereal Supreme**

---

## Geography and Important Locations

- **MACRAGGE**
- **THE YMGA MONOLITH**
- **SCHINDELGHEIST**
- **VENGEANCE**
- **ICHAR IV**
- **HADEX ANOMALY**
- **THE SCOURGE STARS**
- **NECRON SAUTEKH DYNASTY**
- **BLACK REACH**

---

## Fifth Sphere Expansion

The T’au Empire launched a new venture – the **Fifth Sphere Expansion** – as soon as the warp storms dissipated along the Eastern Fringe enough to allow such a thing. This endeavour followed hard on the heels of the ill-fated **Fourth Sphere Expansion**, which was lost at the time of the **Great Rift**.

### Spheres of Expansion and Continuous Advancement

Unlike the Imperium of Mankind, the T’au Empire embraces new technology. Developed by the **Earth caste**, the **Fire caste** are supplied with advanced wargear, often further augmented with special-issue prototype weapons.

T’au **pulse**, **ion**, and **rail weapon technologies** give their warriors a firepower advantage, both in terms of range and hitting power. All who choose to oppose the **Greater Good** learn to fear the deadly efficiencies of such weapons.

The T’au are a dynamic race that have grown an empire in a relatively short time period. Their history – though merely a blink compared to that of the Imperium – has been marked by relentless colonisation efforts, known to them as **spheres of expansion**. Each of these great pushes ripples outwards from their core worlds, known as **sept worlds**, to colonise new systems.

They conquer through trade and coercion, their battle-honed military always ready to step in as the final negotiators. The **First Sphere Expansion** ended when the T’au reached the limits of their ability to traverse space. Being a non-psychic race, the T’au have no understanding of the **warp**, so their star fleets travel at **sub-light speeds**.

New technological innovations have steadily increased their range, allowing them to press ever further into the galaxy. Their **Second** and **Third Spheres of Expansion** were halted only due to the barrier of the **Damocles Gulf** and increased resistance from the Imperium of Mankind.

---

## 134: Map and Sectors

- **CHARADON SECTOR**
- **ULTRAMAR SUB-SECTOR**
- **T’AU EMPIRE**
- **TEMPORARY RIFT CORRIDOR**

---

## 135: T’au Battlesuits

At the apex of the advanced weaponry designed by the T’au are their **battlesuits**. Equipped with a wide variety of deadly weapon loadouts, the battlesuits combine offensive capability, armoured protection, and high manoeuvrability.

Some bear **repulsor jet engines** granting them the ability to strike anywhere on a battlefield. Piloting such a battlesuit is the greatest honour for a **Fire caste warrior**, and before they are allowed to do so they must pass many trials.

### Notable T’au Sept Worlds

- **Vior’la**: One of the major first-phase septs, best known for its aggressive **Fire Warriors**. This sept remains the capital and is the political centre of the T’au Empire.
- **Sa’cea**: The most densely populated sept world. Its warriors are experts in **urban warfare**.

---

## 137: Tyranid Hive Fleets – A New Menace

As the years pass, more **Tyranid** threats continue to enter the war-torn galaxy. Hive Fleets **Hydra, Scylla, Charybdis**, and **Kronus** have thrust tendrils out of the intergalactic void.

Strangely, the initial invasions of **Hydra** seem to have bypassed other, more likely targets, instead seeking out splinters of previous Tyranid invasions in order to cannibalise them. Why the hive fleet would be adding to its growing biomass in this way remains a mystery.

Beyond the edges of the Imperium lies the unspeakable cold of the intergalactic void. It is the great barrier that divides galaxy from galaxy, where grand vistas of space conspire to hold their secrets with inconceivable distances.

Yet the void is not empty. An immeasurably ancient and exceedingly alien intelligence has emerged from that darkness, its many eyes drawn towards the bountiful lifeforms of the galaxy. From the void come the **hive fleets**, stretching out like impossibly vast tendrils, drifting in brooding silence.

Once the remorseless shoals of the bio-ships detect a prey world, they close upon their target. There is no escape.

When the Tyranids depart, they leave behind a barren rock scoured of anything that lives.

---

### Tyranid Hive Mind and Battlefield Behavior

The Tyranid race comprises many different creatures all functioning as one, coordinated by the gestalt consciousness that is the **Hive Mind**. Each creature is linked by that monolithic sentience.

On the battlefield, leader creatures serve as hubs to channel connections to the lesser swarms, synchronising their movements. It is this central intelligence that guides the Tyranid fleets towards prey planets.

So powerful are the emanations from the Hive Mind that they are accompanied by a smothering psychic phenomenon known to the Imperium’s Astropaths as the **Shadow in the warp**. It is as if the darkness of the void is actively isolating worlds about to be consumed.

---

### Tyranid Invasion Description

The sight of an oncoming Tyranid invasion is one that few have witnessed and survived. 

- **Gigantic spores** plummet down, splitting open to reveal broods of ferocious beasts.  
- Swarms of **scythe-limbed aliens** move across the ground as one.  
- Some carry grotesque living weapons capable of firing **parasitic projectiles** that chew into their targets’ flesh.  
- **Stalker organisms** use perfect camouflage to ambush prey.  
- **Winged monstrosities** rain death from above.  
- The ground quakes as **burrowing beasts** tunnel up from below.  
- Towering **behemoths** stride upon multiple sets of legs unleashing **bio-cannon blasts**.

Every Tyranid creature is a perfectly evolved killing machine, adapted for its role.

Thus far, only their vanguard has reached the galaxy – the greater mass is still on its way.

Driven by an insatiable hunger, they come from beyond. They are drawn to galaxies teeming with life like predators on a blood scent. In their wake, they leave nothing behind. They are the **Great Devourer**, the **Tyranids** – a xenos race that seeks to strip down and absorb all living matter they come into contact with.

### Regions Affected

- **REDUCTUS SECTOR**
- **NEPHILIM SECTOR**

---

## Genestealer Cults

Sent out on seeding imperatives, **Genestealers** haunt space hulks, clamber aboard shuttles, and secrete themselves beneath the shadowy bulkheads of enormous starships.

Many a crammed transport has unknowingly carried such lethal cargo, and in their hibernatory state, a Genestealer can even survive the cold vacuum of outer space.

When a Genestealer reaches a world ripe for infection, it unfolds and begins its deadly work.

Genestealers prefer heavily populated planets, especially **hive worlds**, where they can go into hiding, emerging from dark sewers to attack one human at a time.

They do not kill but implant a portion of their own biomass into their chosen host like a virus, turning them into xenos-worshipping followers. Soon, hybrids follow, monstrous crosses between Genestealers and humankind. So the cult grows.

In the final stages, some hybrids – known as **Neophytes** – are merely pallid and bald, passing easily through the unhealthily overcrowded confines of their hive like wolves in sheep’s clothing.

Only when the brotherhood is strong enough do they strike. On the day of the great insurrection, secrecy is cast aside and the cult banners are lifted high.

Surging from ambush, the Genestealer Cult attacks – inhumanly strong **Aberrants**, swarms of weapon-bearing **Acolytes**, and scuttling **Purestrain Genestealers**.

Genestealer Cultists also usurp tanks and armoured vehicles to use against the foe.

They are all led by the **Genestealer Patriarch** – the creature who started it all, since grown to gargantuan size and power. The slaughter that ensues is dreadful to behold.

---

## Cult Uprisings and Symbols

Insidious. Infectious. Hidden from sight, and walking openly, the Genestealer Cults have grown. They have spread their xenos corruption throughout the underbelly of the Imperium.

They are patient, they bide their time – but when the moment is right, the uprising is as swift as it is merciless.

Although only a handful of cults have been codified by the **Ordo Xenos**, data-harvests taken from **Ghosar Quintus** imply the presence of hundreds, perhaps thousands, in **Ultima Segmentum** alone.

Each cult identifies its members by secret colours and hidden tattoos. By the time the cult banners are revealed, it is already too late.

---

## Quote

**“BE STRONG IN YOUR IGNORANCE.”**

**“REASON IS THE CLOAK OF TRAITORS.”**

**“FORGIVENESS IS A SIGN OF WEAKNESS.”**

## Alien Menace  

From the **lithe and deadly Aeldari** to the **ancient terror of the Necrons**, from the **technological supremacy of the T’au** to the **blade-limbed swarms of the Tyranids** and the **ramshackle savagery of the Orks**, the **xenos races** of the **Warhammer 40,000 galaxy** are diverse and spectacular.  

### The Ynnari  
Combining the unparalleled discipline of the **craftworld Aeldari** with the depthless cruelty of the **Drukhari**, **Ynnari warhosts** bring the full fury of their ancient race to bear against their foes.  

> "Trust not in their appearance, for the Eldar are as alien to good, honest men as the vile Tyranids and savage Orks. There is no understanding them because there is nothing to understand – they are a random force in the universe."  
> – Imperial Commander, **Abriel Hume**  

### Key Aeldari Factions  

- **Eldrad Ulthran** is among the greatest of his race’s ancient **Farseers**. Leading the warhosts of **Ulthwé**, this prescient arch-manipulator seeks to turn back the looming darkness and save his people from their final end.  
- Though their **craftworld was fractured** during the birth of **Ynnead**, the **Swordwind of Biel-Tan** still fight to eradicate the taint of the lesser races from a galaxy they believe to be theirs alone.  
- **Alaitoc** is famed for its **Rangers**, courageous Aeldari warriors who have strayed from the well-trodden paths of their people and journeyed far and wide across the stars.  
- The **Wild Rider clans of Saim-Hann** swoop into battle on skimming jetbikes, supported by squadrons of swift grav-tanks and agile combat aircraft. Speed and ferocity are their primary weapons, wielded with expert skill.  
- Breathtakingly swift and surpassingly deadly, the **Harlequins of the Laughing God** follow veiled agendas as they perform deadly dances of war across the far-flung stars.  

### Aeldari Divisions  
Though they share common origins, the **Aeldari of the craftworlds** and those of **Commorragh** remain splintered parts of a once-great whole. Their irreconcilable differences often bring them into conflict.  

- The **Archons** rule over the **Drukhari Kabals**, basking in the fear and pain of their unfortunate victims.  
- Monstrous and deformed warriors of the **Haemonculus Covens** are stitch-fleshed horrors from a madman’s nightmare.  

### T’au Empire  

- **Commander Farsight** is one of the greatest **T’au war heroes** ever, though he is hunted as a rebel by his own people.  
- The **Fire caste** are the warriors of the **T’au Empire**, fighting in close-knit infantry teams or piloting armoured battlesuits with immense firepower.  
- The white-armoured warriors of **Vior’la Sept** are known for being especially hot-blooded examples of their already warlike caste.  

### Necrons  

- The soulless legions of the **Nihilakh Dynasty** advance towards the beleaguered Imperial lines, unleashing ancient weapons of incredible power designed to scour lesser races from existence.  
- **Trazyn the Infinite** is both a powerful war leader and an obsessive collector of esoteric weaponry and living curios.  

### Tyranids  

- Attacking in overwhelming waves of chitinous war-beasts, **Hive Fleet Kraken** seeks to bury the courageous T’au Fire Warriors in seething masses of slashing, biting monstrosities.  
- All-consuming tides of bio-engineered killing machines, the **Tyranid hive fleets** devour everything in their path and leave only death in their wake.  
- **Hive Fleet Leviathan** is one of the most recent apocalyptically destructive swarms.  

### Orks  

- Upon the war-ravaged world of **Armageddon**, endless hordes of Orks followed **Ghazghkull Thraka** into battle.  
- Though the **Imperial defenders** fought bravely, the ramshackle war engines and bellowing hordes of the **greenskins** won victory after victory.  

---

## Eternity of War  

In the **grim darkness of the far future**, there is only war. The **Dark Gods** look out from the **Realm of Chaos** and move their pieces. Giants once more walk the stars, as the greatest of **Daemons** and **Fallen Primarchs** stride forth to do their masters’ bidding. The very gates of hell have been opened, and the galaxy burns.  

### The State of the Imperium  

- Everywhere, the foes of **Humanity** gathered, steeping themselves in the growing apocalypse. The **Emperor’s Realm** was surrounded and besieged. No sub-sector, system, or planet was immune from conflict.  
- As darkness spread, rebellions rose. Some were led by those corrupted by **Chaos**, insidious traitors awaiting a sign from the **Dark Gods** to betray their own species for power or material gain.  
- Not all uprisings were due to Chaos; some Imperial worlds became so repressive that civil strife was inevitable.  
- When the flickering beam of the **Astronomican** returned to parts of the galaxy, it brought new threats. Alien forces—barbaric plunderers, ancient powers, upstart usurpers, voracious monsters—came forwards to claim their piece of the Realm of Mankind.  

### Daemonic Threats  

- The most powerful **Greater Daemons** require vast energies from the **Warp** to remain manifest in reality, resulting in relatively brief appearances.  
- The eruption of the **Great Rift** sent tidal waves of unnatural energy across the galaxy, empowering even the greatest **Daemons** for longer periods.  

### New Age of War  

- A new age of war and darkness plunged the **Imperium** and the galaxy into conflicts never seen since the zenith of the **Horus Heresy**.  
- Battles erupted unpredictably from the roiling warp storms, wreaking havoc before disappearing and reappearing elsewhere across the galaxy.  
- Chaos factions sought to divide and conquer, isolating swathes of the Imperium.  
- The **Red Tide**, a carnage-filled crusade of wanton slaughter, launched bloody campaigns across the galaxy.  

### Dark Mechanicum and Chaos Raids  

- Fallen **Tech-Priests of the Dark Mechanicum** stole from hell-forge planets, seeking ancient archeotech and pieces to complete a terrifying weapon of war not seen since the **Age of Technology**.  
- **Ahriman**, Arch-Sorcerer of the **Thousand Sons**, launched terror raids on over three dozen planets.  
- The Dark Gods established strongholds out of the Great Rift, each coveting the galaxy for their own.  

### Resilience of the Imperium  

- Despite the seemingly hopeless situation, the **Imperium** was not yet defeated.  
- Infighting among the minions of the Dark Gods weakened their efforts as battles spilled from the Realm of Chaos into realspace.  
- The **Emperor’s Light** regained visibility, offering a sliver of hope.  
- Rumors of **Primarchs** returning to the galaxy gave many hope—they might bring victory as in days of legend.  

> "Some may question your right to destroy ten billion people. Those who understand realise that you have no right to let them live."  
> – **Exterminatus Extremis**  

> *"Ruthlessness is the kindness of the wise."*  

> *"Look to your labours and trust to your faith. All else is beyond you."*  

> *"Hope is the first step on the road to disappointment."*  

---

## War Zone: Ultramar  

Greedy eyes lingered on the southern reaches of **Ultima Segmentum**. **Nurgle** desired these prosperous, well-governed, and beautiful worlds for his own. He wished to lavish his gifts upon them, causing citizens to sprout **new growths** while other parts rotted and sloughed off.  

- The worlds of **Ultramar** attracted Nurgle, who aimed to annex them directly into his Garden in the **Realm of Chaos**.  
- After the **Great Rift** tore reality and flooded warp energies into the galaxy, Nurgle declared the time ripe to strike.  

### Plague Wars  

- Where prior poisons like **the Plague That Walks**, **the Oozing Pox**, and **Eyerot** had devastated overcrowded hive worlds, Nurgle intensified his efforts.  
- New virulent strains started the cycle of death anew, but this time, from the corpses of the fallen burst countless **Nurglings**.  
- **Cults of Corruption** summoned further aid. The following battles, known to the Imperium as the **Plague Wars**, ended with three systems north of Ultramar corrupted and renamed the **Scourge Stars**.  

### Nurgle’s Commanders and the Death Guard  

- Nurgle tasked three of his greatest commanders with conquering Ultramar.  
- The first invaders were the **Death Guard**, led by their grim Primarch, **Mortarion**.  
- Mortarion’s meticulously planned seven-part campaign brought untold ruination to all Ultramar.  

### The War of Flies  

- The first phase, known as the **War of Flies**, included:  
  - The assault of the **Three Planets**  
  - The besieging of the hive world of **Ardium**  
  - The **Creeping Doom offensive** against **Espandor** and **Drohl**  
- Virus bombardments preceded the Death Guard’s attacks. Once-glorious hive cities became pits, and agri-worlds became flyblown wastes.  
- The attacks were slow but relentless, slowly wearing down the Ultramarines and their auxilia.  

### Ultramar’s Defense and Guilliman’s Return  

- Communications were severed and relief forces cut off by fresh warp storms, leaving defenders hard-pressed across Ultramar.  
- Then, **Roboute Guilliman** returned from his galaxy-spanning crusade.  
- Tactically, Mortarion and his fellow commanders found themselves evenly matched by Guilliman’s precise counter-attacks, marking a new stage in the war.  

### Attacks on Macragge  

- Early in the invasion, many strikes were levelled at **Macragge**, the capital world.  
- Whether Mortarion aimed to probe the defenses or tie down Imperial forces is unknown.  
- The battles were short, sharp affairs, including rapid strikes from **Plague Drone** forces and cultist attacks attempting to deliver pox bombs into defense networks.  
- The attacks steadily drained morale and resources until Guilliman returned and seized the initiative with counter-strikes into Chaos-held territories.

## The Plague Wars in Ultramar

### Mortarion’s Creeping Doom Offensive

- The offensive began on the cardinal world of **Espandor** and initially made great advances.  
- Upon the return of **Roboute Guilliman**, a new defensive plan was ordered to slow the attacks.  
- The battle became a stalemate as **Guilliman** launched system-wide counter-attacks.

### Iax Befouled

- The final battle of the **Plague War** was fought at **First Landing** on **Iax**.  
- The **Death Guard** held the upper hand with relentless assaults.  
- **Mortarion** was summoned back to defend the **Scourge Stars** at the war’s onset.

### The March of Plagues Deadlocked

- Across **Ultramar**, the Plague Wars escalated with **Guilliman’s** counter-attacks stabilizing fronts.  
- The largest battles occurred at **Parmenio** and **Iax**.  
- At Parmenio, the war featured the largest armour and Titan clash over the **Plains of Hecatone**.  
- **Guilliman** struck Ku’gath’s vanguard, slaying his lieutenant **Septicus** and shattering the Plague Guard.  
- In space, **Galatan**, Ultramar's largest star fortress, was boarded by the Plague Fleet causing massive casualties.

### The Battle for Iax

- Once a verdant garden world, **Iax** was in ruins when **Guilliman** met **Mortarion**.  
- The confrontation ended in a deadlock before the Death Guard withdrew using a virus bomb.

---

## Forces & Commanders Involved in Ultramar Conflict

### Chaos Commanders

- **Mortarion**, Daemon Primarch  
- **Ku’gath Plaguefather**, Greater Daemon leading the Bubonicus legions  
- **Typhus**, First Captain of the Death Guard commanding a Plague Fleet  

### Death Guard and Allies

- Daemon legions ravaged **Tartella System** and **Iax**.  
- The Plague Fleet destroyed three of Ultramar's six star fortresses.  

### Ultramarine Defence Forces

- **Ultramarines** led by **Roboute Guilliman** with reinforcements from successor Chapters and forge worlds.  
- Counter-attack named the **Spear of Espandor** was launched to buy time for Imperium forces.

---

## Defence of Ultramar: Three Key Phases

1. **Initial losses** with defenders giving ground before the Death Guard onslaught.  
2. **Stabilisation** with the Primarch Guilliman's return.  
3. **Seizing the initiative** through counter-attacks and the final battle.

### Cooperation and Rivalries

- **Mortarion** and **Ku’gath** formed an alliance.  
- **Typhus** did not cooperate with Mortarion.

## The Fall of Cadia

### Overview

- The **Thirteenth Black Crusade** culminated in the near destruction of **Cadia** by the **Cicatrix Maledictum**.  
- Great pylons that held back the **warp storm of the Eye of Terror** were toppled.  
- Chaos powers ravaged **Cadia** beyond recovery.

### Defiance of the Region

- Neighboring worlds and systems remained defiant despite the fall of Cadia.  
- Cadia's reputation for resilience inspired the defense of the **Cadian Gate** and surrounding systems.

### Chaos Faction Rivalries

- Chaos hordes turned on themselves due to internal rivalries among mortal and daemonic warlords.  
- The **Imperial defenders** capitalized on these divisions to reclaim territory.

### Continued Fighting

- As the war raged, the Astra Militarum and Space Marines pushed back chaos forces.  
- Survivors of the **Great Exodus** came through the empyrean tempests to reinforce the defenders.  
- Continuous battles spread across the **Cadian**, **Belis Corona**, and **Agripinaa Systems**.

## No Hope Rests for Us Beyond the Emperor  
**Armies of the Imperium Vs Forces of Chaos**

### The Last Defence of Cadia

- The **final battles of Cadia** prevented total disaster.  
- Though **Cadia itself was lost**, defence of **Kasr Kraf** held Abaddon's final assault.  
- This allowed many **troops and military assets** to reach the Imperial evacuation zone.  
- **Abaddon** led the final assault, bringing the legions of the **Eye of Terror** under the Dark Gods' banner.  
- Their cause: destruction of the **Imperium** and demise of the **material realm**.

## The Damned

- Thirteen massive transports of combat-drugged mutants, wretches, zombies, and **Chaos Spawn** crash-landed into **Kasr Kharkovan**.  
- Many final assaults were led by the least storied among Abaddon’s armies.  
- His command: "**Destroy it all. Do not stop until it is ruins. Let it become a monument to death.**"  

---

## War in the Stygius Sector: Under Tzeentch’s Power

- Temporal anomalies from the **Great Rift** hurled entire warfleets through time.  
- Worlds shifted, vanished, or appeared displaced.  
- The **44th Necromundan Spirehawks** were lost on Dakidda, which vanished into an empyric vortex.  
- On the ground, **day became night**, gravity and time behaved erratically, and the dead rose as ghosts tormenting the living.  

---

## War Zone: Stygius  

- After the **Great Rift**, **Tzeentch** sought to outmaneuver his brothers, **Khorne**, **Slaanesh**, and **Nurgle**.  
- Tzeentch aimed to **claim the Stygius Sector**—near the **Eye of Terror** in **Segmentum Obscurus** and cut off from the Emperor’s Light.  
- The sector contains a pattern of **nine-times-nine star systems**, attracting Tzeentch’s designs.  

### Opening Phases  

- Cult uprisings broke out across twenty planets.  
- Frequent warp storms isolated each planet, perfect for Tzeentch’s manipulations.  
- The invasions came with **Magnus the Red**, his **Thousand Sons**, **Greater Daemon M’Katchnar**, and their allies.  
- Three star systems fell quickly; only the hive world **Mordian** resisted.  

### Counter-Attack  

- Distress signals reached several **Adeptus Astartes Chapters** and **Skitarii Legions**.  
- Despite late arrival, immense battles ensued to retake planets.  
- Siege of Mordian was relieved after a long campaign.  
- Six major clashes in the **Dhobash System** featured fighting between Thousand Sons and Space Wolves on **Tarkan**.  
- The arrival of an **Aeldari warhost** on **Rimenok** prevented further defeat.  

---

## Armies of the Imperium Vs Forces of Chaos  

### Stygius Crusade

- Hastily prepared relief effort with insufficient supplies and numbers.  
- Early gains by Adeptus Astartes were unsustainable.  
- Eleven army groups coordinated precise attacks guided by Sorcerers and oracles.  
- A new realm in realspace was carved out for Tzeentch.

## Allies from Ulthwé

- **Seer Council Coven Black Storm:** 4 Warhosts  
- **Lileath’s Blade:** 1 Skyhost  
- **Serpent Striking:** 1 Aspect Warhost  
- **Duality of Purpose:** 2 Revenant Titans

## THE BLOOD CRUSADE  
In celebration of the great conquests that were sure to come, **Khorne** bellowed. His roar shook the galaxy, sending further cracks in reality’s riven middle. His followers - from Daemon legions to brutish beasts to violent-minded hive cultists - all took up that call to arms.

Riding new crests of the warp storms known as the **Blood Waves**, the Daemon legions erupted from the **Cicatrix Maledictum**, unleashing new orgies of slaughter across the galaxy. This marked the beginning of the **Blood Crusade**.

The red-raged armies did not seek out destinations but rode where the storms took them, materializing upon planets to unleash carnage before leaving as the tempests moved on.

---

Multiple spearheads drove into the galaxy, drawing renegades, cultists, and criminally violent forces toward the unbound rage. 

- Tomb worlds fell.  
- Imperial forge worlds became abattoirs.  
- Tyranid hive fleets were eradicated.  

Entire populations were often sacrificed to the **Blood God**, but usually, attacks lasted only a few hours before the **Slaughterhost** moved on.

New forces joined while others dropped off. In thousands of battles, only twice did the Blood Crusade meet its match.

Only upon hearing whispered words from his brother **Tzeentch** did **Khorne** call back his chief lieutenants, starting the **War in the Rift**.

---

## WAR IN THE RIFT  
In the starless gloom of the **Noctis Aeterna**, **Craftworld Iyanden** was assaulted by one of the greatest foes of the **Aeldari**.

- A **Slaaneshi Daemon host**, led by the **Keeper of Secrets N’Kisha**, channeled a warp storm to break through the craftworld’s formidable protections.  
- Fighting raged beneath the domes of Iyanden.  
- Warhosts from all Aeldari factions intervened: **craftworlds**, **Drukhari**, **Corsairs**, **Harlequins**, **Exodites**, and **Ynnari**.  
- Without their aid, all would have been lost.  

Despite this **common-cause victory**, the Aeldari remained fractured.

---

Meanwhile, **Armageddon** was transformed into a hellscape by an influx of warp energies. Daemon armies swept across battlefields, no longer chained to the laws of reality.

- Remaining Imperial armies included twenty-five regiments of **Imperial Guard** and elements of nine **Adeptus Astartes Chapters**.  
- Orks from unknown clans fought as well.  
- The Daemon legions were as content fighting amongst themselves as exterminating survivors.  
- Communication difficulties mean exact Imperial defender numbers are unknown.

---

The **Dark Gods** warred among themselves in realspace.

- The opening campaign saw **Tzeentch** and **Khorne** attacking **Nurgle’s** growing foothold in the **Scourge Stars**.  
- **Nurgle** recalled lieutenants from Ultramar to counter-attack realspace strongholds.  
- **Slaanesh** allied variably to all sides, advancing his own goals.  
- The greatest Daemons clashed in grinding attrition at the **Battle of Vigrid**.  
- Fighting ended only when all agreed to settle via Tzeentch’s proposal: a contest of champions.

---

## PLAYING THE GAME  
Welcome to the rules section of **Warhammer 40,000** – a guide to playing games in the war-torn galaxy of the **Dark Millennium**.

This section includes:

- **Core rules** for tabletop warfare with your miniatures  
- Various ways to enjoy games of Warhammer 40,000  
- Inspiration and battles for all skill levels  

The following pages provide rules and guidelines suited for different hobbyists:

- Casual collectors playing occasionally with friends  
- Veteran warriors competing in tournaments  

---

The **core rules** are the starting point for everyone. Several ways to approach your games are introduced:

- **Open Play**  
- **Narrative Play**  
- **Matched Play**

Each offers a distinct experience but can be mixed to create your desired gaming style.

This section also contains:

- A guide to building battlefields  
- Rules for forming a **Battle-forged army**  
- Introduction to **advanced rules** for additional combat options  

Whether you seek war in deadly galactic environments, team games, or escalating narrative campaigns, options are available.

---

## CORE RULES (PG 176)  
Start here! Whatever game you want to play, the **core rules** are the essential foundation.

- Learn to move, use psychic powers, shoot, charge, and fight with your models.  
- Rules cover everything from infantry to gigantic monsters and armored war machines.  
- Build from simple games to all-out galactic wars.  
- Provides clarifications, hints, tips, and an introductory mission called **Only War**.  

The core rules are essential for getting started and will be your constant companion.

It is recommended to play a few games using only these rules before exploring further options.

---

## ADVANCED RULES (PG 238)  
At its heart, **Warhammer 40,000** is a game that pits armies of warriors against one another in tabletop conflict to the death.

## Advanced Rules and Game Variations

Beyond the **core premise**, Warhammer 40,000 is a hobby of vast and thrilling variation. It allows you to depict everything from **breakneck aerial dogfights** and **orbital drop-assaults** to war across hostile alien environments between multiple different armies and close-run battles through the war-torn streets of an **Imperial hive** — all encompassed by the **advanced rules**.

Whether you choose to introduce any advanced rules to your games or combine several different aspects in a single game, all of these optional mechanics build upon the **core rules**. They add to or provide variation on the core rules rather than requiring you to learn a whole new game system!

From huge multiplayer battles and sprawling sieges to campaigns fought over strange alien worlds, the advanced rules will provide you with exciting new gaming experiences to suit whatever type of game you want to play for years to come.

---

## 1. Open Play (pg 188)

The first of the three distinct ways to play **Warhammer 40,000**, **open play** is the most free-form and adaptable. It can be as simple or as complex as you like — you can literally just pick any **Citadel Miniatures** you have and start playing.

It’s as easy as that, and playing games this way can lead to extraordinary battles as players are free to put their entire collections on the battlefield to get the dice rolling started! Whether this leads to titanic clashes between huge armies that last entire weekends, or desperate and dramatic battles against the odds, the emphasis in open play is firmly on playing a **fun wargame** with whatever parts of your collections you wish, in whatever fashion you choose.

This section also contains a selection of **story hooks** to use as inspiration for your games. With a little prior thought and discussion, your Warhammer 40,000 battles can take on a thrilling, **story-driven aspect**, transcending the simple rules of the game and becoming something altogether more dramatic and involving.

- Desperate last stands  
- Vendettas between mighty heroes  
- Courageous rescue missions  
- Other characterful conflicts  

Open play is ideal when you have multiple players who want to get involved all at once. It allows for all kinds of variation in terms of:

- Team gaming  
- Outnumbered players fighting against the odds  
- Other imaginative scenarios  

This section provides the help needed to get the most out of your multiplayer games.

---

## 2. Narrative Play (pg 192)

**Narrative play** is based around the stories embedded in the background of Warhammer 40,000, either those in official books or those you write yourself. Often, reading up on the history of a particular **Faction**, hero, or battle is all the inspiration needed to set up a game.

Examples of inspiring stories include:

- The bitter rivalry between **Commissar Yarrick** and **Ghazghkull Thraka**  
- **Wolf Lord Logan Grimnar’s** quest for revenge upon **Daemon Primarch Magnus the Red**  

Tales of strategy and massed battle may also inspire you, such as:

- Sudden ambushes  
- Sweeping flank attacks  
- Meat-grinder offensives through the smoke and fire of no man’s land  

Narrative play provides **guidelines** and structured scenarios to recreate your favourite war stories on the tabletop. Sources for these tales include:

- Histories and backgrounds in the rulebook and **codexes**  
- Dramatic stories in **Black Library’s Warhammer 40,000 novels**

Unlike open play, where players determine their own story and victory conditions, narrative play offers a tighter framework. Examples include seven new missions such as:

- **Patrol**  
- **Ambush**

These missions alter game parameters and give players differing roles and objectives, where one plays as the attacker and the other as the defender.

Additional rules help with battlefield storytelling, and with imagination and experience, you and your opponents can create your own exciting narrative missions depicting any deadly scenario you wish.

---

## An Evolving Experience

With **three different styles of play**, dozens of missions, and an ever-expanding array of armies and **Detachments** to collect, Warhammer 40,000 can seem intimidating to new players.

Fortunately, by starting with the core rules and building up at an appropriate pace, you can enjoy your hobby in whatever way suits you. By taking your time and trying things out, you will soon find the combination that best fits your play style. If things start to feel routine, just try out some new rules!

---

## 3. Battle-Forged Armies (pg 240)

While open play encourages gamers to place whatever models they want on the tabletop, in whatever quantities, both **narrative** and **matched play** tend to use **Battle-forged armies**. These forces bring additional **structure** and **balance** to the gaming experience.

When selecting a Battle-forged army, greater restrictions and considerations of **structure** are placed on you. Some players build collections using the Battle-forged template to ensure they can easily assemble a Battle-forged force for any game. Others collect as they please and simply form a Battle-forged army when needed.

Battle-forged armies must be organized into **Detachments** — groupings of units with specific strategic roles. Twelve Detachments are presented in the book.

With your army made up of Detachments, you gain access to **Command Points** (pg 242), which unlock **Stratagems** usable in all Warhammer 40,000 missions.

---

## 4. Matched Play (pg 212)

As the name suggests, tabletop wargames are games to be enjoyed by all players. For some, enjoyment comes from assembling **Battle-forged armies** that provide the optimal combination of units to pit against one another in balanced contests of **strategy** and **skill**.

Matched play allows these armies to be tested under conditions giving no particular advantage to either side, determining which army is strongest and which general is canniest. It is a more **balanced** and controlled way of playing, favored by collectors who compete in tournaments and similar events.

Matched play is also ideal for balanced gaming experiences at local gaming clubs or stores when players face unknown opponents.

This section includes twelve missions designed to complement Battle-forged rules, creating as equal chances of victory as possible.

- The six **Eternal War** missions focus on breaking into enemy territory, securing objectives, or eliminating enemy targets — providing exciting tactical challenges.  
- The six **Maelstrom of War** missions use **dynamic Tactical Objectives** to randomize victory conditions and keep games balanced and unpredictable.

---

## Where to Play

There are many places to play Warhammer 40,000, and opponents are normally easy to find. Options include:

- Local gaming clubs or stores — great places to meet opponents and rivals  
- Playing games with friends, often on home-built gaming tables  
- Campaign events and tournaments — whole weekends playing many games against various opponents  

---

## Datasheets

The warriors, monsters, and war machines fighting for control of the galaxy are incredibly diverse, each with their own style of waging war. Each unit has a **datasheet** listing the **characteristics**, **wargear**, and **abilities** of the models in that unit.

### Datasheet Components

1. **Unit Name**  
   Models move and fight in units, which can have one or more models. This lists the name of the unit.

2. **Battlefield Role**  
   Typically used when making a **Battle-forged army** (pg 240).

3. **Power Rating**  
   The higher the rating, the more powerful the unit. You determine your army’s **Power Level** by adding the Power Ratings of all units.

4. **Profiles**  
   Contain characteristics that describe model capabilities:  
   - **Move (M):** Speed at which a model moves across the battlefield  
   - **Weapon Skill (WS):** Skill in hand-to-hand fighting. A WS of ‘-’ means the model cannot fight in melee  
   - **Ballistic Skill (BS):** Accuracy with ranged weapons. A BS of ‘-’ means no proficiency with ranged weapons  
   - **Strength (S):** How strong a model is and how likely to inflict damage in melee  
   - **Toughness (T):** Model’s resilience against physical harm  
   - **Wounds (W):** How much damage a model can sustain before being defeated  

---

## Warhammer 40,000 Codexes

A **codex** is the ultimate resource for your chosen army or armies! It contains:

- Datasheets for all miniatures of a particular **Faction**  
- Army-specific **special rules** reflecting army character  
- Exciting **Warlord Traits**, **Stratagems**, wargear, and unique relics  
- Inspirational background material and organizational info  
- Stunning artwork, miniatures photography, color guides, and heraldry  

Codexes provide rich context for how a Faction works in the Warhammer 40,000 universe.

To find out more, visit **games-workshop.com**.

---

## Modifying Characteristics

Some large models’ characteristics can change as they suffer damage. By looking at a model’s remaining wounds, consult the appropriate row on its datasheet chart to determine its current characteristics.

You may also encounter abilities and rules that modify characteristics during play.

## Modifiers and Characteristics

- **All modifiers** are cumulative.
- Apply any **multiplication or division** to the characteristic (rounding fractions up) before applying any addition or subtraction.
- Some characteristics may be a **random value** instead of a number, e.g., Move characteristic might be **2D6**, or Attacks might be **D6**.
- When a unit with a random Move characteristic moves, roll the indicated number of dice to determine the entire unit’s move distance (pg 176).
- For other characteristics, roll each time the unit attacks, inflicts damage, etc., on an individual, per-model basis.
- Characteristics of ‘-’ **can never be modified**.
- **Strength**, **Toughness**, and **Leadership** of a model can never be modified below 1.

### Key Characteristics

- **Attacks (A):** Number of times a model can strike in hand-to-hand combat.
- **Leadership (Ld):** How courageous, determined, or self-controlled a model is.
- **Save (Sv):** Protection provided by a model’s armour.

## 5. Unit Composition

- Describes what models are in the unit.

## 6. Wargear

- Details the basic weapons and equipment the models are armed with.

## 7. Abilities

- Many units have special abilities not covered by the core rules, described here.

## 8. Weapons

Weapons are described using the following characteristics:

- **Range:** How far the weapon can shoot. 'Melee' indicates the weapon is only for hand-to-hand combat. All others are ranged weapons.
- **Type:** Explained under Shooting and Fight phases of the core rules.
- **Strength (S):** Likelihood to inflict damage. If listed as **User**, it equals the wielder’s current Strength.
  - Modifiers like **+1** or **x2** modify the wielder’s Strength. Example: a weapon with Strength **x2** and wielder Strength **6** has Strength **12**.
- **Armour Penetration (AP):** Effectiveness against armour.
- **Damage (D):** Amount of damage inflicted by a successful hit.

Other optional weapons are described elsewhere, such as in a codex.

## 9. Keywords

- All datasheets list **keywords**, sometimes separated into **Faction keywords** and others.
- Keywords guide army composition and apply when rules specify models with certain keywords.
- Example: A rule applying to “all ADEPTUS ASTARTES models” means it applies only to models with the Adeptus Astartes keyword on their datasheet.

---

# Core Rules

## Models & Datasheets

- Rules and characteristics for all models and some terrain features are presented on **datasheets**.
- Datasheets are necessary to use models in battle.

## Units

- Models move and fight in **units**, each consisting of one or more models.
- Units must maintain **unit coherency**: every model in the unit must be within **2" horizontally** and **6" vertically** of at least one other model.
- If a unit becomes split, it must re-establish coherency at its next move.

## Tools of War

- Required: tape measure and dice.
- Distances measured in **inches (")** between the closest points of model bases or hulls.
- Uses **six-sided dice (D6)**.
- Rolls like **2D6**, **3D6** mean roll that many dice and add.
- **D3** rolled by halving a dice roll and rounding fractions up before modifiers.
- Modifiers are cumulative.
- Dice roll requirements like “3 or more” are shown as **3+**.

---

# The Battle Round

- Played in a series of **battle rounds**.
- Each round, both players take a turn.
- The same player takes the first turn each round; mission defines which player.
- Each turn has phases resolved in order:

### Battle Round Phases

1. **Movement Phase:** Move units that can do so.
2. **Psychic Phase:** Psykers use mental powers.
3. **Shooting Phase:** Units may shoot enemy units.
4. **Charge Phase:** Units move to close combat.
5. **Fight Phase:** Both players’ units attack with melee.
6. **Morale Phase:** Test courage of depleted units.

- After one player's turn, the opponent takes theirs.
- The battle round ends when both players complete turns.
- Repeat until battle conclusion.

---

## 1. Movement Phase

The ground shakes as armies advance for advantageous positions.

- Choose a unit and move each model in it as desired.
- Repeat for as many units as you wish.
- No model moves more than once in the phase.

### Moving Rules

- A model moves any direction up to its **Move characteristic** in inches.
- Cannot move through other models or terrain (like walls).
- Can move vertically to climb or cross scenery.
- Models with **FLY** move across models and terrain as if not there.

### Minimum Move for FLY Models

- Some FLY models have two values: minimum speed and maximum speed.
- Must move at least minimum speed.
- Cannot exceed maximum speed.
- Failing minimum move or moving off battlefield destroys the model.

### Enemy Models

- Models in the same army are **friendly**.
- Opponent’s are **enemy models**.
- Models cannot be moved within **1"** of enemy models.

### Falling Back

- Units within 1" of an enemy at start of Movement can:
  - Remain stationary, or
  - **Fall Back**, moving more than 1" away from enemies.
- Falling Back prohibits further Advance, charge, or shooting unless the unit can FLY.

### Advancing

- When moving, declare that the unit will **Advance**.
- Roll a dice and add it to Move for all models this turn.
- Advancing units cannot shoot or charge later that turn.

### Reinforcements

- Units may arrive mid-turn via teleporters, grav chutes, etc.
- Usually deployed at end of Movement phase but can happen during others.
- These units cannot move or Advance further during the arrival turn but can shoot, charge, etc.
- Treated as having moved for rules purposes.
- Units not arrived by battle end are destroyed.

> **Quote:**  
> “Shall we lie down meekly as a lamb before the ravening wolf or shall we oppose such horrors as the galaxy will throw at us with proud contempt? Suffer not the beasts and abominations of other worlds to live in our Imperium!”  
> — **Orthas Gregoran**, Chief Demagogue of the Forlan Synod

### Wobbly Models Syndrome

- If terrain makes placing a model difficult, balance it safely with both players’ agreement.
- Hold the model correctly when checking visibility or shooting.

---

## Perils of the Warp and Psychic Powers

- Rolling **double 1** or **double 6** on a psychic test means the psyker suffers **Perils of the Warp**.
- Psyker suffers **D3 mortal wounds**.
- If psyker is slain, the targeted power fails and every unit within 6" suffers **D3 mortal wounds**.

### Smite Power

- Warp charge value: **5**.
- If manifested, the closest visible enemy within 18" suffers **D3 mortal wounds** (pg 181).
- If Psychic test result exceeds 10, the target suffers **D6 mortal wounds**.

---

## 2. Psychic Phase

- Psykers wield the warp’s powers to aid allies and harm foes.
- Risks are high, as mistakes cause dangerous effects.

### Steps in the Psychic Phase

1. **Choose Psyker and Power**  
   - Models noted as **PSYKERS** on datasheets.
   - Psykers know powers and how many per phase on their datasheet.
   - All psykers know **Smite** unless stated otherwise.
   - Psykers may know other powers in addition or instead.

2. **Make Psychic Test**  
   - Attempt to manifest a power by rolling **2D6**.
   - If total ≥ power’s warp charge value, power manifests.
   - Psykers cannot manifest the same power more than once per turn.

3. ...

## Deny the Witch Tests

A **psyker** can attempt to resist a **psychic power** manifested by an enemy model within **24"** by taking a **Deny the Witch test** – this takes place immediately, even if it is not your turn.

- Roll **2D6**.
- If the total is greater than the result of the **Psychic test** that manifested the power, the power is resisted and its effects are negated.
- Only one attempt to deny each successfully manifested psychic power can be made each turn, regardless of the number of psykers within 24" of the enemy model.

---

## 4. Resolve Psychic Power

If the **Psychic test** is successful, the psyker survives the **Perils of the Warp**, and the power was not denied by a **Deny the Witch test**, you may resolve the psychic power’s effect as described in the power.

---

## Psychic Sequence

1. Choose **psyker** and psychic power.
2. Make **Psychic test**.
3. Enemy takes **Deny the Witch test**.
4. Resolve psychic power.

---

## Sequencing

When two or more rules apply at the same time (e.g., at the start of the Movement phase or before the battle begins), the player whose turn it is chooses the order.

- If these things occur before or after the game, or at the start or end of a battle round, players roll off to decide who chooses the order.

---

## Re-rolls

- Some rules allow **re-rolls**, meaning you can roll some or all dice again.
- You can **never re-roll a dice more than once**.
- Re-rolls happen *before* modifiers are applied.

---

## Roll-offs

- Both players roll a **D6**; highest roll wins.
- If there is a tie, both players re-roll.
- This is the only time players can re-roll a re-roll.
- Keep rolling until a winner is decided.

---

## 3. Shooting Phase

Guns thunder and shrapnel fills the sky, with muzzle flashes illuminating the battlefield.

### 1. Choose Unit to Shoot With

- Select a unit with ranged weapons to shoot.
- You **may not** pick a unit that **Advanced** or **Fell Back** this turn.
- You **may not** pick a unit within **1"** of an enemy unit.
- Each model attacks with all the ranged weapons it has.
- After one unit has fired, choose another eligible unit to shoot if desired.

### 2. Choose Targets

- Pick enemy unit(s) within the **range** of the weapon being used.
- The model must have **line of sight** to the target.
- A model can see through other models in its own unit for visibility.
- Cannot target enemy units within **1"** of friendly units.

### 3. Choose Ranged Weapon

- Models can shoot all weapons at the same target or split firing between different targets.
- For multiple models in a unit, shots may be divided as desired.
- Declare how shots are split before rolling dice.
- Resolve all attacks against one target before moving to the next.

---

### Number of Attacks

- Each ranged weapon has a number of attacks listed on its profile.
- Roll one dice per attack.
- Weapon types can affect the number of attacks.

---

## Shooting Sequence

1. Choose unit to shoot with
2. Choose targets
3. Choose ranged weapon
4. Resolve attacks
5. Make hit roll
6. Make wound roll
7. Enemy allocates wound
8. Enemy makes saving throw
9. Inflict damage

---

## Characters

- Models marked as **CHARACTER** are heroes, officers, prophets, and warlords.
- A **CHARACTER** can only be chosen as a target if they are the closest visible enemy unit to the shooter.
- This does not apply to **CHARACTERS** with **10 or more Wounds** due to their size.

---

## Fast Dice Rolling

- You may roll multiple similar attacks together to speed up play.
- Attacks must share the same **Ballistic Skill** or **Weapon Skill**, **Strength**, **Armour Penetration**, **Damage**, and target the same unit.
- Roll all hit rolls together, then all wound rolls.
- Opponent allocates wounds and makes saving throws one at a time.
- Damage must be allocated to models already wounded first.

---

## Aura Abilities

- Some units, usually **CHARACTERS**, have abilities affecting models within a range.
- Unless otherwise stated, the unit with the ability is also affected.
- Example: A **Lord of Contagion’s Nurgle’s Gift** ability affects all **DEATHGUARD** models within 7".

---

## Weapon Types

There are **five types of ranged weapons**:

- **Assault**
- **Heavy**
- **Rapid Fire**
- **Grenade**
- **Pistol**

A model with a weapon type number (e.g., Assault 1) can make that many attacks.

---

### Assault

- Can fire even if the model **Advanced** this turn.
- Subtract **1** from hit rolls if fired after advancing.

### Heavy

- Big, powerful weapons that require setup.
- Subtract **1** from hit rolls if the model **moved** this turn.

### Rapid Fire

- Can make **double** attacks if target is within **half the maximum range**.

### Grenade

- One model per unit may throw a grenade instead of firing a weapon.

### Pistol

- Can be fired even if enemy units are within **1"**.
- Must target the closest enemy unit.
- Models with both Pistols and other weapons may choose to fire either Pistols only or non-Pistols only.
- Choice declared before hit rolls.

---

## The Most Important Rule

In unclear situations during play:

- Discuss with your opponent to find the most sensible or fun solution.
- If no agreement, roll off and winner chooses.

---

## 4. Resolve Attacks

Attacks can be resolved one at a time or in groups.

### 1. Hit Roll

- Roll a dice.
- If roll ≥ model’s **Ballistic Skill**, the attack hits.
- A roll of **1 always fails**.

### 2. Wound Roll

- Roll to wound after a hit.
- Required roll depends on comparing **weapon Strength** and target’s **Toughness**.

| Strength vs Toughness | Required Roll to Wound |
|----------------------|-----------------------|
| Strength ≥ 2× Toughness | 2+ |
| Strength > Toughness     | 3+ |
| Strength = Toughness     | 4+ |
| Strength < Toughness     | 5+ |
| Strength ≤ ½ Toughness   | 6+ |

- Roll of **1 always fails**.

### 3. Allocate Wound

- Target player allocates wound to any model in unit.
- Wounds must be assigned to models already wounded first.

### 4. Saving Throw

- Target player rolls dice to save.
- Modify roll by the **Armour Penetration** characteristic of the damaging weapon.
- If the result ≥ target model’s **Save**, damage is prevented.

---

*“A mind without purpose will wander in dark places.”*  
*“Analysis is the bane of conviction.”*  
*“Look upon the Emperor’s works and tremble!”*  
*“Knowledge is to be feared!”*

## Damage and Saving Throws

If the result is less than the model’s **Save characteristic**, the saving throw fails and the model suffers damage. A roll of **1 always fails**, irrespective of any modifiers.

### Inflict Damage

- The damage inflicted is equal to the **Damage characteristic** of the weapon used.
- A model loses one **wound** for each point of damage suffered.
- If a model’s wounds are reduced to **0**, it is slain or destroyed and removed from play.
- Excess damage from a single attack does not carry over to other models if the target is destroyed.

### Invulnerable Saves

- Some models have **supernatural reflexes** or **force fields** granting them an **invulnerable save**.
- When allocating wounds, you may choose to use either the normal save or the invulnerable save, **not both**.
- If a model has more than one invulnerable save, it can only use **one** for that wound.
- Invulnerable saves **ignore weapon Armour Penetration** values.

### Mortal Wounds

- Mortal wounds are powerful attacks that cannot be stopped by armour or force fields.
- Each mortal wound inflicts **one point of damage** without a wound roll or saving throw.
- Excess mortal wound damage can be allocated to other models until all damage is allocated or the unit is destroyed.

## Terrain and Cover

Battlefields contain terrain features like **ruins**, **craters**, and **twisted copses** that provide cover.

- Units completely on or within terrain gain **+1 to saving throws** against shooting attacks.
- Invulnerable saves are **not affected** by terrain cover.
- Units gain **no cover benefit in the Fight phase**.

## Wound Roll Table

| Attack’s Strength vs Target’s Toughness | D6 Roll Required |
|-----------------------------------------|------------------|
| Strength TWICE (or more) than Toughness | 2+               |
| Strength GREATER than Toughness          | 3+               |
| Strength EQUAL to Toughness               | 4+               |
| Strength LOWER than Toughness             | 5+               |
| Strength HALF (or less) than Toughness    | 6+               |

---

## 4. CHARGE PHASE

Warriors charge into battle with **blade, hammer, and claw**.

### 1. Choose Unit to Charge With

- Units within **12" of the enemy** can charge.
- Units that **advanced or fell back** this turn, or started within 1" of an enemy, **cannot charge**.

### 2. Choose Targets

- Select one or more enemy units within **12"** as charge targets.
- Each target unit attempts to fire **Overwatch**.

### 3. Overwatch

- Targets may fire Overwatch immediately after a charge is declared.
- A unit cannot fire Overwatch if any enemy models are within 1" of it.
- Overwatch uses normal shooting rules but requires a **6 to hit**, regardless of Ballistic Skill or modifiers.

### 4. Make Charge Move

- Roll **2D6** for charge distance.
- Each model may move up to this distance.
- The first model must end within 1" of an enemy model from the target units.
- Models cannot move within 1" of enemies not targeted by the charge.
- If this is impossible, the charge fails.
- Repeat for other eligible units.

---

## 5. FIGHT PHASE

The battlefield is engulfed in carnage as armies clash.

### 1. Choose Unit to Fight With

- Any unit that charged or has models within 1" of an enemy fights.
- All charging units fight first; turn player chooses their order.
- Players alternate choosing units until all eligible units have fought.
- No unit fights more than once per Fight phase.

### 2. Pile In

- Each model may move up to **3"**, ending closer to the nearest enemy model.

### 3. Choose Targets

- Attacking models must be within 1" of the enemy unit or within 1" of a friendly model that is within 1" of the enemy.
- Models that charged can only target units they charged.
- Attacks can be split among multiple targets, declared before rolling.

### Fight Sequence

- Choose unit to fight with
- Pile in up to 3"
- Choose targets
- Choose melee weapon
- Resolve close combat attacks
- Make hit roll
- Make wound roll
- Enemy allocates wound
- Enemy makes saving throw
- Inflict damage
- Consolidate up to 3"

### Charge Sequence

- Choose unit to charge with
- Choose targets
- Enemy resolves Overwatch
- Roll 2D6 and make charge move

---

## Heroic Intervention

After enemy charge moves, **CHARACTER models** within 3" of an enemy unit may move up to **3"** closer as a Heroic Intervention.

---

## Number of Attacks

- Determined by the model’s **Attacks characteristic**.
- Roll one dice per close combat attack.

---

## 4. Choose Melee Weapon

- Models use melee weapons from their datasheet.
- If none listed, the model uses a default **close combat weapon**:

| Weapon              | Range   | Type  | Strength (S) | Armour Penetration (AP) | Damage (D) |
|---------------------|---------|-------|--------------|-------------------------|------------|
| Close combat weapon  | Melee   | Melee | User         | -                       | 1          |

- Models with multiple weapons choose which to use.
- Attacks can be split between multiple melee weapons.

---

## 5. Resolve Close Combat Attacks

- Use similar sequence as shooting attacks, but use **Weapon Skill** instead of Ballistic Skill for hit rolls.

---

## 6. Consolidate

- Models may move up to **3"**, ending closer to the nearest enemy model.

---

## 6. MORALE PHASE

Battle horrors test even the bravest hearts.

- Players take Morale tests for units that lost models this turn.
- Roll a dice and add the number of models slain.
- If the result exceeds the highest **Leadership characteristic** in the unit, the test fails.
- For each point failed, one model flees and is removed.
- The player chooses which models flee.

---

## TRANSPORTS

Transport vehicles ferry warriors, offering speed and protection.

### Transport Capacity

- Listed on datasheets.
- Limits number and type of carried friendly models.
- Capacity cannot be exceeded.
- Units may start embarked inside transports.

### Embark

- Units can embark by ending their move within **3"** of a friendly transport.
- Remove the embarked unit from the battlefield.
- Embarked units cannot act or be affected unless stated.
- If the transport is destroyed, embarked units immediately disembark with risk of casualties (roll 1 dice per model; a roll of 1 kills one model).

### Disembark

- Units may disembark before the transport moves.
- Must be set up within 3" of the transport and not within 1" of enemies.
- Models that cannot be placed this way are slain.
- Disembarked units can act normally that turn.
- Disembarking counts as having moved for rules.

---

## Example Melee Weapon Profile

| WEAPON                | RANGE | TYPE  | S (Strength) | AP (Armour Penetration) | D (Damage) |
|-----------------------|-------|-------|--------------|-------------------------|------------|
| Close combat weapon    | Melee | Melee | User         | -                       | 1          |

---

## Example Turn (Warhammer 40,000)

This example shows a turn for the **Death Guard** player attacking a **Space Marines** force.

### 1. Movement Phase

- The Death Guard moves their **Plague Marines** (Move characteristic 5") close to the Space Marines.
- The Death Guard then moves their **Malignant Plaguecaster**, choosing to Advance.

### 3. (Text ends abruptly here)

## Shooting Phase

The **Death Guard player** selects the unit of **Plague Marines** to shoot with. The **Plague Marines** will shoot with their **boltguns**, while the **Plague Champion** will throw a **krak grenade**.

## 2. Psychic Phase

The **Death Guard** only has a single psyker – the **Malignant Plaguecaster**. This model attempts to manifest the **Smite** power. The player rolls a **D6**, scoring a **4**.

The **Malignant Plaguecaster** (Move 5") can move up to **9"**. The targets are **6"** away, which is within range of the **Plague Marines’ boltguns**. These are **Rapid Fire 1** weapons, and so each fires twice at half range or less.

The **Death Guard player** rolls **8 dice** to see if the shots hit. The **Plague Marines’ Ballistic Skill is 3+**, so **6 shots hit** and the others miss.

The **Death Guard player** takes a **Psychic test** by rolling **2D6**, scoring a total of **6**. This is greater than the power’s **warp charge value of 5**, so the test is passed.

The closest enemy unit are the **Intercessors**. They suffer **D3 mortal wounds**. The **Death Guard player** rolls a **5**, which means the **Intercessor Squad loses 3 wounds**, enough to kill one **Intercessor** and wound another.

The **Death Guard player** then makes a wound roll for each hit. A **boltgun’s Strength of 4** equals the target’s **Toughness of 4**, meaning a roll of **4+** is required to successfully wound the target. The **Death Guard player** rolls for each shot; four of which are successful.

The **Space Marine player** will now need to make a **saving throw** for each wound. One of the rolls is less than the **Intercessor’s Save characteristic of 3+**, so the wound is allocated to the wounded **Intercessor**.

A **boltgun inflicts 1 point of damage** on this model, which removes its last wound and it is slain. The other wounds are saved and bounce off the **Space Marines’ power armour**.

## 4. Charge Phase

The **Death Guard player** chooses the **Plague Marines** to charge the **Intercessors**.

## 5. Fight Phase

Units that charged always resolve their fights first. In this case, that means the **Plague Marines unit fights first**.

The **Space Marine player** fires **Overwatch** and makes **4 hit rolls**. Models only hit on **6s** when firing Overwatch; however, both hits go on to wound, and both saving throws are failed – **two models are slain**!

After resolving **Overwatch**, the **Death Guard player rolls 2D6**, scoring **7**. The **Plague Marines can charge 7"**, enough to move within **1"** of the **Intercessors**.

They start by **piling in**, each model moving up to **3" closer** to the nearest model. All are now within **1" of an enemy**.

The **Death Guard player** has no other units that can fight, so the **Space Marine unit fights**, slaying a single **Plague Marine** in return.

The **Plague Marines** will use their **plague knives** to make their close combat attacks against the **Intercessor unit**, but the **Plague Champion**, who has an **Attacks characteristic of 2**, chooses to make **1 close combat attack using his plague sword**, and **1 using his power fist**.

The **Death Guard player rolls 2 hit rolls** for the **plague knives** (rolling a 3 and a 5), **1 for the plague sword** (rolling a 3), and **1 for the power fist** (rolling a 2).

The **Plague Marines** and the **Plague Champion** both have a **Weapon Skill characteristic of 3+**, so the attack made with the **power fist** misses, but all the others hit.

After **wound rolls and saving throws** are taken, another **Intercessor has been slain**.

The **Plague Marine unit then consolidates**, one of its models moving closer to the nearest enemy model.

The **Plague Champion** then throws a **krak grenade**, which hits. This grenade has a **Strength of 6**, which wounds the **Intercessors on a roll of 3+** as its Strength is greater than the Intercessors’ Toughness.

The **Space Marine player** then rolls a **3** for their saving throw but must subtract **1** from the roll because the krak grenade has an **AP characteristic of -1**. The final result of **2 fails to protect** the Space Marines.

A **krak grenade inflicts D3 damage**; the **Death Guard player rolls a 6**, inflicting **3 points of damage**. This causes an **Intercessor to lose both its wounds**.

As it is slain by this attack, the other point of damage is discarded and has no effect.
