The **Death Guard player** goes first, rolling a **6**. Three **Plague Marines died this turn**, so **3** is added to the roll, for a total of **9**.

This exceeds the **highest Leadership in the unit by 1** (the **Plague Champion has a Leadership characteristic of 8**), so **1 of the remaining models flees the battlefield**.

The **Space Marine player** then takes a **Morale test for the Intercessors**, rolling a **3**. When the number of casualties is added, they have a total of **7**.

This is less than the **unit’s highest Leadership of 8** – the test is passed and **no models flee**.

The **Death Guard turn** is now complete, and the **Space Marine player** can start their turn.

---

## Fighting a Battle

### The Mission

Before you can wage war in a game of **Warhammer 40,000**, you must select a **mission**.

The **core rules** include a single mission – **Only War** – which is ideal to get the action started quickly.

Other missions can be found elsewhere in this book, in other books, or you could play a mission of your own creation.

If you and your opponent can’t agree on which mission to play, both players should roll a dice, re-rolling ties, and whoever rolls the highest decides on the mission.

### The Battlefield

In the far future, battles are fought across an infinite variety of strange and alien planets where no land is left untouched by the blight of war.

Examples of **fantastical landscapes** include:

- Crystal moons  
- Derelict space hulks  
- Carnivorous death worlds  
- Nightmarish Daemon worlds  

A **battlefield** can be any surface upon which the models can stand – a dining table, for example, or the floor.

We typically assume a battlefield is **6' by 4'** (although some missions will state other dimensions), but it should always be large enough to accommodate all your models – if it is not, simply increase the size of the battlefield.

Unless the mission you are playing instructs otherwise, you should then feel free to create an exciting battlefield using any **terrain features** from your collection that you wish.

In general, we recommend having **one or two features** in each **2' by 2'** area.

Don’t worry if your battlefield doesn’t match these requirements, but keep in mind that playing on very small or very large battlefields, or ones that are either a barren wasteland or filled to overflowing with terrain features, may give an advantage to one side or the other.

### Battlezones & Expansions

If you are battling in a specific **battlezone**, or if you are using a particular **expansion**, there might be additional rules pertaining to setting up the battlefield, and special rules that alter how some terrain interacts with your warriors.

Bear these in mind when creating your battlefield.

### The Warlord

Once you have mustered your army, nominate one of your models to be your **Warlord**.

If your Warlord is a **CHARACTER**, it can use a **Warlord Trait** – a preferred tactic or personal ability that marks them out amongst their peers.

Immediately before either player starts to deploy their army, you can roll on the **Warlord Trait table** here to determine what Warlord Trait your Warlord has.

Alternatively, choose the trait that most suits your Warlord’s temperament or style of war.

### Warlord Traits

| D3 | Warlord Trait        | Description                                                                                     |
|-----|----------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 1   | Legendary Fighter    | If this Warlord charges in the Charge phase, add **1** to their **Attacks characteristic** until the end of the ensuing Fight phase. |
| 2   | Inspiring Leader     | Friendly units within **6"** of this Warlord can add **1** to their **Leadership characteristic**. |
| 3   | Tenacious Survivor   | Roll a dice each time this Warlord loses a wound. On a **6**, the Warlord shrugs off the damage and does not lose the wound. |

> **'There can be no bystanders in the battle for survival. Anyone who will not fight by your side is an enemy you must crush.'**  
> – Scriptorus Munificantus

---

## Only War

### Primary Objectives

| D3 | Victory Conditions                                                     |
|-----|------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 1   | **Slay and Secure**: At the end of the battle, each objective marker is worth **2 victory points** to the player who controls it. Players also earn **D3 victory points** if the opposing army’s **Warlord was slain** during the battle. |
| 2   | **Ancient Relic**: At the start of the first battle round, but before the first turn begins, randomly select one objective marker; remove the other objective markers from the battlefield. At the end of the battle, the remaining objective marker is worth **6 victory points** to the player who controls it. |
| 3   | **Domination**: At the end of each turn, each objective marker is worth **1 victory point** to the player who controls it. Keep a running score from turn to turn. |

### The Armies

To play this mission, first muster an **army** from the miniatures in your collection.

You can include any models in your army.

Sometimes you may find that you do not have enough models to field a minimum-sized unit (found on each unit’s datasheet); if this is the case, you can still include one unit of that type in your army with as many models as you have available.

### The Battlefield Setup

Create the battlefield and set up **terrain**.

The players must then place **objective markers** to represent sites of tactical or strategic import that one or both armies are attempting to secure.

Objective markers can be represented by any suitable marker or piece of terrain.

Each player must place **two objective markers** anywhere on the battlefield, so long as they are each at least **10" away** from any other objective marker.

It is suggested to take turns placing these, starting with whichever player wins a roll-off.

A player **controls** an objective marker if there are **more models from their army within 3" of it** than there are enemy models (measure to the centre of the marker).

### Deployment

Once the victory conditions have been determined, the player who did not roll on the primary objectives table divides the battlefield into two equal-sized halves.

Their opponent then decides which half is their own **deployment zone**, and which half is the other player’s deployment zone.

Players then alternate deploying their units, one at a time, starting with the player who did not pick their deployment zone.

Models must be set up:

- In their own deployment zone  
- More than **12"** from the enemy deployment zone  

Continue setting up units until both players have set up all the units in their army or run out of room.

### Power Level

Before battle begins, determine each army’s **Power Level** by adding together the Power Ratings of all the units set up in that army.

Whichever player has the lowest is the **Underdog**.

If both have the same Power Level, the player who assigned the deployment zones is the Underdog.

If the difference between the Power Levels of the two armies is:

- **10 to 19:** Underdog receives **one Command re-roll**  
- **20 to 29:** Underdog receives **two Command re-rolls**  
- And so on...

Each **Command re-roll** can be used once, at any point during the battle, to re-roll a single dice.

### First Turn

The **Underdog** chooses who has the first turn.

### Battle Length

The battle lasts for **five battle rounds**, or until one army has slain all of its foes.

### Victory Conditions

If one army has slain all of its foes, it immediately wins a **major victory**.

Otherwise, at the end of the battle, the player who has the most **victory points** wins a **major victory**.

If both players have the same number of victory points at the end of the battle, the **Underdog wins a minor victory**.

---

**The time has come to prove your worth as the greatest warlord in the galaxy!**

## Open Play in Warhammer 40,000

All that stands between you and **ultimate glory** is an enemy army bent upon your destruction.  

Are you new to **tabletop wargaming**? Or are you a grizzled veteran looking for a new challenge? Either way, **open play games** are one of the best ways to get started, providing you with almost limitless options and flexibility. Brilliant ideas are sometimes the simplest, and open play games of **Warhammer 40,000** epitomise this.

Open play is a style of gaming that allows you to take to the battlefield with **any army**, made up of any **Citadel Miniatures** from your collection – no restrictions. It’s as straightforward and streamlined as wargaming gets, and it’s a great way to begin.

Many players love the deep and complex rules that have traditionally defined tabletop wargaming, and if that’s your preferred style, then you’ll find plenty of support and guidance right here in this book. However, there’s also a lot of fun to be found in a more flexible approach.

### What You Need for Open Play

All you need to play an open play game are your **painted miniatures**, their **datasheets**, the **core rules**, a **set of dice**, a **tape measure**, a surface on which to play, and a **willing opponent**. Then, just set up your models and start having fun!

You can add extra dimensions to your open play games by incorporating any of the rules or guidelines that appear in this and other **Warhammer 40,000** books, such as rules for **Detachments**, **Battlezones**, and **battlefield terrain**.

Alternatively, you can devise your own missions, creating entirely new objectives or special rules, or adapt any existing mission to better suit your needs.

### Flexibility and Accessibility

The flexible nature of open play means that you can spend as much or as little time as you like reading rules. It’s a great introduction to the world of tabletop games. This style of gaming is perfect for **beginners**, who may not yet own a complete collection of miniatures. It’s also ideal for veterans thinking of starting a new collection, allowing battles to be fought with just a few units of the models you plan to collect, so you can see how they perform and what tactics work best with them.

> "THERE IS NOTHING TO FEAR BUT FAILURE. THROUGH BLOOD AND FIRE I MARCH. IN WAR ETERNAL MY HEARTS THUNDER. I AM AN ANGEL BORN OF VIOLENCE, A SOLDIER FORGED IN LEGEND. I AM THE BLADE IN THE EMPEROR’S HAND, THE HOLY CERAMITE OF HIS ARMOUR."  

## Army Selection in Open Play

Open play games allow the broadest choice of **army selection**, providing the greatest degree of freedom for collecting miniatures and putting together an army. Rather than structuring your collection around a particular **Faction** (pg 240), you can be inspired by any facet of the diverse and brutal galaxy, or simply by the models you most admire.

If you’re the proud owner of a varied collection of warriors, war machines, and monstrous creatures, there’s nothing to stop you fielding all of them in a single game. You can even deploy every last miniature you own in a battle of apocalyptic proportions, or set yourself unusual challenges.

For instance, you could:

- Discover how many **Space Marine Intercessors** it takes to bring down your friend’s **Khorne Bloodthirster**
- See how long a heroic **Terminator Captain** could fight off a **Nurgling horde**

While there are no restrictions or requirements placed on the models you can use in open play games, it’s best to have a chat with your opponent before the game begins to discuss what models you will each be taking in your armies.

You can even make use of elements of **matched play**, like points, if you wish, but it is entirely up to you.

### Multi-Player Battles and Customisation

Besides giving you freedom to do more with your collection, open play games are also perfect for battles between multiple players. For example, a third player might bring their **Drukhari raiders** to the battlefield. The piratical xenos strike from the shadows, preying on targets from the other armies, or perhaps even forging fleeting alliances with one side or the other.

In open play, the types of battles you fight are limited only by your imagination.

You should feel free to tinker with any aspect of playing a game of **Warhammer 40,000** that appeals to you. You could, for example, devise other methods of deploying your forces. You might place a screen across the centre of the table so armies can deploy in secret, or both players might draw maps showing where they plan to deploy their units.

With so much scope for fun and creativity, open play is one of the most accessible and enjoyable gaming styles, for both beginners and veterans alike.

So what are you waiting for? Grab your miniatures collection, however large or small, and give open play a try!

> “‘Sickness, disease, plague and pox, suffering and the slow, living rot. Such wondrous gifts does Nurgle seek to bestow upon the unworthy human cattle of the Imperium. We are merely the vectors by which His virulent beneficence may be spread to the undeserving masses.’”  
> — Urgloth Rotheart, Plague Champion of the Death Guard

## WAR WITHOUT END: Sample Open Play Missions

No form of war is unknown in the galaxy. Here are three examples of open play missions – **Annihilation**, **Hold at all Costs**, and **Death or Glory** – that you can use to start waging war right away.

You will also find a few ideas below to spark your imagination for other open play battles; feel free to use these hooks as the basis of your battles or create your own.

### Sample Mission Ideas

- An elite force strikes behind enemy lines to assassinate the foe’s commanders.
- An evil ritual is nearing completion – fight to prevent its culmination or bring about its fruition.
- A group of sappers attempts to sabotage a mighty war machine or fortress before it becomes fully operational.
- A convoy is ambushed – how many of its vital supplies can it escape with?
- You and your opponent(s) race to reach a powerful relic first, using your fastest units.
- Your allies suddenly turn traitor and open fire upon your lines. Can you wage war on two fronts?
- Your enemy believes their position unassailable; lead a forlorn attempt to breach their defenses.
- A band of operatives must silence sentries to enable their army’s approach.
- A priceless piece of **archeotech** is lost in war-torn ruins – your forces must secure it.
- A beleaguered army must hold out long enough for reinforcements.
- Escort a dignitary safely across the war zone.
- Snipers and close-quarters fighters battle amid the ruins of a fallen hive city.
- After months of fighting, the enemy army is on the verge of routing. Break their morale to secure victory.

## TEAM GAMES

**Warhammer 40,000** battles are conventionally fought between two players, but battling it out with three or more players adds a different dynamic and ensures no one has to sit out.

The real joy of **team games** is the social aspect. You’ll discover true camaraderie with your fellow gamers through good-natured banter across the battlefield. This gaming style is fun for friend and foe alike.

### How to Play Team Games

- Once all players have assembled with their armies, split into two teams – how you divide players is entirely up to you.
- Select one model on each team to be their **Warlord**.
- Play the battle exactly as normal, using the same rules but replacing terms like ‘player’ and ‘opponent’ with ‘team’ or ‘opposing team’.

## Missions

### Annihilation

Two warlords face each other, intent on destroying all that stand before them. Each must attempt to annihilate their opponent whilst minimising their own losses.

#### The Armies

- Muster an army from your miniatures collection.
- You can include any models.
- Works best when both armies have a roughly equal **Power Level**.

#### The Battlefield

Create the battlefield and set up terrain.

#### Deployment

1. Players roll off.
2. The highest roll divides the battlefield into two equal halves.
3. The player with the lowest roll picks a half as their deployment zone; the other half is their opponent’s.
4. Players alternate deploying units, starting with the player who did not pick their deployment zone.
5. Models must be set up in their deployment zone, more than 12" from the enemy.
6. Continue until all units have been deployed or there is no room.

#### First Turn

The player who finished setting up first chooses whether to take the first or second turn.

#### Battle Length

The battle lasts for five battle rounds, or until one army has slain all foes.

#### Victory Conditions

- Immediate **major victory** if one army slays all foes.
- Otherwise, the player with the most models remaining wins a **minor victory**.

---

### Hold at All Costs

The battlefield lies at a crossing of key strategic importance. A defending army stands ready to hold it at all costs against a superior foe.

#### The Armies

- Muster an army from your miniatures collection.
- Includes any models.
- Works best when one army’s **Power Level** is between a third higher and double that of the other.
- The higher Power Level army is the **Attacker**; the other is the **Defender**.

#### The Battlefield

- Create battlefield and terrain.
- Centre should have at least one terrain feature (hill, building, or large ruin) that the Defender’s units hold.

#### Deployment

- Defender sets up entire army anywhere within 18" of the centre.
- Attacker sets up entire army more than 12" from any enemy model.

#### First Turn

Players roll off; highest can choose first or second turn.

#### Battle Length

Five battle rounds or until one army has slain all foes.

#### Victory Conditions

- Immediate **major victory** if one army slays all foes.
- Otherwise, player whose model is closest to the centre wins a **major victory**.

---

### Death or Glory

An outnumbered army faces inevitable defeat, but if they sell their lives dearly, and at least one warrior survives, they earn a heroic death.

#### The Armies

- Muster an army from your miniatures collection.
- Any models allowed.
- Best when one army’s **Power Level** is at least twice that of the other.
- The stronger army is the **Attacker**; the other is the **Defender**.

#### The Battlefield

Create the battlefield and set up terrain.

#### Deployment

1. Players roll off.
2. The player who rolled lowest chooses a half as their deployment zone; the other half is the opponent’s.
3. Attacker sets up entire army first.
4. Defender sets up entire army second.

## Deployment and Battle Setup

- **Models** must be set up in their own **deployment zone**, more than **12"** from the enemy deployment zone.

### First Turn

- The **Defender** can choose whether to have the **first** or **second turn**.

### Battle Length

- The battle lasts for **five battle rounds**, or until one army has slain all of its foes.

### Victory Conditions

- If one army has slain all of its foes, it immediately wins a **major victory**.
- Otherwise, at the end of the battle, the **Defender** wins a **heroic victory** if they have even a single model remaining on the battlefield.

---

## Narrative Play

With a cast of **indomitable heroes**, **diabolical villains**, and **enigmatic xenos**, a plot of **system-spanning conflicts**, unshakeable loyalty, and ruthless betrayals, and of course spectacular battles, every **Warhammer 40,000 story** is an epic in itself.

### Concept

- **Narrative play** is all about enacting such tales on your own battlefield.
- Across the galaxy, **relentless battles** of conquest and survival are fought between the forces of the **Imperium**, **Chaos**, and the disparate **xenos** races.
- Recreating these sprawling conflicts on the tabletop is a hugely popular part of the Games Workshop hobby, allowing you to make these stories your own.

### Characteristics

- Narrative play ties the battles you play on your tabletop to the **stories of the Imperium and its foes**.
- Most games of **Warhammer 40,000** tell a story.
- Players often talk about why their armies might be fighting, creating a **narrative game**.

### Story Integration

- Armies might be modified to better reflect protagonists of the story.
- Specific **scenery** might recreate the landscape.
- **House rules** might represent the consequences of victory and defeat.
- Paint schemes can reflect the narrative the players are trying to create.

### Battle-Forged Armies

- Narrative play can be enhanced through **Battle-forged armies** (pg 240).
- Units are organized into **Detachments**, reflecting the background of their Faction.
- Commands Points are awarded, giving access to general and mission-specific **Stratagems** to shape the battle.

### Story Examples

- Stories in Warhammer 40,000 describe battles fought by named individuals and specific armies.
- Example: The **Ambush at Dhorak Pass**, where **Cadian regiments** commanded by **Commissar Odoski** came under attack from the **Alpha Legion**.

---

## Narrative Play Missions

We have included a mission that allows you to refight the **Ambush at Dhorak Pass**, as well as a general guide on creating your own missions based on historical events.

- These battles are called **‘Echoes of War’** missions.
- The section also includes **six missions** called **‘Crucible of War’** missions, representing classic battle types that can be adapted for your narrative.

### Example Mission: The Meat Grinder

- Centers on a **desperate defense** against a foe who throws forces in ceaseless waves.
- Represents conflicts like **Ghazghkull Thraka’s assault on Hades Hive** or the **Ultramarines’ defense of Macragge’s polar fortresses** during the **First Tyrannic War**.

### Asymmetrical Gameplay

- Narrative games are typically **asymmetrical**, with one player as the attacker, the other the defender.
- Players’ armies might have different composition and abilities.
- Such games require different skills and stratagems to succeed.

### Detailed and Bespoke Rules

- Narrative games tend to have more bespoke rules than open or matched play.
- This is because narrative missions try to recreate specific stories, events, and strategies.
- Planning and selecting special rules is often as fun as playing.

### Flexibility and Creativity

- All missions and rules in this section inspire battles of your own creation.
- Games can be **one-off** or **campaigns** (pg 272), with flexible armies and rules.
- The only limitation is the story you create!

### Quote

> “To hunt the Fallen, we must be strong, swift and silent. We must place trust in our sworn brothers alone, and show neither mercy nor hesitation to any who seek to obstruct or betray us.”  
> — Sergeant Zamorael, Dark Angels Ravenwing

> **HATRED IS THE EMPEROR’S GREATEST GIFT TO HUMANITY.**

---

## Narrative Play Mission Rules

Most narrative play missions use additional **special rules** to better represent tactics and strategies for attackers and defenders.

### Concealed Deployment

- The **Defender** gets a **set-up marker** for each unit they intend to start deployed on the battlefield.
- No markers are needed for units embarked on a **TRANSPORT** (only for the transport itself).
- Each marker must be **distinct** (e.g., by number) to correspond to a specific unit.
- The defender writes down which unit each marker represents, keeping this **secret**.
- The defender sets up markers instead of models, after which the attacker deploys.
- Then the defender reveals marker-to-unit assignments and sets up models.
- The first model in each unit must be placed exactly where its marker was.
- The unit must be wholly within the defender’s deployment zone.

### Dawn Raid

- Both players subtract **1** from all **hit rolls** made in the **Shooting phase** during the **first battle round**.
- Represents commanders attacking under **cover of darkness**.

### Preliminary Bombardment

- At the start of the first battle round, before the game begins, the **Attacker** rolls a dice for each enemy unit on the battlefield (not embarked units).
- A roll of **6** means the unit suffers a **Preliminary Bombardment** and takes **D6 mortal wounds**.
- Infantry units hit can choose to **go to ground** before damage: suffer only **D3 mortal wounds** but cannot act in their first turn.

### Random Battle Length

- At the end of **battle round 5**, the player who had the **first turn** rolls a D6.
  - On **3+**, the game continues; otherwise it ends.
- At the end of **battle round 6**, the player who had the **second turn** rolls a D6.
  - On **4+**, the game continues; otherwise it ends.
- The battle automatically ends at the end of **battle round 7**.

### Reserves

- Some units start in **Reserve** and are not deployed initially.
- The mission states when Reserve units arrive, usually at the end of a Movement phase.
- If unspecified, roll a **Reserve roll** at the end of your second Movement phase and each thereafter.
  - On **3+**, the unit arrives.
- Units embarked inside a **TRANSPORT** arrive with the transport.
- Arrival points and deployment are explained in each mission, typically near a designated battlefield edge.

### Sentries

- Used to guard locations and raise alarms.
- The **Defender** gains an extra unit as **Sentries**, usually Troops, up to 10 models, Power Rating 10 or less.
- Sentries’ Power Rating is excluded from total army Power Level.
- Each Sentry model acts as a **separate, individual unit**.
- At the start of each Defender Movement phase, both players roll a dice for each Sentry model in an order Defender chooses.
  - The highest roller moves the model the number shown on the dice in any direction (no Advancing).
  - If tied, the Sentry does not move.
- The alarm is initially **not raised**.

#### Alarm Conditions

The alarm is raised if any of the following occur:

- An **Attacker** fires a ranged weapon or manifests a psychic power.
- An **Attacker** attacks a Sentry in the Fight phase but fails to kill it.
- An **Attacker** is spotted by a Sentry (within spotting range at the end of any Movement phase).

**Spotting range** depends on the Power Rating of the Attacker’s unit.

> If the alarm arises during the Attacker’s turn, that turn immediately ends after the action that caused the alarm.

---

## Thought for the Day

**ONLY IN DEATH DOES DUTY END**

## Alarm and Defender's Turn

If the **alarm** is raised during the **Defender’s turn**, the Defender immediately starts a new turn in which they can typically set up **response forces** or **reinforcements**; this will be detailed in the mission itself. In either case, the **Sentries** are now under full control of the Defender.

### Power Rating Spotted Within

- **5 or less:** 3"
- **6-10:** 6"
- **11-19:** 9"
- **20 or more:** 12"

---

## Sustained Assault

Occasionally, an army will possess overwhelming superiority in numbers, with wave upon wave of its troops hurling themselves forward. If your mission uses **Sustained Assault**, any of the **Attacker’s units** that are destroyed can be brought back into play later in the battle, to represent their almost limitless supply of reinforcements.

At the end of each of the **Attacker’s Movement phases**, roll a dice for each of their destroyed units, adding 2 to the result if that unit has the **Troops Battlefield Role**. On a 4+, immediately set up that unit within 6" of a battlefield edge – the mission will specify which.

The **Attacker** can also, at the end of any of their turns, remove any of their units from the battlefield that have a quarter or less of their starting number of models (or, in the case of single-model units, a quarter or less of its starting number of wounds). This unit then counts as having been destroyed for all purposes, and so can be brought back into play later as described above.

---

## Crucible of War

### Meat Grinder

The enemy forces arrayed against you are the last stubborn defenders of this war zone, grimly holding out despite being overwhelmingly outnumbered. You have been committed to lead an all-out attack to annihilate them in their entirety. Friendly casualties are of no concern – no enemy must survive!

### The Armies

Each player must first muster an **army** from the miniatures in their collection. A player can include any models in their army, but if their army is **Battle-forged** (pg 240) they will also be able to use the appropriate **Stratagems** included with this mission. 

Once the armies have been chosen, the players must then decide who will be the **Attacker** and who will be the **Defender**. If the **Power Levels** of the two armies are different, then the player whose army has the higher Power Level should be the Attacker and their opponent should be the Defender. Otherwise the players can roll off to decide.

### The Battlefield

Create a battlefield using the deployment map below and then set up terrain. The **Defender’s deployment zone** should contain several defensible pieces of terrain, such as **ruins** or **obstacles**, from which they can make their defiant last stand. The **Attacker’s deployment zone** should be more sparse by comparison, to better represent the **no man’s land** they are crossing.

### Deployment

After terrain has been set up, the players then deploy their armies using the **Concealed Deployment rules** (pg 194). None of the Defender’s units can use abilities that allow them to arrive on the battlefield mid-battle – such units must be set up on the battlefield during deployment, using the Concealed Deployment rules.

### Preliminary Bombardment

Once both sides have been set up, the **Attacker** launches a **Preliminary Bombardment** (pg 194).

### First Turn

The Attacker rolls a dice. On a 1, 2 or 3, the Attacker has the first turn, and on a 4, 5 or 6, the Defender has the first turn.

### Sustained Assault

The Attacker can use the **Sustained Assault rules** (pg 195) to represent their overwhelming superiority in numbers. Each time one of the Attacker’s replacement units arrives, set up the models in that unit within 6" of the Attacker’s battlefield edge.

### Battle Length

The players should use the **Random Battle Length rules** (pg 194) to determine how long the battle lasts.

### Victory Conditions

If at the end of the battle the **Defender** has any models remaining on the battlefield, they win a **major victory**. Any other result is a major victory for the Attacker.

---

### Key Map Terms

- **Defender’s Deployment Zone**
- **Defender’s Battlefield Edge**
- **Attacker’s Battlefield Edge**
- **Attacker’s Deployment Zone**

---

## Stratagems for Meat Grinder Mission

In this mission, players can use **Command Points (CPs)** to use the following bonus Stratagems:

- **Sustained Bombardment** (Attacker Stratagem)  
  Use immediately before rolling to see if a unit is hit by your Preliminary Bombardment. Roll 3 dice instead of 1. (1 CP)

- **Outflanking Reinforcements** (Attacker Stratagem)  
  Use when a replacement unit arrives on the battlefield. That unit can be set up anywhere within 6" of any battlefield edge other than the Defender’s battlefield edge. (2 CP)

- **Spies** (Attacker Stratagem)  
  Use immediately after the Defender has finished placing their setup markers. Select one of the markers – the Defender must reveal which unit is hiding there and immediately set the unit up. (1 CP)

- **Decoys** (Defender Stratagem)  
  Use immediately before placing your set-up markers. You can place two extra set-up markers as **decoys**. When a decoy is revealed, simply remove the marker. (1 CP)

- **Foxholes** (Defender Stratagem)  
  Use when one of your **INFANTRY** units is hit by a Preliminary Bombardment, but before hits are determined. Halve the number of hits (rounding up) suffered by that unit. (1 CP)

- **Traps** (Defender Stratagem)  
  Use when a replacement unit arrives on the battlefield. Roll a dice for each model in that unit – for each roll of 6, one model in that unit is slain (controlling player’s choice). (1 CP)

---

> **Thought for the Day:** LET NOT THE MUTANT SEEK OUR PLACES AND SHARE OUR LOT.

---

## Crucible of War: Ambush!

### Scenario Overview

Under cover of darkness, the attacker’s forces have prepared a deadly trap and are lying in wait for a convoy of enemy reserves heading for the front line. They hope to catch their foe unawares and destroy them utterly before they can escape or mount a retaliatory counter-strike.

### The Armies

Each player must muster an **army** from their miniatures collection. This mission works especially well with **ground-based armies** that contain few, if any, units that can **FLY**. Battle-forged armies can use the appropriate **Stratagems** included with this mission.

Players decide attacker/defender as before, based on **Power Levels** or by roll-off.

### The Battlefield

Create a battlefield using the deployment map below and then set up terrain. The **Defender’s deployment zone** represents a thoroughfare leading towards the front line and should be **exposed**. The **Attacker’s deployment zone** should be covered in dense terrain such as **woods** or **ruins**, making it a perfect ambush site.

### Deployment

After terrain setup:

- The **Attacker** uses **set-up markers** to deploy their army first.
- The **Defender** then sets up as normal using **Concealed Deployment rules** (pg 194).

### First Turn

The **Attacker** has the first turn.

### Dawn Raid

This mission uses the **Dawn Raid rules** (pg 194).

### Escape Route

The **Defender’s units** can move off the battlefield edge labelled **Escape Route** if all models can leave in the same phase. Units that escape are removed from the battlefield and take no further part in the battle.

### Battle Length

Use the **Random Battle Length rules** (pg 194) to determine battle length.

### Victory Conditions

At the end of the battle, add up the Power Ratings of all the **Defender’s escaped units** and compare this to the Power Level of their army. If the combined Power Rating of escaped units is one third or more of the army's Power Level, the Defender wins a **major victory**. Any other result is a major victory for the Attacker.

---

### Key Map Terms

- **Defender’s Deployment Zone**
- **Escape Route**
- **Attacker’s Deployment Zone**
- **Centre of Battlefield**

---

## Stratagems for Ambush! Mission

Players can spend **Command Points (CPs)** on these bonus Stratagems:

- **Night Raider** (Attacker Stratagem)  
  Use immediately after deployment. For each CP spent, the Dawn Raid rules apply for one additional battle round. (1+ CP)

- **Spectrum Enhancement Wargear** (Attacker Stratagem)  
  Select one of your units immediately before it makes shooting attacks. That unit can shoot without penalties from Dawn Raid this phase. (1 CP)

- **Preliminary Bombardment** (Attacker Stratagem)  
  Use immediately after both sides have deployed. Launch a Preliminary Bombardment (pg 194). (3 CP)

- **The Tables Turned** (Defender Stratagem)  
  Use immediately after deployment but before the first turn begins. Defender rolls a dice—on a 6, they get the first turn instead. (1 CP)

- **Return Fire** (Defender Stratagem)  
  Use at the end of your opponent’s first Shooting phase. Select a unit that was targeted by shooting; it can make a shooting attack as if it were your Shooting phase. (2 CP)

- **Iron Discipline** (Defender Stratagem)  
  Use after the Attacker has resolved a Preliminary Bombardment. Roll a dice for each unit that went to ground; on a 2+ they can act normally during their first turn. (1 CP)

---

> **Quote:** NOBODY IS INNOCENT, THERE ARE MERELY VARYING LEVELS OF GUILT.

---

## Crucible of War: Patrol

### Scenario Overview

You have been detailed to patrol **no man’s land** and drive off any enemy forces encountered. Additional forces are near at hand to secure victory, but watch out—the enemy also has reserves and will attempt the same.

### The Armies

Each player must muster an **army** from their collection. Battle-forged armies can use appropriate **Stratagems**. If the Power Level of one army is a third or more higher than the other, the higher Power Level army player is the Attacker. Otherwise, roll off to decide.

### The Battlefield

Create a battlefield with **ruined buildings** and **craters**, remnants of months of conflict.

### Deployment

- The **Defender** sets up any **three units** within their deployment zone; one of these must have the **Troops Battlefield Role**.
- The **Attacker** selects three units to serve as their patrol; one must have the Troops Battlefield Role.
- All other units arrive later using the **Reserves rules** (pg 194).

### First Turn

Both players roll a dice, rerolling ties. The highest roller chooses who has the **first turn**.

### Drawn to Battle

Starting from the second battle round, each player rolls for each of their units in **Reserve** at the end of their Movement phase.

- **Attacking units** arrive on a 4+
- **Defending units** arrive on a 3+

---

## Units Arrival and Setup

Units **automatically arrive** at the end of a player’s **fourth Movement phase** if they have not already done so. When a unit arrives, set it up **anywhere within 6" of the controlling player’s battlefield edge**.

- **Defender’s Battlefield Edge**  
- **Attacker’s Battlefield Edge**  
- **Defender’s Deployment Zone**  
- **Attacker’s Deployment Zone**  
- **Centre of Battlefield**

---

## STRATAGEMS

In this mission, players can use **Command Points (CPs)** to activate the following bonus **Stratagems**:

### Attacker Stratagems

- **ENCIRCLING REINFORCEMENTS**  
  Use this Stratagem when one of your units **arrives from Reserve**. That unit can be set up **anywhere within 6" of any battlefield edge other than the Defender’s battlefield edge**.

- **PATROL IN FORCE**  
  Use this Stratagem after the Defender has deployed their patrol. You can set up **one additional unit during deployment – this unit must have the Troops Battlefield Role**.

- **SIGNAL THE ATTACK**  
  Use this Stratagem at the end of your Movement phase, before making any Reserve rolls. Until the end of the turn, **add 1 to every Reserve roll you make**.

### Defender Stratagems

- **RAPID REINFORCEMENTS**  
  Use this Stratagem immediately before making a Reserve roll. The unit being rolled for **automatically arrives** – no roll is needed.

- **DELAYED RESERVES**  
  Use this Stratagem immediately before your opponent makes a Reserve roll. If you spend 1 CP, your opponent must subtract 1 from the roll; if you spend 2 CPs, they must subtract 2.

- **HOME ADVANTAGE**  
  Use this Stratagem immediately before rolling to determine who will have the first turn. You can roll **two dice instead of one, and choose the highest result**.

---

## Battle Length

Players should use the **Random Battle Length rules (pg 194)** to determine how long the battle lasts.

---

## Victory Conditions

- The player with the **most victory points** at the end of the game wins a **major victory**.
- If both players have the same number of victory points, the game is a **draw**.
- Each player scores **1 victory point for each enemy unit destroyed** (any unit not on the battlefield at the end counts as destroyed).

> **“MERCY IS A WORD FOR TRAITORS AND COWARDS. IT IS A WORD FOR HERETICS. LET ALL WHO SPEAK IT BE STRUNG UP BY THEIR DUPLICITOUS TONGUES.”**  
> – *Confessor Belithael of the Dark Angels*

> **ONLY FOOLS LISTEN TO THE HERETIC’S LIES.**

---

# CRUCIBLE OF WAR

## BLITZ

The **war progresses** with the offensive pushing the enemy back all along the front. The foe has mustered a **strong defence at a vital crossing**. You must attempt to **smash the defenders aside and drive deep into enemy territory**.

---

## THE ARMIES

- Each player must muster an **army from their miniatures collection**.
- This mission works best with **ground-based armies** that contain few or no units that can **FLY**.
- Battle-forged armies (pg 240) can use appropriate Stratagems included in this mission.
- Players decide who is the **Attacker** and **Defender**:
  - The player with the higher **Power Level** becomes the Attacker.
  - The other becomes the Defender.
  - If equal Power Levels, players roll off to decide.

---

## THE BATTLEFIELD

- Use the deployment map below and set up terrain.
- The battlefield represents a **well-defended and fortified position**.
- The **Defender’s Front Line** and **Second Line deployment zones** should have **dense terrain features** (ruins, obstacles, defense lines, razor wire) to halt the Attacker.
- The **Attacker’s deployment zone** is a **killing field** with **little cover available**.

---

## DEPLOYMENT

- After terrain setup, players use **Concealed Deployment rules (pg 194)**.
- The Defender must place an **equal number of set-up markers in their Front Line and Second Line deployment zones**.

---

## PRELIMINARY BOMBARDMENT

Once both sides are set up, the **Attacker launches a Preliminary Bombardment** (pg 194).

---

## FIRST TURN

The **Attacker has the first turn**.

- **Defender’s Battlefield Edge**  
- **Attacker’s Battlefield Edge**  
- **Attacker’s Deployment Zone**  
- **Defender’s Front Line Deployment Zone**  
- **Defender’s Second Line Deployment Zone**  
- **Centre of Battlefield**

---

## STRATAGEMS

Players can use the following **bonus Stratagems** by spending CPs:

### Attacker Stratagems

- **HEAVY BOMBARDMENT**  
  Use this immediately before rolling to see if a unit is hit by your Preliminary Bombardment. The unit is hit on a **4+ instead of 6**.

- **FORCED MARCH**  
  When a replacement unit arrives, set it up **anywhere within the Attacker’s deployment zone more than 9" away from any enemy**.

- **COVER GROUND**  
  Before a unit rolls for its Advance distance, **count as having rolled a 6**.

### Defender Stratagems

- **DUG-IN DEFENCES**  
  After setting up a unit, add **1 to that unit’s saving throws against all shooting attacks until it moves**.

- **PROXIMITY MINES**  
  The first time an enemy unit moves into or through your Front Line deployment zone, roll a dice for each model. For each **6**, one model in that unit is slain (controller's choice).

- **DECOYS**  
  Before placing set-up markers, place **two extra markers as decoys**. When revealed, simply remove the marker.

---

## SUSTAINED ASSAULT

- Represents the Attacker’s **overwhelming superiority in numbers**.
- Each time an Attacker replacement unit arrives, set it up **wholly within 6" of the Attacker’s battlefield edge**.
- The Attacker must **bring on units if possible – no holding back**.

---

## BATTLE LENGTH

Use the **Random Battle Length rules (pg 194)** to determine battle duration.

---

## VICTORY CONDITIONS

- The player with the most **victory points** wins a **major victory**.
- If tied, the game is a draw.
- Victory points are earned as follows:

  - **Break Through:**  
    - The Attacker scores **1 victory point** for each unit with at least one model completely within the **Defender’s Front Line deployment zone** at battle’s end.  
    - Scores **2 victory points** for each unit with at least one model completely within the **Defender’s Second Line deployment zone**.

  - **Destroy any Approach:**  
    - Each Attacker unit destroyed scores the **Defender 1 victory point**.

> **“SINS HIDDEN IN THE HEART TURN ALL TO DECAY.”**

---

# CRUCIBLE OF WAR

## SABOTAGE

The attacker leads a **surprise raid deep in enemy territory**. Their mission is to **sneak past sentries** guarding an important installation and **plant explosives to destroy it**. The defender is alert, ready to respond with deadly force if alarm is raised.

---

## THE ARMIES

- Players muster armies from their collection.
- This mission works best for armies with **Power Level 50 to 100**.
- Avoid armies with many (or any) **VEHICLES or MONSTERS**.
- Battle-forged armies (pg 240) can use mission-specific Stratagems.
- Players decide who is Attacker and Defender based on Power Levels or a roll-off.
- The Defender needs an **additional unit to act as Sentries** (pg 195).

---

## THE BATTLEFIELD

- Use the deployment map and set up terrain.
- The Defender’s deployment zone must include an **objective marker or suitable scenery wholly within 12" of the battlefield centre** representing the **Objective**.

---

## DEPLOYMENT

- Defender sets up **Sentries**:
  - At least **half within 12"** of the battlefield centre.
  - Remainder anywhere in Defender’s deployment zone.
- Attacker sets up as many units as desired within their deployment zone.
- Remaining units are placed in **Reserve**, arriving during battle as described.

---

## FIRST TURN

The **Attacker has the first turn**.

---

## RESERVES

### Attacker’s Reserves

- The Attacker can bring on Reserve units **at the end of each Movement phase**.
- Units must be set up **within 6" of their battlefield edge**.

### Defender’s Reserves

- The Defender can bring on Reserve units **at the end of any Movement phase after the alarm is sounded**.
- On the first turn after the alarm, a **roll of 3+ is required** to bring a reserve unit on.
- In subsequent turns, no roll is required.
- Units must be set up **wholly within 6" of one of the Defender’s battlefield edges** and **more than 9" from any enemy models**.

- **Attacker’s Deployment Zone**  
- **Centre of Battlefield**  
- **24"**  
- **Defender’s Deployment Zone**  
- **Defender’s Battlefield Edges**  
- **Attacker’s Battlefield Edge**

---

## STRATAGEMS

Players may use the following **bonus Stratagems** via CPs:

### Attacker Stratagems

- **SILENCED WEAPONS**  
  Use when making a shooting attack, immediately before resolution. The **alarm is only sounded if the target loses one or more wounds but is not slain**.

- **EXTRA EXPLOSIVES**  
  After a unit makes a Sabotage attempt, it can make **one additional Sabotage attempt during the game** (not another this turn).

- **CAMOUFLAGE**  
  When setting a unit up during deployment, **halve the unit’s Power Rating** for distance spotting by Sentries.

### Defender Stratagems

- **SENSORS**  
  After setting up Sentries, they can add **3" to spotting distances** for enemy models.

- **CUT THE WIRES**  
  If any unit is within 3" of the Objective at game end, reduce the number of Sabotage attempts made by 1 (minimum 0).

- **EXTRA SENTRIES**  
  Immediately before setting up Sentries, **two units can be set up as Sentries instead of one**.

---

## SABOTAGE

Attacker units can make a **Sabotage attempt** if they are within **3" of the Objective at the end of any of their turns**.

## Sabotage Attempts

An **individual unit** cannot attempt to **Sabotage the Objective** more than once during the battle. However, any number of different units from the **Attacker’s army** can make attempts. **VEHICLES** and **MONSTERS** are unable to make Sabotage attempts.

- Keep track of the number of Sabotage attempts during the mission.
- At the end of the battle, the **Attacker** rolls a dice and adds the number of Sabotage attempts.
- If the total is **7 or more**, the **Objective is destroyed** in a massive explosion.

**Proximity Alert:** The alarm sounds automatically from the end of the turn when the first Sabotage attempt is made, even if no **Sentries** remain on the battlefield.

## Battle Length

Players use the **Random Battle Length rules** (pg 194) to determine how long the battle lasts.

## Victory Conditions

- If the **Objective is destroyed** (see Sabotage), the **Attacker wins a major victory**.
- Otherwise, the **Defender wins a major victory**.

---

## Rescue Mission

A **spy** has narrowly evaded capture but remains trapped behind enemy lines. The mission is to locate the spy and escort them off the battlefield before enemy reinforcements arrive.

### The Armies

- Each player must **muster an army** from their miniatures.
- This mission works best with armies having a **Power Level of 50 to 100**, with few or no **VEHICLES** or **MONSTERS**.
- **Battle-forged armies** (pg 240) can use appropriate **Stratagems** included in this mission.
- Decide which player is the **Attacker** and which is the **Defender**:
  - Player with the higher Power Level is the Attacker.
  - Otherwise, decide by a roll-off.
- The **Attacker** needs a single **INFANTRY model** with Wounds no more than 4 to represent the Spy.
- The **Defender** requires an additional unit to act as **Sentries** (pg 195).

### The Spy

- The **Spy model** is not part of the Attacker’s Battle-forged army.
- It does **not contribute** to the Attacker’s Power Level.
- Treated as a **single model unit**.
- Can only be attacked if it is the **closest target**.

### The Battlefield

- Use the deployment map and set up terrain.
- Players alternate, starting with the Attacker, to choose terrain pieces in the Defender’s deployment zone where the Spy may hide.
- A total of **six terrain pieces** must be chosen (or six objective markers placed).

### Deployment

- Defender sets up **Sentries** (pg 195).
  - At least a third must be within 12" of battlefield center.
  - Remainder can be anywhere in Defender’s deployment zone.
- Attacker sets up any number of units within their deployment zone.
- Remaining units placed in **Reserve** to arrive later.
- **Attacker** has the **first turn**.

### Attacker’s Reserves

- May bring Reserve units onto the battlefield at the end of their **Movement phases**.
- Units arrive within **6"** of their battlefield edge.

### Defender’s Reserves

- Allowed to bring Reserve units at the end of any **Movement phase** after the alarm sounds.
- On the first turn after alarm, must roll a dice to arrive (4+).
- No roll required on subsequent turns.
- Units deploy wholly within **6"** of Defender’s battlefield edge, and **more than 9"** from enemy models.

### Finding the Spy

- Roll a dice when an Attacker’s model finishes a move within **3"** of a possible Spy terrain or marker.
- On a roll of **6**, or if last location possible, the Spy is placed within **3"** of the terrain, more than **1"** from enemy models.
- If this is impossible, the Spy is slain and the Attacker immediately **loses the battle**.
- The Spy cannot move during the Movement phase they are discovered.
- Alarm sounds automatically at the end of the turn the Spy is found, even if no Sentries remain.

### Battle Length and Victory

- Use **Random Battle Length rules** (pg 194).
- If the **Spy is discovered and alive** at the end, **Attacker wins**.
- Otherwise, **Defender wins**.

---

## Stratagems in Rescue Mission

Players can spend **Command Points (CPs)** to use the following bonus Stratagems:

### Attacker Stratagems

- **Silenced Weapons**  
  Use when a unit makes a shooting attack before the attack resolves. The alarm only sounds if the target loses 1 or more wounds but is not killed.

- **Scan for Distress Beacons**  
  Use at the end of Movement phase if a model is within **12"** of an unexplored terrain piece that may hide the Spy. On a **6**, the Spy is found and placed.

- **Night Raid**  
  Use after both sides deploy. The **Dawn Raid rules** (pg 194) apply and the spotting range for Sentries is halved during the first battle round.

### Defender Stratagems

- **Sensors**  
  Use after setting up Sentries. Sentries add **3"** to spotting distances.

- **Rapid Response**  
  Use before the Reserve arrival roll after the alarm sounds. The unit arrives automatically without a dice roll and can deploy within **6"** of any battlefield edge except the Attacker’s.

- **Extra Sentries**  
  Use immediately before setting up Sentries. Allows two units to be set up as Sentries instead of one.

---

## Historical Battles

The galaxy is filled with **heroic deeds** and **legendary battles**. With imagination, players can recreate these events on the tabletop and explore alternate outcomes.

- Players may want to replicate battles exactly or just incorporate thematic elements.
- Replaying a historical battle requires planning depending on scale and detail.
- Some battles have **Echoes of War missions** that provide ready-made scenarios.
- When no mission exists, players can create their own rules inspired by source materials, artwork, and detailed history.
- Translating units, heroes, strategies, and terrain into game terms enhances **authenticity and fun**.

---

## The Ambush at Dhorak Pass

### Background

- The **Cadian Dhorak front** was collapsing under relentless **Chaos** attacks.
- Reinforcements from the **Cadian 309th Armoured Regiment** and **822nd Infantry "The Sureshots"** were en route.
- The **Alpha Legion** set a trap with **quake-mines** and hidden troops under **warp storm darkness**.
- Vehicles stalled by mines and trapped by crossfire from hidden enemies.
- Despite superior numbers, the Imperial forces were whittled down.
- **Commissar Odoski** tried to reorganize a defensive line but fell into further Chaos ambushes with materializing Daemons.
- The battle ended with overwhelming loss and no reinforcements arriving.

### Echoes of War: Ambush at Dhorak Pass - The Mission

- Based on the **Ambush! mission** (pg 198) with additional rules and modifications.
- The **Defender** commands an **Astra Militarum army** of the **Cadian 309th Armoured** and **822nd Infantry** under **Commissar Odoski**.

## The Attacker

The **Attacker** commands **Alpha Legion Chaos Space Marines** and a host of their **Daemon allies**. The **Cadian forces** outnumber the Alpha Legion forces.

### The Battlefield

Use the deployment map and set up terrain as shown below to create the **Dhorak Pass battlefield**.

### Daemonic Ambush

The **Alpha Legion player's DAEMON units** are not set up during deployment but will arrive later during the battle. At the end of the Alpha Legion player's third **Movement phase**, they set up all of their **DAEMON units** anywhere on the battlefield more than 9" from any enemy model.

### Unnatural Darkness

Do not use the **Dawn Raid rules**. Instead, use all the rules from **Battlezone: Night Fight (pg 252)** to better reflect the darkness caused by the **warp storms**.

### Blocked Route

The wrecks in the middle of the battlefield have blocked the road. Models **cannot move through or over them** and must move around them.

### Quake-Mines

Roll a dice each time an **ASTRA MILITARUM** unit **Advances** along the **Dhorak Road** (see map) – on a 1 it triggers **quake-mines** buried by the Alpha Legion, and the unit immediately suffers **D6 mortal wounds**.

### The Sureshots

To represent their disciplined firing lines, the **Cadian player** can **re-roll any hit rolls of 1** in the **Shooting phase** for any of their **INFANTRY units** that remained stationary in their preceding **Movement phase**.

### Commissar Odoski

If **Commissar Odoski** exits the battlefield (see **Escape Route, pg 198**) then the battle immediately ends and the **Cadian player wins a major victory**.

The final battles of **Cadia** were marked not just by the terrible onslaught of **Abaddon’s assaults**, but also by innumerable synchronized ambushes. The action at the **Dhorak Pass crossroads** is an example of how the smaller **Alpha Legion strikes** could eliminate larger Imperial forces.

---

## Matched Play

Armies come in all shapes and sizes, with unique strengths and weaknesses, but to test a general’s mettle as a commander, there needs to be a level playing field. This is the goal of **matched play**.

### What is Matched Play?

Matched play games give you the option to fight battles with armies that are intentionally **balanced** against one another, allowing you to test both your **tactical skill** on the battlefield and your **strategic ability** to choose an army that can defeat all opponents!

### Army Selection Methods

There are several ways to choose an army for matched play games:

- Build an army to an agreed **points limit**
- Build armies with a set number of units
- Use the **Wounds characteristic** or **Power Rating** of each unit
- Set upper limits for each unit or fixed totals for both armies

These are only examples—you and your opponent can use any system you like, as long as you both agree.

### Forging an Army

Forging an army for matched play is a more detailed process than for open or narrative play games:

- Start with a conversation between you and your opponent to decide the parameters of the battle.
- Perform calculations to select forces according to agreed limits.
- Organize your army into **Detachments**, as all matched play games use **Battleforged army rules** (pg 240).

This process is straightforward and fun, and means the game essentially starts before the first miniature is even set up. Knowledge of units, wargear, and your opponent’s force is pivotal.

> "**BELLIGERENCE ALLIED TO FAITH CAN MOVE A MOUNTAIN.** ‘COLONEL DAGOSTIN, THE MUNITORUM MUST REGRETFULLY DENY YOUR REQUEST FOR REINFORCEMENT AT THIS TIME. LET FAITH AND PIETY BOLSTER YOUR RANKS IN THEIR PLACE. THE EMPEROR EXPECTS.’"  
> — Munitorum missive, War Zone: Narthossus

### Finding Balance

Which combinations of units work best may not be obvious initially, but playing a few games will help you find the best balance.

Most **Battleforged Detachments** grant you **Command Points** (pg 242), which provide access to **Stratagems**, powerful tools to turn the tide of battle.

---

## Eternal War and Maelstrom of War Missions

This section includes:

- Six **Eternal War** missions using fixed ways of scoring victory points.
- Six **Maelstrom of War** missions using dynamic **Tactical Objectives** that reflect changing orders.

Unlike narrative play missions where attackers or defenders may have slight advantages, matched play missions give both players the same goal for an even chance at victory.

### Benefits of Matched Play

- Equal army balance allows a decisive test of strategic acumen.
- Outcomes are unpredictable.
- Once settled, you have a **pick-up-and-play force** suitable for any opponent or table.
- No need to agree on settings or story, unlike narrative play.
- Ideal for **school leagues** and **tournaments**, ensuring battles are fair.
- Limits make it easier to control game length, perfect for quick games.
- Some tournaments add extra rules such as limits on Detachments or exclusive new Detachments for additional challenges.

> "**TWIST YOUR ENEMY’S DEEDS. RENDER HIS VICTORIES YOUR OWN. WEAVE ABOUT HIM THE STRANDS OF FATE AND PROVIDENCE UNTIL, WITH BUT A TWITCH OF HIS STRINGS, YOU COMPEL YOUR PUPPET TO LIE, TO KILL, AND EVEN SACRIFICE HIS OWN LIFE, IN FURTHERANCE OF THE WILL OF TZEENTCH.**"  
> — Ezorath Qu’rastis, Sorcerer of the Thousand Sons

---

## Choose Armies

When choosing an army for matched play:

- Your army must be **Battle-forged** (pg 240).
- The total **points value** cannot exceed the limit set for the game.

### Army Faction

All units, except **UNALIGNED** ones, must share at least one **Faction keyword** in common (e.g., **IMPERIUM**, **CHAOS**), even across different Detachments.

### Points Limit

- Agree on points limits with your opponent.
- Reference points values from codexes or Warhammer 40,000 publications for each model and weapon.
- The total points of all models and weapons in your army must not exceed the agreed limit.

### Reinforcement Points

- Sometimes special abilities allow adding or replacing units during battle, often summoning **DAEMON units**.
- You must set aside points as **reinforcement points** in your army roster.
- Each time a unit is added during battle, subtract its points from the reinforcement pool.
- If insufficient points remain, reduce the unit size or upgrades or decide not to use the unit.
- If you choose not to use the unit, the ability or psychic power still counts as used, even if no unit arrives.

### Army Roster

Record your army details on an **army roster**:

- List units and their upgrades.
- Identify the army’s **Warlord**.

### Organized Events

For tournaments or organized events, consider the following guidelines:

| Points Limit    | Number of Detachments | Battlefield Size | Game Length        |
|-----------------|-----------------------|------------------|--------------------|
| Up to 1,000     | Up to 2 per army      | 4' x 4'          | Up to 2 hours      |
| 1,001–2,000     | Up to 3 per army      | 6' x 4'          | 2 to 3 hours       |
| 2,001–3,000     | Up to 4 per army      | 8' x 4'          | 3 or more hours    |

These are guidelines and can be modified to suit your event’s needs.

---

## Choose Mission

The last step is to choose the mission for the game.

- Matched play uses missions.
- You can agree with your opponent on a mission set or roll to decide.
- There are six **Eternal War missions** and six **Maelstrom of War missions**, each with different tactical challenges.
- Select one mission or roll a dice to randomly determine the mission.

### Objective Markers

Many missions use **objective markers** representing sites of tactical or strategic importance.

- Represent by any appropriate marker, terrain piece, or spare model.
- Always measure distances to and from the **centre** of the marker.

### Sudden Death

A game does not generally finish before the agreed turn limit but may end early with a **sudden death victory** in these cases:

1. One player concedes, giving their opponent a **crushing victory** immediately.
2. At the end of any turn after the first battle round, if a player has **no models on the battlefield**, the game ends immediately with their opponent winning a crushing victory. 

> Note: Do not count Fortifications unless they have a unit embarked inside. Even the most formidable bastion requires a garrison to pose a threat.

## Eternal War Table

### D6 Mission
- **1 Retrieval Mission** (pg 218)  
- **2 No Mercy** (pg 219)  
- **3 The Scouring** (pg 220)  
- **4 Big Guns Never Tire** (pg 221)  
- **5 Secure and Control** (pg 222)  
- **6 The Relic** (pg 223)  

## Maelstrom of War Table

### D6 Mission
- **1 Cleanse and Capture** (pg 230)  
- **2 Contact Lost** (pg 231)  
- **3 Tactical Escalation** (pg 232)  
- **4 Spoils of War** (pg 233)  
- **5 Cloak and Shadows** (pg 234)  
- **6 Deadlock** (pg 235)  

## Matched Play Mission Rules

The following three special rules apply to all **matched play games**:

### Psychic Focus
With the exception of **Smite**, each **psychic power** can be attempted **only once per turn**, rather than once per psyker per turn.

### Strategic Discipline
The same **Stratagem** cannot be used by the same player more than once during any single phase. This does not affect Stratagems that are not used during a phase, such as those used ‘before the battle begins’ or ‘at the end of a battle round’.

### Tactical Reserves
- Many units have the ability to be set up on **teleportariums**, in high orbit, or in **Reserve**, to arrive mid-game as reinforcements.
- When setting up your army during Deployment for a matched play game, **at least half the total number of units in your army must be set up on the battlefield**, even if all units have an ability to be set up elsewhere.
- Any unit that has not arrived on the battlefield by the **end of the third battle round** counts as destroyed.

---

These six **standard deployment maps** are referenced in matched play missions. When playing, randomly select one map by rolling a D6. The mission states which player rolls; if not specified, the youngest player rolls.
