## Eternal War Missions

### Retrieval Mission

#### The Armies
Each player selects a **Battle-forged army** to an agreed points limit.

#### The Battlefield
- Create the battlefield and set up terrain.
- Players set up **4 objective markers**.
- Players roll off; the highest roller places the first objective marker.
- Players alternate placing objective markers until all 4 are placed.
- Objective markers must be more than **12" apart** and **6" from the battlefield edge**.

#### Deployment
- The player who placed the **fourth objective marker** selects a **standard deployment map** (pg 216).
- This player picks their deployment zone; the opponent uses the other.
- Players alternate deploying units, one at a time, starting with the player who did not pick their zone.
- Models must be set up within their own deployment zone.
- Continue until both armies are set up.

#### First Turn
- The player who finished deployment first chooses to take the **first or second turn**.
- If choosing the first turn, the opponent can roll a dice.
- On a **roll of 6**, the opponent seizes the initiative and takes the first turn instead.

#### Battle Length
- At the end of battle round 5, the first player rolls a D6; the game continues on a **3+**, otherwise ends.
- At the end of battle round 6, the second player rolls a D6; the game continues on a **4+**, otherwise ends.
- The battle ends automatically at the end of battle round 7.

#### Victory Conditions
The player with the most **victory points** wins. A draw occurs if points are tied.

- **Take and Hold**: Each objective marker is worth 3 victory points to the player controlling it. A player controls a marker if they have more models within **3" of the centre** than the opponent.
- **Slay the Warlord**: 1 victory point if the enemy Warlord is slain.
- **First Blood**: The first unit destroyed is worth 1 victory point to the opponent; if simultaneous destruction occurs, both players score 1 point.
- **Linebreaker**: 1 victory point if, at the end of battle, you have at least one model in the enemy deployment zone.

---

### No Mercy

#### The Armies
Each player selects a **Battle-forged army** to an agreed points limit.

#### The Battlefield
Create the battlefield and set up terrain.

#### Deployment
- Players roll off; the highest roller selects a standard deployment map (pg 216).
- That player picks their deployment zone; opponent takes the other.
- Players alternate deploying units, starting with the player who did not pick their zone.
- Models must be deployed within their deployment zones.
- Continue until both armies are set up.

#### First Turn
- The player who finishes deployment first chooses first or second turn.
- If first turn chosen, the opponent may roll a die.
- On a **roll of 6**, opponent seizes initiative and takes first turn.

#### Battle Length
- After battle round 5, player who had first turn rolls D6; continues on **3+**, else ends.
- After round 6, second player rolls D6; continues on **4+**, else ends.
- Battle ends automatically after round 7.

#### Victory Conditions
The player with the most **victory points** wins; ties result in a draw.

- **No Quarter Given**: 1 victory point for each enemy unit destroyed.
- **Slay the Warlord**: 1 point for killing enemy Warlord, in addition to points for destroyed units.
- **First Blood**: First unit destroyed scores 1 point for the opposing player; simultaneous destruction results in both scoring 1 point.
- **Linebreaker**: 1 point if at least one model is in the enemy deployment zone at game end.

---

### The Scouring

#### The Armies
Each player selects a **Battle-forged army** to an agreed points limit.

#### The Battlefield
- Create the battlefield and set up terrain.
- Players set up **6 objective markers**.
- Players roll off; highest roller places first objective.
- Players alternate placing markers until all 6 are placed.
- Objective markers must be more than **12" apart** and **6" from the battlefield edges**.

#### Deployment
- The player who placed the **sixth objective marker** selects a **standard deployment map** (pg 216).
- This player picks their deployment zone; the opponent uses the other.
- Players alternate deploying units one at a time, starting with the player who did not pick their zone.
- Models must be set up within their own deployment zone.
- After deployment, randomly select one objective marker as the **Superior objective marker**, and a different one as the **Inferior objective marker**.

#### First Turn
- The player who finishes deployment first chooses to take the first or second turn.
- If the first turn is chosen, opponent rolls a die.
- A **roll of 6** allows the opponent to seize initiative and take the first turn instead.

#### Battle Length
- At the end of battle round 5, first player rolls D6; the game continues on a **3+**, else ends.
- At the end of battle round 6, second player rolls D6; the game continues on a **4+**, else ends.
- The battle ends automatically after round 7.

#### Victory Conditions
The player with the most **victory points** wins; a draw occurs if tied.

- **Take and Hold**: Each objective marker is worth points to the player who controls it.
- A player controls an objective marker if they have more models within **3" of its centre** than their opponent.

## Victory Points and Objective Markers

- The **Superior objective marker** is worth **4 victory points**, whilst the **Inferior objective marker** is only worth **1 victory point**.
- All other objective markers are worth **2 victory points**.

### Slay the Warlord

- If the enemy **Warlord** has been slain during the battle, you score **1 victory point**.

### First Blood

- The first unit, of any kind, to be destroyed during the battle is worth **1 victory point** to the opposing player at the end of the game.
- If two or more units from opposing forces are destroyed simultaneously, then **both players** get **1 victory point**.

### Linebreaker

- If, at the end of the battle, you have at least one model within the enemy’s deployment zone, you score **1 victory point**.

---

## Battle Setup and Deployment

Both sides are sweeping through the area, tasking recon units to identify sites of strategic import. However, not all sites are of equal worth – victory will go to the player who can secure the most valuable sites and cripple the enemy’s ability to locate others.

> +++ THOUGH WE MAY KNOW THE BITTER TEARS OF DEFEAT, WE TRUST IN THE EMPEROR’S VICTORY. +++

Each player selects a **Battle-forged army** to an agreed points limit.

### The Battlefield

- Create the battlefield and set up terrain.
- Players roll off, and starting with the highest roller, alternate placing **4 objective markers**.
- Objective markers must be:
  - More than **12"** from the centre of any other marker.
  - More than **6"** from the edge of the battlefield.

### Deployment

- The player who placed the **fourth objective marker** determines the deployment map and picks a deployment zone.
- The opponent uses the other deployment zone.
- Players alternate deploying units, starting with the player who did **not** pick their zone.
- Models must be set up within their deployment zone.
- Continue until both sides have fully deployed.

### First Turn

- The player who finishes setting up first chooses first or second turn.
- If they choose first, their opponent rolls a die; a **6** means the opponent seizes initiative.

### Battle Length

- End of round 5: The first-turn player rolls a **D6**; a **3+** continues the game.
- End of round 6: The second-turn player rolls a **D6**; a **4+** continues the game.
- Battle ends automatically after round **7**.

---

## Victory Conditions

At the end of the game, the player with the most **victory points** wins. A tie results in a **draw**.

### Key Positions

- Each objective marker is worth **3 victory points** to the player controlling it.
- Control is defined as having more models within **3"** of the objective's centre.
- If only one player has models from a **Heavy Support unit** within **3"**, they control it regardless of enemy models.

### Destroy the Big Guns

- Each player scores **1 victory point** for each enemy **Heavy Support unit** completely destroyed.

### Slay the Warlord

- Scoring **1 victory point** if the enemy **Warlord** is slain.
- If the Warlord is **Heavy Support**, this is in addition to the **Destroy the Big Guns** point.

### First Blood

- First unit destroyed yields **1 victory point** to the opponent.
- Simultaneous destruction grants both players **1 victory point**.

### Linebreaker

- Having a model inside the enemy’s deployment zone at the end scores **1 victory point**.

---

## Big Guns Scenario

Both sides are attempting to secure key positions with overwhelming firepower to crush enemy heavy weaponry.

> +++ GUNS AND WARRIORS ARE USEFUL BUT IT IS OUR INDOMITABLE WILL THAT PROMISES THE ULTIMATE VICTORY. +++

---

## Secure and Control Scenario

Both sides attempt to capture and defend bases of operation or similarly vital objectives by splitting their armies into offensive and defensive forces.

> +++ SUCCESS IS MEASURED IN BLOOD; YOURS OR YOUR ENEMY’S. +++

### Deployment

- Players roll off to choose deployment map and zones.
- Starting with the chosen zone player, each sets up **1 objective marker** in their deployment zone.
- Objective markers must be at least **6"** away from battlefield edges.
- Players alternate deploying units starting with the player who set up their marker last.

### Victory Conditions

- **Take and Hold**: Each objective marker controlled at the end scores **3 victory points**.
- Control means having more models within **3"** of the centre than the opponent.
- **Slay the Warlord**: Score **1 victory point** if enemy Warlord slain.
- **First Blood** and **Linebreaker** as above.

---

## The Relic Scenario

Both sides attempt to recover a valuable relic from the front lines—an irreplaceable artefact vital to the war effort.

> +++ ALL HAIL THE MARTYRS! ON THEIR BLOOD IS OUR IMPERIUM FOUNDED, IN THEIR REMEMBRANCE DO WE HONOUR OURSELVES. +++

### Battlefield Setup

- Create battlefield and terrain.
- Place a single **objective marker** representing the **Relic** at the battlefield centre.

### Deployment

- Players roll off and choose deployment zones.
- Alternate deploying units starting with the player who did **not** pick their deployment zone.
- Models must be set up within their deployment zone.

### First Turn and Battle Length

- Same procedure as previous scenarios.

### Victory Conditions

- If a model is **carrying the Relic** at game end, that player wins a **major victory**.
- If no one carries the Relic, the player whose model is closest to it wins a **minor victory**.
- A tie if models are equally close.

### The Relic Rules

- An **INFANTRY model** can pick up the Relic by moving into contact with it.
- The Relic moves with the carrier.
- The carrier cannot:
  - Embark in a **TRANSPORT**.
  - Leave the battlefield.
  - Move more than **9"** per phase.
- Relic is dropped only if the carrier is slain or flees.

---

## Tactical Objectives Overview

War is unpredictable; priorities change rapidly. Effective commanders must adapt and exploit opportunities.

### Using Tactical Objectives

- Some missions, often **Maelstrom of War**, use **Tactical Objectives**.
- Place **6 numbered objective markers (1–6)** after terrain setup and before deployment.
- Players roll off; highest starts placing objective markers alternately.
- Markers must be spaced:
  - More than **12"** from each other.
  - More than **6"** from battlefield edge.

### Generating Tactical Objectives

- The mission will specify how many Tactical Objectives to generate at the start of each turn.

## Generating a Tactical Objective

To generate a **Tactical Objective**, roll two dice, one after the other:

- The first die represents **tens**
- The second die represents **digits**

This gives a result between **11 and 66**. Consult the Tactical Objectives list and write down the corresponding result.

Note that unless the mission states otherwise:

- Results are **not secret**
- Both players should be able to see what Tactical Objectives the other has

If you own a deck of **Tactical Objective cards**, you can instead generate your Tactical Objectives by:

- Shuffling the deck
- Drawing the top card

Cards drawn should be kept **face up** for opponent visibility, unless the mission instructs otherwise.

Note that while several Tactical Objectives share the same name, they are all **uniquely numbered**. If you roll the same number twice in a game, **roll again** until a different number is generated.

Tactical Objectives that have been generated are said to be **active** until they are either **achieved** or **discarded**.

---

## Stratagems

If the mission uses **Tactical Objectives**, a player can use **Command Points (CPs)** to activate the following bonus Stratagem:

### New Orders

- Use this Stratagem **after generating** your Tactical Objectives at the start of your turn.
- **Immediately discard** a Tactical Objective and generate a new one.

---

## Achieving Tactical Objectives

At the end of every turn (both yours and your enemy’s), check if you have **achieved** any of your active Tactical Objectives.

- The descriptions tell you **how and when** they are achieved and the number of **victory points** scored.
- If you can achieve a Tactical Objective at the end of a turn, you **must immediately score** the victory points.
- Players can achieve **any number** of their Tactical Objectives in the same turn.

Many Tactical Objectives require a player to **control an objective marker**.

- A player controls an objective marker if they have **more models within 3"** of its centre than their opponent.

---

## Discarding Tactical Objectives

Once a Tactical Objective has been **achieved**, it is **discarded**.

After discarding achieved Tactical Objectives:

- The player whose turn it is can **choose to discard** one of their remaining active Tactical Objectives (scoring no victory points).

Discarded Tactical Objectives:

- Cease being active
- Cannot be generated or achieved for the rest of the game

---

## Tactical Objectives List

### Capture and Control / Take and Hold

- Score **1 victory point** if you control the specified **objective marker** at the end of your turn.
- Objective markers: **1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6**

### Secure Objectives (11-26)

| Number | Objective                | Condition                                          |
|--------|-------------------------|---------------------------------------------------|
| 11-16 | Secure Objective 1      | Control objective marker 1 at end of your turn    |
| 21-26 | Secure Objectives 2-6   | Control objective markers 2 to 6 at end of your turn |

---

### Defend Objectives (31-36)

You are charged with **defence of a key objective**. It must not fall into enemy hands.

- Score **2 victory points** if you control the specified objective marker at the **end of two consecutive turns**.

Objective markers: **1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6**

---

### Advance Behind Enemy Lines (41)

- Score **1 victory point** if **no unit** from your army is within your **deployment zone** at the end of your turn.

---

### Hold the Line (42)

- When generated, roll a **D6**
- Score **1 victory point** if you control the corresponding objective marker.
- If you **capture it from your opponent** that turn, score **D3 victory points** instead.

---

### Supremacy (43)

- Score **1 victory point** if you have at least **one unit completely within** the enemy’s deployment zone at the end of your turn.
- Score **D3 victory points** if at least **three units** are completely within the enemy’s deployment zone.

---

### Domination (44)

- Score **D3 victory points** if you control **any three objective markers** at the end of your turn.

---

### Mission Critical Objective (45)

- Score **1 victory point** if you have at least **three units completely within** your deployment zone and your opponent has **no models** there at the end of your turn.
- This objective **cannot be achieved on your first turn**.

---

### Defend Objective 6 (46)

- Score **D3+3 victory points** if you control **every** objective marker on the battlefield at the end of your turn.

---

## Storm and Defend Tactical Objectives

| Number | Tactical Objective           | Description & Scoring                                                                                   |
|--------|-----------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 51     | Enemy Units Destroyed (Shooting)       | Score **1 victory point** if an enemy unit destroyed during your Shooting phase.<br>Score **D3 victory points** if 3 or more enemy units destroyed. |
| 52     | Kill the Enemy Warlord       | Score **D3 victory points** if your opponent's **Warlord** has been destroyed this or any previous turn. |
| 53     | Exterminate Enemy Units      | 1 victory point if an enemy unit destroyed during your turn.<br>D3 victory points if 3-5 units destroyed.<br>D3+3 if 6 or more units destroyed. |
| 54     | Assassinate Enemy Characters | 1 victory point if at least one enemy **CHARACTER** destroyed this turn.<br>D3 victory points if 3 or more CHARACTERS destroyed. |
| 55     | Eliminate Enemy Psykers      | 1 victory point if at least one enemy **PSYKER** destroyed this turn.                                  |
| 56     | Control Battlefield Centre   | 1 victory point if no enemy models within 6" of centre at turn end.<br>D3 victory points if none within 12".     |

---

## Additional Tactical Objectives

| Number | Tactical Objective                            | Description & Scoring                                                                              |
|--------|----------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 61     | Destroy Large Enemy Units                     | 1 victory point if enemy unit with **10+ Wounds** destroyed.<br>D3 victory points if unit with **20+ Wounds** destroyed. |
| 62     | Destroy Enemy Units in Fight Phase            | 1 victory point if an enemy unit destroyed during Fight phase.<br>D3 victory points if 3 or more destroyed. |
| 63     | Maintain Air Superiority                       | 1 victory point if at least one enemy unit that **can FLY** destroyed.                           |
| 64     | Break Enemy Morale                             | 1 victory point if opponent failed a **Morale test**.<br>D3 victory points if 3 or more failed.  |
| 65     | Mission of Utmost Importance                   | Immediately generate a **bonus Tactical Objective** that does not count towards active objectives.<br>Your **Warlord** must be the only unit used to achieve the bonus objective.<br>Score both the victory points from the bonus objective and **3 additional points**.<br>If discarded, the bonus objective is discarded as well. |

---

## Summary of Control Mechanics

- **Control an objective marker:** have more models within **3"** of its centre than your opponent.
- Objectives scored must be **immediately recorded** at the end of turns.
- Players may have more than one active Tactical Objective at a time.
- Discarding allows changing tactics but does not earn victory points.

---

## Key Terms

- **Tactical Objective:** Specific mission goals generated randomly or via cards.
- **Active Tactical Objective:** Currently in play and can be achieved or discarded.
- **Command Points (CP):** Resource spent to perform Stratagems like New Orders.
- **Victory Points:** Points gained for accomplishing Tactical Objectives.
- **Deployment Zone:** Area where units enter the battlefield.
- **Objective Marker:** A point on the battlefield to be controlled or defended.

---

## Important Notes

- Tactical Objective results and cards are **visible** to all players unless specifically stated.
- If the **same Tactical Objective number** is rolled twice in a game, the second roll must be re-rolled.
- Tactical Objectives are a vital part of mission success, offering **varied paths to victory**.



## Master the Warp

**Desperate times call for desperate measures** – harness the power of the **Warp** to defeat your foes. Score **1 victory point** if you manifested or denied a **psychic power** during this turn. If you manifested or denied **3 or more psychic powers**, score **D3 victory points** instead.

---

## Priority Orders

- **OVERWHELMING FIREPOWER**
- **BLOOD AND GUTS**
- **NO PRISONERS**
- **AREA DENIAL**
- **PSYCHOLOGICAL WARFARE**
- **MASTER THE WARP**
- **KINGSLAYER**
- **WITCH HUNTER**
- **SCOUR THE SKIES**
- **ASSASSINATE**
- **BIG GAME HUNTER**

---

## Purge and Annihilation

- **Purge**
- **Annihilation**

---

## Priority Orders Received

- **MAELSTROM OF WAR**
- **CLEANSE AND CAPTURE**

---

## Between the Stars

The evidence of **war** can be clearly seen all across the battlefield as the wounded cry for aid and vital resources are at risk of falling into **enemy hands**. Search for and recover these **artefacts** at all costs and eliminate any enemy forces that dare oppose you.

---

## The Armies

Each player selects a **Battle-forged army** to an agreed points limit.

---

## The Battlefield

Create the battlefield and set up **terrain**. Next, the players should place **6 objective markers**, as detailed on page 226.

---

## Deployment

- The player who placed the sixth objective marker determines which of the standard deployment maps is used in the battle (pg 216).  
- That player picks one of the deployment zones on the map for their army. Their opponent uses the other deployment zone.  
- Players alternate deploying their units, one at a time, starting with the player who did **not** pick their deployment zone.  
- A player’s models must be set up within their own deployment zone.  
- Continue setting up units until both sides have set up their army.

---

## First Turn

- The player who finished setting up their army first can choose to take the **first** or **second** turn.  
- If they decide to take the first turn, their opponent can roll a dice; on a roll of **6**, they seize the **initiative** and take the first turn instead.

---

## Tactical Objectives

This mission uses **Tactical Objectives**.  
- If, at the start of a player’s turn, they have fewer than **3 active Tactical Objectives**, they must generate Tactical Objectives until they have **3**.

---

## Battle Length

- At the end of battle round **5**, the player who had the first turn must roll a **D6**. On a roll of **3+**, the game continues; otherwise, the game ends.  
- At the end of battle round **6**, the player who had the second turn must roll a **D6**. This time, the game continues on a roll of **4+**; otherwise, the game ends.  
- The battle automatically ends at the end of battle round **7**.

---

## Victory Conditions

At the end of the game, the player who has scored the most **victory points** is the winner. If both players have the same number of victory points, the game is a **draw**.

In addition to achieving **Tactical Objectives**, victory points are earned through the following:

- **Slay the Warlord**: If the enemy **Warlord** has been slain during the battle, you score **1 victory point**.  
- **First Blood**: The first unit, of any kind, to be destroyed during the battle is worth **1 victory point** to the opposing player at the end of the game. If two or more units from opposing forces are destroyed simultaneously, both players get **1 victory point**.  
- **Linebreaker**: If, at the end of the battle, you have at least one model within the enemy’s deployment zone, you score **1 victory point**.

---

## Maelstrom of War: Contact Lost

All contact with command has been lost and the enemy are doubtless advancing towards your position. Secure sites of **tactical import** to re-establish communications with all due haste and engage any hostile forces encountered with **extreme prejudice**.

---

## Maelstrom of War Setup

- The **Armies**, **Battlefield**, **Deployment**, and **First Turn** setup are as described previously.

---

## Tactical Objectives (Maelstrom of War Variation)

- Each player generates **1 Tactical Objective** at the start of their first turn.  
- In subsequent turns, if a player has fewer than **6 active Tactical Objectives**, they must generate **1 Tactical Objective** for each objective marker they control (max 6 active Tactical Objectives).

---

## Stratagems

In this mission, players can use **Command Points (CPs)** to use the following Stratagem:

### Temporary Comms Uplink Stratagem

- If you have fewer than **6 active Tactical Objectives**, you can use this Stratagem to immediately generate **1 extra Tactical Objective**.  
- Cost: **3 CP**

---

## Maelstrom of War: Tactical Escalation

What began as a simple raid has escalated into full-blown battle, as both sides commit more forces to the fray. Every moment, more combatants engage and new mission-critical targets are identified.

---

## Tactical Priority

- At the start of the first battle round but before the first turn begins, each player nominates a single **Tactical Objective type** (e.g., Take and Hold).  
- You score an additional victory point for each Tactical Objective of that type you achieve.  
- However, you lose **1 victory point** each time you discard a Tactical Objective of that type.

---

## Tactical Objectives (Tactical Escalation Variation)

- At the start of a player’s turn, if they have fewer active Tactical Objectives than the current battle round number, they must generate Tactical Objectives until they have a number equal to the current battle round number.

---

## Precious Cargo

- Both players can achieve any active Tactical Objective titled “**Secure Objective X**,” where **X** is a number between **1 and 6**, regardless of who generated it.  
- These Tactical Objectives can only be discarded when **achieved**.

---

## Victory Conditions (Tactical Escalation Variation)

At the end of the game:

- The player who scored the most victory points is the **winner**; ties result in a **draw**.  
- **Mission Priorities**: If one player has achieved more Tactical Objectives of their nominated type than their opponent at game end, they receive **1 additional victory point**.  
- **Slay the Warlord**: Score **1 victory point** for slaying the enemy **Warlord**.  
- **First Blood**: The first unit destroyed grants **1 victory point** to the opposing player. If multiple units are destroyed simultaneously, both players get **1 victory point**.  
- **Linebreaker**: Score **1 victory point** if you have at least one model in the enemy’s deployment zone at game end.

---

## Inspirational Quotes

- “**Between the stars**... every voyage into the nothing is a confrontation with **horror**, with the implacable things of the **Warp**, and with man’s innermost **fear**.”  
- “It is better to **die for the Emperor than to live for yourself**.”  
- “In an hour of darkness, a blind man is the best guide. In an age of insanity look to the madman to show the way.”  
- “The reward for treachery is **retribution.**”  
- “Facts are chains that bind perception and fetter truth. For a man can remake the world if he has a dread and no facts to cloud his mind.”  
- “Know the **mutant**; kill the mutant!”

## Battle Length

At the end of **battle round 5**, the player who had the **first turn** must roll a **D6**. On a roll of **3+**, the game continues; otherwise, the game is over. At the end of **battle round 6**, the player who had the **second turn** must roll a **D6**. This time the game continues on a roll of **4+**, otherwise the game is over. The battle automatically ends at the end of **battle round 7**.

## Victory Conditions

At the end of the game, the player who has scored the most **victory points** is the winner. If both players have the same number of victory points, the game is a **draw**.

In addition to achieving **Tactical Objectives**, victory points are achieved for the following:

- **Steal the Loot**: If, at the end of the game, one player has achieved more ‘Secure Objective X’ Tactical Objectives (see *Precious Cargo* above) than their opponent, that player receives **1 additional victory point**.  
- **Slay the Warlord**: If the enemy **Warlord** has been slain during the battle, you score **1 victory point**.  
- **First Blood**: The first unit, of any kind, to be destroyed during the battle is worth **1 victory point** to the opposing player at the end of the game. If two or more units from opposing forces are destroyed simultaneously, both players get **1 victory point**.  
- **Linebreaker**: If, at the end of the battle, you have at least one model within the enemy’s deployment zone, you score **1 victory point**.  

---

## Maelstrom of War

### Spoils of War

A **vital resupply convoy** has been intercepted and its cargo lost in no man’s land. You must reclaim these spoils of war before the enemy can reach them, while inflicting as much damage as possible.

> +++ **WE DO NOT HATE THE ALIEN BECAUSE HE IS DIFFERENT, WE HATE THE ALIEN BECAUSE HE HAS NAUGHT BUT HATE IN HIS HEART FOR US.** +++

---

### The Armies

- Each player selects a **Battle-forged army** to an agreed points limit.

### The Battlefield

- Create the battlefield and set up terrain.
- Players place **6 objective markers** as detailed on page 226.

### Deployment

- The player who placed the sixth objective marker determines which of the **standard deployment maps** is used (pg 216) and picks a deployment zone for their army.
- The opponent uses the other deployment zone.
- Players alternate deploying units, starting with the player who did **not** pick their deployment zone.
- A player’s models must be set up within their own deployment zone.
- Continue until both sides have set up their armies.

### First Turn

- The player who finished setting up first chooses to take the **first or second turn**.
- If they choose the first turn, their opponent can roll a dice; on a roll of **6**, the opponent seizes the initiative and takes the first turn instead.

### Tactical Objectives

- This mission uses **Tactical Objectives**.
- If, at the start of a player’s turn, they have fewer than **3 active Tactical Objectives**, they must generate more until they have 3.

### Secret Orders

- Players keep their Tactical Objectives **secret**.
- Only reveal Tactical Objectives when achieving them.

### Cover of Darkness

- When rolling to hit in the Shooting phase, subtract **1** from the roll if the target is more than **18"** away.

---

## Maelstrom of War: Cloak and Shadows

Enemy patrols operate in this area, searching for critical objectives. Scout under the **cover of darkness** to discover their plans but avoid revealing your own goals. Achieving the enemy’s objectives while securing yours will assure victory.

> **IF YOU CANNOT SPEAK WELL OF YOUR MASTER, BE SILENT!**

### Stratagems

- Players can use **Command Points (CPs)** to use the additional Stratagem below:

#### Flares  
- Select an enemy unit. For the duration of your turn, your units can shoot at that unit without penalty from **Cover of Darkness**.  
- Cost: **1 CP**

---

## Battle Length (Repeated)

- At the end of **battle round 5**, the player with the first turn rolls a **D6**; on **3+**, the game continues, else the game ends.
- At the end of **battle round 6**, the player with second turn rolls a **D6**; on **4+**, the game continues, else the game ends.
- The battle ends automatically at the end of **battle round 7**.

---

## Victory Conditions (Repeated)

In addition to Tactical Objectives:

- **Slay the Warlord**: Score **1 victory point** for slaying the enemy Warlord.  
- **First Blood**: The first unit destroyed scores **1 victory point** for the opposite player. Simultaneous destruction grants **1 victory point** to both players.  
- **Linebreaker**: Control of the enemy deployment zone scores **1 victory point**.

---

## The Armies (Repeated)

- Each player selects a **Battle-forged army** to an agreed points limit.

## The Battlefield (Repeated)

- Create the battlefield and set up terrain.
- Place **6 objective markers** (page 226).

## Deployment (Repeated)

- The sixth objective marker placer chooses deployment map(pg 216) and their deployment zone. The opponent uses the other zone.
- Players alternate deployment starting with the player who did not pick deployment zone.
- Models set up within their deployment zone until both armies are ready.

## First Turn (Repeated)

- First to finish can take first or second turn.
- Opponent rolls a dice; on **6** they seize first turn.

## Tactical Objectives (Expanded)

- Players generate **6 Tactical Objectives** at start of their first turn.
- In the **second battle round**, players can have **5 active Tactical Objectives**, in the third, **4**, and so on.
- If a player has too many active Tactical Objectives at the start of their turn, they must discard until correct.
- If fewer, generate Tactical Objectives until correct number is met.

## Battle Length (Expanded)

- At the end of **battle round 5**, player with first turn rolls **D6**; on **3+**, continue, else ends.
- At end of **battle round 6**, player with second turn rolls **D6**; on **4+**, continue, else ends.
- Battle ends automatically after **battle round 7**.

## Strategic Deadlock

- From the start of **battle round 3**, the **Command Point cost** of all Stratagems is **doubled**.

---

## Victory Conditions (Expanded)

- As above, in addition to Tactical Objectives:  
  - **Slay the Warlord** scores **1 victory point**.
  - **First Blood** scores **1 victory point**.
  - **Linebreaker** scores **1 victory point**.

---

## Maelstrom of War: Deadlock

Months of bitter fighting ended in deadlock, but a fleeting opportunity arises to strike a devastating blow. Strike hard and fast; with every moment you delay, your tactical options dwindle and victory slips away.

> **DO NOT QUESTION THE WILL OF THE EMPEROR!**

> +++ **TO A SPACE MARINE, THE BOLTGUN IS FAR MORE THAN A WEAPON—IT IS AN INSTRUMENT OF MANKIND’S DIVINITY, THE BRINGER OF DEATH TO HIS FOES, WHOSE HOWLING BLAST IS A PRAYER TO THE GODS OF BATTLE.** +++

---

## Advanced Rules

> “**Warriors of Ultramar. This is where we make our stand. If death is to be our fate, then we shall meet it with the Emperor’s word on our lips and his light in our eyes. If we must die, we will die; but we shall never yield.**”  
> — **Marneus Calgar, Lord of Macragge**

### Introduction

By now, you’ve scratched the surface of many ways to enjoy the **Warhammer 40,000** hobby. The missions seen so far are just the beginning — there are always new ways to play and new battles to fight!

### Battle-Forged Armies

- These armies reflect the **Factions of Warhammer 40,000** as they would be deployed.
- Restrictions exist on army formation, but in exchange, you gain powerful benefits.

### Battlefield Terrain

- Terrain rules describe many features such as **twisted woods**, **shattered ruins**, **barricades**, and **statues**.
- These features bring the battlefield to life and add a tactical dimension to games.

### The Battlezones

- Battlezones introduce **environmental effects** such as **radioactive dust storms**, **perpetual darkness**, or warp-saturation.
- Rules and Stratagems reflect specific battlezones and times.
- They affect both players equally and add new tactical challenges.

### Expansions

- **Warhammer 40,000 expansions** provide new ways to use your collections and tailor tactics for diverse theatres of war.
- Options range from massive battles with vast armies, squad-focused urban fights, to orbital assaults.
- Four expansions are introduced:
  - **Planetstrike**
  - **Stronghold Assault**
  - **Cities of Death**
  - **Death from the Skies**

- Each modifies core rules to reflect specific warfare styles.
- Expansions offer new tactical challenges and better reflect the background events.
- Suitable for all play styles and skill levels.

## PLANETSTRIKE

**Planetstrike** is about **planetary invasion**:

- **Orbital bombardments** rain down, hammering defenders as attackers deploy troops by **dropship** and **teleport strike**.
- Defenders use mighty weapons from fortifications and ready elite troops to repel invaders.
- The first blows can decide the fate of a world; **no quarter will be asked or given**.

The introduction to **Planetstrike** provides rules to represent battle conditions and includes a Planetstrike mission, **‘Planetfall’**, to experience planetary invasion immediately.

> “When the people forget their duty, they are no longer human and become something less than beasts. They have no place in the bosom of Humanity nor in the heart of the Emperor. Let them die and be forgotten.”  
> — *Prime Edicts of the Holy Synod of the Adeptus Ministorum*  

> “Strive, my brothers, to cage the beast within, for its crimson thirst shall make monsters of us all. Yet know that, should ever the beast break free, the shame of that moment can only be salved through the unmitigated slaughter of the foe.”  
> — *Veteran Sergeant Gabrian, Blood Angels 6th Company*

---

## CITIES OF DEATH

**Vicious urban combat** is best recreated using the **Cities of Death** expansion:

- Battles are fought through war-torn streets instead of open plains.
- Combat is bitter and short-ranged, with booby traps and snipers.
- Ruined buildings may contain valuable caches or medical supplies.
- Both sides seek high ground to command the battlefield.

The section overview includes rules for claustrophobic battles and a **Cities of Death** mission, **‘Firesweep’**, to conduct urban warfare.

---

## STRONGHOLD ASSAULT

**Stronghold Assault** focuses on **siege warfare**—some of the most intense attacker vs. defender battles:

- Combat occurs in blood-soaked trenches or against fortress walls bristling with automated weapons.
- The introduction includes rules for fortifications.
- The **‘Bunker Assault’** mission tests siege tactics for both warlords.

---

## DEATH FROM THE SKIES

**Aerial combat** between deadly aircraft squadrons is the heart of the **Death from the Skies** expansion:

- Bombers devastate undefended ground units.
- Agile fighter craft scramble to intercept bombers.
- Dogfights above the battlefield can decide the war’s outcome.
- Controlling the skies is crucial for ground victory.

The introduction includes rules for a **Dogfight phase** and the **‘Tactical Strike’** mission to earn your wings.

---

## MULTIPLAYER BATTLES

Multiplayer battles complicate warfare with **multiple warring parties**:

- Temporary alliances form and quickly break.
- The battlefield center becomes a deadly killing ground.
- Awareness and initiative are crucial; a glory-hungry warlord may quickly find the tables turned.

This section presents a multiplayer mission, **‘Carnage’**, and includes rules for fighting chaotic multiplayer battles.

---

## CAMPAIGNS

Most wars extend beyond a single battle into **brutal campaigns**:

- Campaigns are a series of linked battles with recurring clashes.
- They allow players to create heroes and legends.
- Victory and defeat impact not just battles, but the broader war.

Campaigns can be created from any mission in this book, other Warhammer 40,000 publications, or custom scenarios.

This section introduces campaign principles and suggests how to play **tree**, **matrix**, and **map campaigns** with examples.

---

## AND MUCH MORE...

- This section offers numerous missions and extra rules.
- New rules, missions, and expansions are regularly released on **games-workshop.com**.
- Players are encouraged to write and fight their own missions for greater rewards in their hobby.

---

## BATTLE-FORGED ARMIES

All armies, from the **T’au** to the **Orks**, are organized forces called **Detachments**:

- A **Detachment** is a group of units that fight together and gain strategic or tactical bonuses.
- When a mission requires a **Battle-forged** army, all units must be organized into Detachments.
- Armies can include any number of Detachments mixed freely.
- Several universal Detachments are listed on pages 243-245 and in other sources.

### Organizing Detachments

- Units must fit restrictions and limitations detailed for each Detachment.
- A unit cannot belong to more than one Detachment.
- Use information such as **Faction** and **Battlefield Role** from unit datasheets to determine placement.

### Detachment Information May Include:

- **Battlefield Role Slots**: Number of units of each role required or optional.
- **Dedicated Transports**: Number of transport units allowed.
- **Restrictions**: Limits on unit types or Factions.
- **Command Benefits**: Bonuses granted by including the Detachment.

---

## FACTIONS

- Every unit belongs to one or more **Factions** that fight for control across the galaxy.
- A unit’s Faction is listed in the **keywords** section of its datasheet.
- Some Detachments require all units to be from the same Faction.
  
For example, a **Space Marine Captain** has the **IMPERIUM** and **ADEPTUS ASTARTES** keywords, meaning it belongs to both Factions. A Detachment requiring units from the same Faction must include only units from the Imperium or Adeptus Astartes.

---

## BATTLEFIELD ROLES

Units have a **Battlefield Role**, shown as a symbol:

- **HQ**
- **Fast Attack**
- **Flyer**
- **Troops**
- **Heavy Support**
- **Fortification**
- **Elites**
- **Dedicated Transport**
- **Lord of War**

Battlefield Roles indicate a unit’s typical duties and affect Detachment composition.

---

## BATTLEFIELD ROLE SLOTS

- Detachments specify how many units of each Battlefield Role must or may be included.
- Slots are icons indicating these minimum or maximum amounts.
- **Red icons** are **compulsory** selections.
- **Grey icons** are optional selections.

Example: The **Battalion Detachment** requires at least three **Troops** units and allows up to six Troops units.

Some slots may accept multiple Battlefield Roles or specific units only.

---

## UNDERSTRENGTH UNITS

- Units have a minimum number of models.
- When lacking enough models, you may field an **understrength** unit with fewer models.
- Must pay full points cost as if at minimum size.
- Understrength units count normally within Detachment slots.

---

## RESTRICTIONS

- Detachments list restrictions on units included.
- Units violating these cannot be part of that Detachment.
- The most common restriction: all units must be from the same Faction.

---

## COMMAND BENEFITS

- Detachments often grant **bonuses** when included in an army.
- Common benefit: increased **Command Points** available for Stratagems.

---

## COMMAND POINTS

- **Battle-forged armies** start with 3 Command Points.
- More Detachments usually increase total Command Points.
- Command Points are spent to use **Stratagems**—strategic or tactical assets during battle.
- Each Stratagem costs a certain number of Command Points.
- Insufficient Command Points means a Stratagem cannot be used.
- Stratagems can usually be used multiple times unless stated.

---

## STRATAGEMS

Players with Battle-forged armies may spend Command Points to use these basic Stratagems in any mission:

### COMMAND RE-ROLL STRATAGEM

- Allows the player to **re-roll any single dice** during the game.

## Counter-Offensive Stratagem

This **Stratagem** is used right after an **enemy unit** that charged has fought. Select one of your own eligible units and fight with it next.

---

## Insane Bravery Stratagem

You can automatically pass a single **Morale test** (this **Stratagem** must be used before taking the test).

Cost:  
- 1 CP  
- 2 CP  
- 2 CP

---

## Detachment Restrictions and Command Benefits

### Brigade Detachment  
- **Restrictions**: All units must be from the same **Faction**.  
- **Command Benefits**: +3 **Command Points** (CP).  
- **Dedicated Transports**: May include 1 for each other choice.  
- Composition:  
  - HQ: 2-3  
  - Troops: 3-6  
  - Flyers: 0-2  
  - Elites: 0-6  
  - Fast Attack: 0-3  
  - Heavy Support: 0-3  

### Patrol Detachment  
- **Restrictions**: All units must be from the same **Faction**.  
- **Command Benefits**: +1 CP.  
- **Dedicated Transports**: May include 1 for each other choice.  
- Composition:  
  - HQ: 1-2  
  - Troops: 1-3  
  - Elites: 0-2  
  - Fast Attack: 0-2  
  - Heavy Support: 0-2  
  - Flyers: 0-2  

### Battalion Detachment  
- **Restrictions**: All units must be from the same **Faction**.  
- **Command Benefits**: +9 CP.  
- **Dedicated Transports**: May include 1 for each other choice.  
- Composition:  
  - HQ: 3-5  
  - Troops: 6-12  
  - Elites: 3-8  
  - Fast Attack: 3-5  
  - Heavy Support: 3-5  
  - Flyers: 0-2  

### Vanguard Detachment  
- **Restrictions**: All units must be from the same **Faction**.  
- **Command Benefits**: +1 CP.  
- **Dedicated Transports**: May include 1 for each other choice.  
- Composition:  
  - HQ: 1-2  
  - Troops: 0-3  
  - Elites: 0-2  
  - Fast Attack: 0-2  
  - Heavy Support: 3-6  
  - Flyers: 0-2  

### Spearhead Detachment  
- **Restrictions**: All units must be from the same **Faction**.  
- **Command Benefits**: +1 CP.  
- **Dedicated Transports**: May include 1 for each other choice.  
- Composition:  
  - HQ: 1-2  
  - Troops: 0-3  
  - Elites: 3-6  
  - Fast Attack: 0-2  
  - Heavy Support: 0-2  
  - Flyers: 0-2  

### Outrider Detachment  
- **Restrictions**: All units must be from the same **Faction**.  
- **Command Benefits**: +1 CP.  
- **Dedicated Transports**: May include 1 for each other choice.  
- Composition:  
  - HQ: 1-2  
  - Troops: 0-3  
  - Elites: 0-2  
  - Fast Attack: 3-6  
  - Heavy Support: 0-2  
  - Flyers: 0-2  

---

## Other Detachments

### Auxiliary Support Detachment  
- **Restrictions**: All units must be from the same **Faction**.  
- **Command Benefits**: +3 CP.  

### Fortification Network  
- **Restrictions**: All units must be from the same **Faction**.  
- **Command Benefits**: +1 CP.  
- Includes 1-3 **Fortifications**.

### Auxiliary Detachment  
- **Restrictions**: None.  
- **Command Benefits**: None.  
- Includes 1 **Lord of War**.

### Super-Heavy Detachment  
- **Restrictions**: None.  
- **Command Benefits**: None.  
- Includes 1 **Lord of War**.

### Air Wing Detachment  
- **Restrictions**: None.  
- **Command Benefits**: None.  
- Includes 3-5 **Flyers**.

### Supreme Command Detachment  
- **Restrictions**: All units must be from the same **Faction**.  
- **Command Benefits**: +1 CP.  
- Composition:  
  - HQ: 3-5  
  - Elites: 0-1  
  - Lord of War: 0-1  

> Note: Unlike other Detachments, you lose 1 **Command Point** for each **Auxiliary Support Detachment** in your army. These are deducted from your total after adding up the bonuses from all other sources.

---

## The Battlefield and Terrain

### The Imperium vs. Hive Fleet Leviathan

Hissing and roaring, the living tide of **Hive Fleet Leviathan** surges across war-torn battlefields of **Praxis II**. Against this alien horror stands the mighty **Astra Militarum**, its battle tanks rising like mobile fortresses from the steely eyed Imperial ranks.

---

### Battlefield Terrain

Expanded terrain rules add a new dimension to your battlefield and help bring it to life. They are optional but provide more tactical depth beyond the basic **cover rules** in the core rules.

---

### Woods

- Twisted woodlands grow on many corpse-strewn battlefields.  
- **Infantry units** entirely on the base of a wood receive the **benefit of cover**.  
- If wood is not on a base, discuss boundaries with your opponent before the battle.  
- Other units gain cover if at least 50% of every model is obscured from the shooting unit's point of view.  
- Models charging through woods are **slowed**: subtract 2" from the unit's charge distance if any models move across a wood’s base.

---

### Ruins

- The galaxy is littered with remains of once-proud cities.  
- **Flyers, Vehicles, Monsters, and Bikes** can only end their move on the ground floor unless they can FLY.  
- **Infantry** can scale walls and traverse through windows, doors, and portals.  
- Infantry units on ruins gain cover, and other units only if 50% of models are obscured.  

---

### Barricades

- Makeshift barricades provide excellent defensive positions.  
- Infantry units within 1" of a barricade and behind it gain cover.  
- Units can fight across barricades up to 2" apart, rather than the normal 1".

---

### Craters

- Many worlds bear scars of heavy bombardment.  
- Infantry units completely within a crater gain cover.  
- Units charging across a crater are slowed: subtract 2" from charge distance.

---

### Obstacles

- Two types: **tank traps** (obstacle to Vehicles and Monsters) and **tanglewire** (obstacle to other units).  
- Units advancing or charging over obstacles have their movement halved (rounding up).  
- **Titanic models** are not slowed by obstacles.

---

### Imperial Statuary

- Heroes of the Imperium immortalised in stone.  
- Units within 3" and at least 25% obscured by statuary gain cover.  
- **Imperium units** within 3" add +1 to their **Leadership**.

---

### Fuel Pipes

- Armoured pipes carrying explosive fuels across many worlds.  
- Follow barricade rules with an additional hazard:  
  - On a saving throw of 7+ for a model within 1" of fuel pipes in the Shooting phase, roll a dice.  
  - On a roll of 1, the pipe is ruptured causing a **mortal wound** to the model’s unit.

---

### Battlescape

- Includes smoking tank hulls and blasted tree remains, hinting at mines or traps.  
- Follow rules for woods with a hazard:  
  - On a model advancing or charging across battlescape, roll a dice.  
  - On a roll of 1, the unit takes a **mortal wound** from triggered mines.  
- Models that can FLY only trigger mines if they charge across battlescape.

---

### Scratch-Built Terrain

- Terrain created from scratch by hobbyists.  
- Players need to devise their own rules for such terrain features.  
- Examples include ruins, rivers (lava or acid), or impassable rock formations.  
- Promotes creativity and unique battlefield experiences.

---

### Hills

- Hills and elevated positions offer commanding views and fields of fire.  
- Hills are part of the battlefield, not terrain features, so models on hills do **not** get cover benefits.  
- Large hills may block visibility.

---

## Battlezones

The galaxy is ablaze with war across millions of planets of varied environments. Battlezones can be used with mutual agreement to recreate diverse battlefield conditions.

---

### Battlezone: Night Fight

- Represents battles in low or zero visibility due to darkness, ash storms, celestial phenomena, or psychic obfuscation.  
- **Low Visibility**: Apply shooting penalties based on the target’s distance. Use the lesser penalty if distances are exact multiples (12", 24", 36").  
- **Fog of War**: Units arriving after the battle starts (e.g., via Reserves) must roll a die on arrival. On 1 or 2, arrival is delayed by one turn.  

---

### Stratagems in Night Fight Battlezone

- Both players may use Command Points for available **Stratagems**.  

---

## Stratagem - Light ’Em Up

Select an enemy unit.

## Turn Shooting and Distance Penalties

For the duration of your turn, your units can **shoot at that unit without penalties from Low Visibility**.  

### Distance Penalty
- **0-12"**: No penalty  
- **12-24"**: Hit rolls have a **-1 penalty**  
- **24-36"**: Hit rolls have a **-2 penalty**  
- **36"+**: Hit rolls have a **-3 penalty**  

### D6 Result Effects for Objective Markers
1. **Sabotaged!**: The unit that identified this objective marker takes **D3 mortal wounds**.  
2. **Nothing of Note**: This has no additional effect.  
3. **Grav-wave Generator**: If you control this objective marker, any unit attempting to charge a friendly unit within **3"** of this objective subtracts **2** from its charge move.  
4. **Targeting Relay**: If you control this objective marker, friendly units within **3"** re-roll hit rolls of **1** when shooting.  
5. **Scatterfield**: If you control this objective marker, friendly units within **3"** re-roll saving throw rolls of **1**.  
6. **Fire Support**: If you control this objective marker, roll a dice at the end of your Shooting phase. On a roll of **5+**, choose an enemy unit within **36"**. That unit suffers **D3 mortal wounds**.

---

## Battlezone: Fire and Fury

The armies clash under a burning sky – a **cataclysmic battle in orbit** causes casualties to descend in burning fragments, bombarding armies on cracked earth. It is **insanity to fight in these conditions**, but you must persevere.

### Burning Skies
- Units that can **FLY** must roll a dice each time they move in the Movement phase (roll after completing their move).  
- On a roll of **1**, they suffer **D3 mortal wounds**.

### The Earth Cracks
- All **Move characteristics are halved** for units that begin their turn entirely within a terrain feature.  
- A unit that charges through such terrain must roll a dice; on a roll of **1**, it suffers **D3 mortal wounds**.  
- Units that can **FLY** are not affected.

### Meteoric Debris
- In each Shooting phase, place three dice numbered **1, 2, and 3** anywhere on the battlefield at least **12" apart**.  
- Roll another dice; if the number matches one of the placed dice, a flaming chunk crashes at that location, and every unit within **6"** suffers **D3 mortal wounds**.  
- If no match, debris lands elsewhere.

---

## Warlord Trait

Your Warlord can choose the following trait instead of any other:

- **Insane Bravado**: This Warlord and friendly units within **8"** do **not** have to take Morale tests.

---

## Stratagems in Fire and Fury

Both players can spend **Command Points (CPs)** to use the following stratagem.

---

## Battlezone: Psychic Maelstrom

On many worlds, uncontrolled **psykers** become conduits for warp energies, infesting their planets with daemonic corruption and amplifying psychic powers.

### D6 Result Effects on Psykers
1. **A Fate Worse Than Death**: Psyker suffers **6 mortal wounds**. If slain, opponent places a **Chaos Spawn** model where the psyker stood or as close as possible.  
2. **Overload**: Psyker suffers **D3 mortal wounds**. If slain, all units within **6"** suffer **D3 mortal wounds**.  
3. **A Door Closes**: Psyker immediately forgets the psychic power they were manifesting and cannot manifest it for the rest of the battle.  
4. **Timeslip**: Psyker may immediately attempt to manifest an **extra psychic power** in this phase (even one already manifested).  
5. **Possession**: Roll **2D6**; if total > psyker’s Leadership, they become possessed and controlled by your opponent for the rest of the battle.  
6. **Transformation**: Until the next Psychic phase, the psyker has a **Strength of 10** and an **invulnerable save of 2+**.

---

## Orbital Bombardment Stratagem

- In your Shooting phase, place **six dice** for Meteoric Debris numbered **1 to 6**, instead of 3.  
- The Warp Overflows: Psykers add **2** to their Psychic and Deny the Witch tests.  
- Psychic Amplification: Psykers can manifest **one extra psychic power** per psychic phase, and all psychic power ranges are **doubled**.  
- Mortal Peril: Rolling any double on a Psychic test causes the psyker to suffer the **Terrors of the Warp**, resolved via a specific table rather than standard Perils of the Warp.

---

## Planetstrike Overview

**Planetstrike** is an expansion for devastating planetary assaults involving two players: 

- The **Attacker** tries to wrest control of a planet.  
- The **Defender** fights to hold it.

Planetary invasions are swift and terrible, with deafening noise, explosions, and death. Warriors plunge from drop-craft amid fire and vapour trails.  

### Description of the Battlefield
- **Noise**, **explosions**, and the **stench of death** fill the air.  
- Aircraft swoop through lasers and rockets.  
- Pillars of ghostly light scan skies, lethal to any invader caught in beams.  
- Anti-aircraft batteries rain red-hot debris.  
- Gigantic landers impact, releasing more warriors into the brutal battle.  
- The landscape is chewed by bombardments, dotted with ruined buildings and strongholds.  

### The Defender’s Garrison
- Bastions and heavy emplacements bristle with firepower to cut down invaders.

### The Attacker’s Role
- Sends deadly firestorms from orbit before ground forces drop in the fighting heart.

---

## Planetary Assault Roles

Planetstrike involves fighting on all fronts, where the enemy can attack at any time or place, including from above.

- **Defender**: Sets up strong fortifications and repels invaders.  
- **Attacker**: Launches hellfire and sends best troops to seize strongholds.

Actions determine the fate of the planet.

---

## Planetstrike Additional Rules

### Firestorm Attack
- The **Attacker** makes Firestorm Attacks at the start of the first battle round, before the first turn.  
- The attacker places **six dice numbered 1 to 6** at least **9" apart**.  
- For each Firestorm Attack, roll one dice: units within **3"** of the location suffer **D6 mortal wounds**.  
- **Infantry units** can choose to **go to ground** before damage is rolled, suffering only **D3 mortal wounds** but cannot act in their first turn.

---

## Planetary Assault Setup

- The Attacker’s units start in **Reserve** and are not placed on the battlefield during deployment.  
- **Infantry and FLY units** start **in orbit**.  
- Other units begin in a **landing zone** off one battlefield edge.  
- Roll a dice at the end of each Movement phase (called a Reserve roll). On a **3+**, the unit arrives from Reserve.  
- If embarked in a **TRANSPORT**, they arrive with the transport.  
- Units from orbit deploy anywhere on the battlefield more than **6"** from enemy models.  
- Units from a landing zone deploy within **6"** of the chosen landing zone edge.

---

## Planetstrike Defences

### Bastions
- Shelter Defender forces against invasions.  
- Cannot move or fight. Enemy models automatically hit Bastions in fights (no hit rolls).  
- Stats: **Toughness 10**, **Save 3+**, **20 Wounds**.  
- Equipped with four **heavy bolters** (Ballistic Skill 5+).  

### Garrisoning Bastions
- Defender’s **INFANTRY units** can garrison Bastions (up to 20 models).  
- Garrisoning units cannot typically act or be affected but can **shoot in the Shooting phase**.  
- If destroyed, units must disembark.  
- For each model disembarked, roll a dice; on **1, 2, or 3**, a model is crushed by rubble and slain (Defender’s choice).

---

## Planetstrike Stratagems

### Attacker Stratagems
- **Scorched Skies**: Used before Firestorm Attacks; make **D3 additional Firestorm Attacks**.  
- **Rapid Drop Assault**: Used before Reserve rolls start of first turn; **D3 units automatically arrive** from Reserve.

### Defender Stratagems
- **Targeting Jammers**: Used before Firestorm Attacks; move one Firestorm location dice up to **2D6"** in any direction.  
- **Fortified Stronghold**: Used before Firestorm Attacks; select one Bastion to have **25 Wounds** instead of 20.

## Defence Emplacements

**Defence Emplacements** are used to shoot down invading forces. They **cannot move** for any reason, nor can they fight. Enemy models **automatically hit** them in a fight – do not make hit rolls.

Each Defence Emplacement has:
- **Toughness** of 7
- **Save** of 4+
- **3 Wounds**
- Is removed once it loses all of its wounds
- **Ballistic Skill** of 5+

They are armed with either an **Icarus lascannon** or a **quad-gun** (see weapon profiles below).

Add **1** to hit rolls when shooting these weapons at:
- A unit that can **FLY**
- A unit that arrived from orbit during the Attacker’s previous turn

Subtract **1** when shooting at any other target.

### Weapon Profiles

| Weapon          | Range  | Type   | Shots | Strength | AP  | Damage |
|-----------------|---------|--------|-------|----------|-----|--------|
| Heavy bolter    | 36"     | Heavy  | 3     | 5        | -1  | D6     |
| Quad-gun       | 48"     | Heavy  | 8     | 7        | -1  | 1      |
| Icarus lascannon| 96"     | Heavy  | 1     | 9        | -3  | 1      |

---

## Planetstrike

Invading forces orbit above, raining fire upon the foe, their landing parties inbound to take for themselves any fortresses still standing. The defender must weather the storm and repel the enemy, no matter the cost. The attacker must not rest until the world is theirs.

The battlefield shown here is an example of a classic setup for a game of **Planetstrike**. The Defender has chosen to place his **Fortifications** in the centre of the battlefield so they are ready regardless of the Attacker’s approach.

### The Armies

- Players choose who is the **Attacker** and who is the **Defender**.
- Each selects a **Battle-forged army**.
- The **Power Level** of the Attacker’s army should be greater than the Defender’s.

### The Battlefield

- The **Defender** creates the battlefield.
- Sets up any number of Fortifications (**Bastions, Defence Emplacements, etc.**).
- Places all other terrain as desired.
- The **Attacker** chooses one battlefield edge as their **landing zone**, where non-orbital Reserves arrive.
- The Defender places **6 objective markers**:
  - One may be inside each Bastion.
  - Others must be placed so the centre of each is more than 6" away from other markers, Bastions, or battlefield edges.
- If a Bastion containing an objective marker is destroyed, the Defender must place the marker where the building used to be.

### Deployment

- The Defender sets up all of their units anywhere on the battlefield.
- The Attacker’s units start off the battlefield and arrive using **Planetary Assault** rules (pg 256).

### Firestorm Attack

- The Attacker rolls a **D3**, adds 1 for each Bastion on the battlefield.
- This total is the number of **Firestorm Attacks** made.

### First Turn

- The **Attacker** has the first turn.

### Battle Length

- The game lasts for **6 battle rounds**.

### Victory Conditions

The player with the most **victory points** at the end wins. If tied, the game is a draw.

Victory points are scored as follows:

- **Storm and Defend:** Each objective marker controlled at game end is worth **3 victory points**.
  - A player controls a marker if they have more models within 3" of its centre than the opponent.
  - If within a Bastion, count all models within 3" of the building plus any garrisoned inside.
- **Slay the Warlord:** If the enemy Warlord is slain, score **1 victory point**.

---

## Cities of Death

In the nightmare of the far future, armies battle to annihilation amid the shattered ruins of vast corpse-strewn cities. The **Cities of Death** expansion recreates brutal, close-confines urban warfare.

### Description

- Cities are **bombed from orbit** and overrun by hordes of aliens or crushed beneath titanic war machines.
- Combatants fight **bitter close-quarters battles** amidst crumbling buildings.
- Victory requires ruthlessness and determination to drive out enemies, eradicate firebases, and **level strongholds**.
- Every building, staircase, and hallway becomes a battleground.
- Soldiers engage in **desperate, brutal tactics** including hand-to-hand combat when ammunition is low.
- Territory is crucial; lives are cheaper; survival is nearly impossible.

### Warfare Dynamics

- Fast-moving armies can get bogged down in intense urban fighting.
- **Ruined buildings** provide elevated firing positions and cover.
- Assault forces use grenades and flamers to clear pockets of resistance.
- Key city locations become bunkers, field hospitals, or command posts.
- Buildings may be rigged with **deadly traps**.
- Small squads perform hit-and-run tactics, raids through sewer networks, and cover darkness operations.

---

## Cities of Death Rules

### City Ruins

- Unless they can **FLY**, **VEHICLES, MONSTERS, and BIKES** can only end their move on the **ground floor** of ruins.
- **INFANTRY** can scale walls and move through windows, doors, and portals without impediment.
- Infantry on or behind ruins receive **cover benefits**.
- Infantry that do not move in their Movement phase add **+2** to saving throws against shooting attacks until they next move.
- Other units receive cover only if at least 50% of each model is obscured from the shooter.

### Height Advantage

- Models occupying upper levels of ruins gain **Height Advantage** when shooting at units at street level or lower levels.
- The target unit must be at least **3" below** all firing models' levels.
- Shooting with Height Advantage ignores target cover benefits.

### Streets and Roads

- Units moving entirely on streets or roads gain an extra **2" movement**.
- Units that Advance on streets/roads gain an extra **4" movement**.
- This does not apply to units that can FLY.

### Stratagems

#### Sewer Rats

- Used before setting up an INFANTRY unit.
- Instead of placing them on the battlefield, the unit infiltrates the sewer network.
- At the end of any Movement phase, deploy the unit anywhere at street level more than 9" from enemy models and not inside city ruins.

#### Medicae Facility

- Used after deployment and before the first round.
- Nominate a city ruin to house the **Medicae Facility**.
- Roll a dice each time a model in that ruin loses a wound; on a 6, the wound is healed and not lost.

#### Death in the Streets

- When a unit with Height Advantage shoots an enemy unit fully at street level and not in cover, re-roll all failed hit and wound rolls.

#### Booby Traps

- Used after deployment and before the first round.
- Secretly nominate a city ruin without models to contain **Booby Traps**.
- The first time any model enters this ruin, they suffer **D3 mortal wounds** (**D6** if Advancing).

### Fire in the Hole

- Grenades are especially effective in close urban combat.
- Re-roll all failed wound rolls for Grenades attacking targets in or on ruins.
- Grenades with random attacks always deal the **maximum number** of attacks when thrown at units in ruins.

---

## Cities of Death Stratagems

| Stratagem        | Cost |
|------------------|------|
| Firesweep        | 2CP  |
| Sewer Rats       | 1CP  |
| Medicae Facility | 1CP  |
| Death in the Streets | 1CP  |

---

## Firesweep Scenario

Both sides advance room-to-room, building-to-building, and street-to-street, attempting to claim city ruins and clear enemy forces.

### The Battlefield

- Contains several city ruins suitable for infantry combat and cover.
- Exposed roads provide challenging ground to cross.
- Terrain should include **obstacles, barricades, wreckage, and detritus** to offer shelter between buildings.

### The Armies

- Both players select **Battle-forged armies**.
- **No Fortifications** allowed.

### Objective Markers

- Place at least **6 objective markers** denoting critical city ruins.
- Players roll off; the highest scorer places the first marker.
- Players alternate marker placement until all 6 are placed.

## Objective Markers and Deployment

- **Objective markers** must each be located in a different **city ruin**.

### Deployment

- The player who placed the **sixth objective marker** picks one quarter of the battlefield for their **deployment zone**.
- Their opponent uses the **diagonally opposite** quarter of the battlefield as their deployment zone.
- Players alternate deploying their units, one at a time, starting with the player who did **not** pick their deployment zone.
- A player's models must be set up within their own deployment zone.
- Continue setting up units until both sides have set up their army.

### Power Level

- After deployment, determine each army’s **Power Level** by adding the **Power Ratings** of all its units.
- The player with the **lowest Power Level** is the **Underdog**.
- If the Power Levels are equal, the player who assigned deployment zones is the Underdog.
- If the difference between Power Levels is:
  - 10 to 19: Underdog receives **1 bonus CP**.
  - 20 to 29: Underdog receives **2 CPs**.
  - And so on.

### First Turn

- The player who completed setting up their army first can choose to take the **first or second turn**.

### Battle Length

- The game lasts for **6 battle rounds**.

### Victory Conditions

- At game end, the player controlling the most **Critical city ruins** earns a **major victory**.
- If tied, the **Underdog scores a minor victory**.
- A player controls a Critical city ruin if they have **more models** on or in that ruin than their opponent.

---

## Stronghold Assault

### Introduction

- Siege warfare is integral across the galaxy.
- One player is the **Attacker**, assaulting massive **monolithic fortresses**.
- The other player is the **Defender**, garrisoning fortifications, gun emplacements, and trenches.
- Strongholds are monumental, enduring centuries or even millennia of battle.
- Some fortresses house weapons capable of destroying colossal war machines or orbiting battleships.
- Defence lines and trench networks protect and connect bunkers and weapon towers.
- Fortifications require garrisons to realize their true defensive potential.
- Even a single squad in a bunker can pour down devastating firepower.
- Commanders seek control over strongpoints as they are **strategic lynchpins** for war efforts.
- Strongpoints are prime objectives and are heavily contested.

### History and Importance

- ManyImperium fortresses have been destroyed over millennia but many still stand as armored monuments.
- Fortresses withstand heavy bombardments and assaults but their fall often signals defeat.

---

## Stronghold Assault Rules

### Big Guns Never Tire

- The **Attacker's models** can move and shoot **Heavy weapons** at Bunkers or Fortresses without the typical **-1 penalty** to hit rolls.

### Demolitions

- When the **Attacker** rolls a **wound roll of 6+** against a **Bunker or Fortress**, the structure suffers a **mortal wound** in addition to other damage.

---

## Stronghold Defences

### Defence Lines

- Trenches or armored shield sections providing shelter.
- **Infantry models** within 1" behind a **Defence Line** (from firing unit’s perspective) gain **cover**.
- These models can take cover any time during the enemy turn, improving their **Save by 2** until the enemy’s next turn but cannot act.
- Enemy units can fight across a Defence Line even if the distance is more than 1".
- Units can fight across up to 2" in this case.
- To attack across a Defence Line, models must be either within 2" of the enemy unit or within 1" of a friendly unit that is itself within 2" of the enemy.

### Bunkers and Fortresses

- Used to shelter Defenders’ forces.
- Defenders may include any number of **Bunkers** and **Fortresses** in their army.
- Each is a single model occupying one **Fortifications Battlefield Role** slot.
- **Power Ratings**:
  - Bunker: 5
  - Fortress: 15
- Cannot move or fight. Enemy models automatically hit them in fights.
- Stats:
  - Toughness: 10
  - Save: 3+
  - Bunker Wounds: 15
  - Fortress Wounds: 30
- Fortress has **Ballistic Skill 5+**, equipped with:
  - Two **Icarus lascannons**
  - One **missile silo**
  - Up to four **heavy bolters**

- Infantry units can **garrison** Bunkers and Fortresses (up to 20 models in a Bunker, 40 in a Fortress).
- Garrisoned units can **shoot** but generally cannot act or be affected.
- If destroyed, garrisoning units must **disembark**.
- After destruction, roll one die per disembarked model: for rolls 1, 2, or 3, a model is slain (player’s choice).

### Captured Fortress

- Undefended strongholds can be captured and controlled by the Attacker.
- Buildings can change hands multiple times during battle.

---

## Stronghold Assault Stratagems

- Players may use additional Stratagems depending on their role as Attacker or Defender.

### Sappers (Attacker)

- Use just before a unit fights a Bunker or Fortress.
- Add **+1** to all wound rolls for that unit against the Bunker or Fortress during that fight phase.
- **Cost:** 1 CP

### Escape Hatch (Defender)

- Use when one of your Bunkers or Fortresses is destroyed.
- Garrisoning models are slain only on a roll of 1 instead of 1, 2, or 3.
- **Cost:** 1 CP

---

## Bunker Assault Scenario

### Setup

- One side defends behind unyielding bunkers, halting the advancing foe.
- The attacker must destroy or overwhelm bunkers rapidly to avoid bombardment.
- Fortifications purchased must be placed wholly within their controlling player’s half of the table.

### Armies

- Players choose Attacker and Defender.
- Power Level of the Attacker’s army should be greater.
- Defender must include at least one **Fortification Network Detachment** with 1 to 3 Bunkers and/or Fortresses.

### Battlefield

- Defender sets up Bunkers and Fortresses within their deployment zone.
- Sets up Defence Lines, then other terrain such as ruins or craters.

### Deployment

- Defender deploys their army first within their zone.
- Attacker deploys next within their zone.

### Targeting Auger

- After deployment, Defender selects a Bunker or Fortress to house the **Targeting Auger**.
- While garrisoned, the Defender can direct an artillery strike at the start of each Shooting phase:
  1. Place a marker anywhere on the battlefield.
  2. Opponent moves the marker **D6"** in any direction.
  3. Roll a die for each unit within 3" of the marker; on a 3+, that unit suffers **D3 mortal wounds**.

### First Turn

- The **Attacker** has the first turn.

### Battle Length

- The game lasts for **6 battle rounds**.

### Victory Conditions

- The player with the most **victory points** at game’s end wins.
- Tie results in a draw.
  
#### Victory Points

- **No Quarter Given:** Each player scores 1 VP for each enemy unit destroyed.
- **Rubble and Ruin:**
  - Attacker scores 3 VP for each Bunker destroyed or captured and held at game end.
  - Defender scores 3 VP for every other Bunker still on the battlefield.
  - Each Fortress is worth 6 VP instead.

## Attacker’s Deployment Zone  
## Defender’s Deployment Zone  
## Defender’s Battlefield Edge  
## Attacker’s Battlefield Edge  
## Attacker’s Table Half  
## Defender’s Table Half
