# **Death from the Skies**  

Fire fills the skies as squadron after squadron of **aircraft** scream into battle. The **Death from the Skies expansion** allows players to recreate battles where squadrons of aircraft are critical to success and where skilled **aces** engage in fast-paced **dogfights** for dominance of the skies.  

Hurtling into battle with guns spitting death, wings of **combat aircraft** fight their own war high above the blood-soaked battlefield. The clouds burn as squadrons of aircraft tear across the skies and engage in deadly combat.  

Even as mighty armies clash upon war-torn battlefields, the skies above play host to battles of their own. Swift fighter wings dogfight furiously, and ace pilots prey upon their victims with sublime skill.  

Squadrons of **bombers** thunder through skies alive with flak, dropping ordnance into the swirling battle below. Meanwhile, **attack craft** punch through enemy fighter screens to strafe the foe and deliver warriors to the heart of battle.  

Everywhere, wise commanders seek to dominate the air, knowing that this will secure victory on the ground. Wings of lightning-fast jet fighters hurtle through acid squalls or weave between towers of megalithic cityscapes to blow enemy aircraft out of the skies.  

As their landbound comrades fight and die below, these courageous pilots engage in adrenaline-charged aerial duels where a split second’s hesitation means death.  

All the while, flights of bombers thunder into cauldrons of fire to hammer **shield generators**, **dark idols**, and **super-heavy war engines** with lethal ordnance. The destruction wrought by squadrons of heavy bombers obliterates such ground targets wholesale.  

Even as this carnage is unleashed, **aerial transports** and **gunships** swoop from on high. Strafing runs shred infantry formations, gunning down bestial monsters and turning enemy tanks into fireballs, before disgorging hordes of battle-ready killers from their armoured holds.  

Whether forging through sentient **rust-cyclones** or engaging winged **Daemons** in the starlit void of space, squadrons of aircraft rule the war-torn heavens.  

The first moments of a **dogfight** are crucial; pilots jockey for position, attempting to tail their quarry and line up for the kill shot. It is an aerial dance in which the slightest mistake can be fatal.  

An aircraft may be forced to **bug out**, temporarily leaving combat airspace, usually to shake off enemy fighters. Though it avoids imminent destruction, its absence leaves allies on the ground unprotected and at the mercy of deadly strafing fire and bombing runs until it can return to wreak vengeance.  

---

## Death from the Skies Missions - Additional Rules  

### Flyers  

- All **Flyers** – units specifically with the **Flyer Battlefield Role** – can make use of the expanded Flyer rules below.  
- Flyers have four 90° arcs: one **front**, one **rear**, and two **side** arcs.  

### Dogfight Phase  

- Aircraft duel in the **Dogfight phase**, which is an extra phase between Movement and Psychic phases each turn.  
- During this phase, Flyers can only target enemy Flyers with shooting attacks.  
- Players alternate selecting their Flyers and target enemy Flyers to perform Dogfights.  
- Flyers shoot as if it were the Shooting phase but can only shoot their targeted Flyer and cannot use bombs or similar ordnance.  
- Only weapons in the correct arc can shoot:
  - **Turret weapons**: any direction  
  - **Tail-mounted weapons**: rear arc only  
  - All other weapons: front arc only  
- To determine which weapons can fire, draw a line from the center of your Flyer to the center of the target Flyer.  

### Hit Roll Modifiers Based on Target Arc  

- **Rear (Tailing): +2 to all hit rolls**  
- **Front (Head-on Pass): +1 to all hit rolls**  
- **Side (Deflection Shot): No modifier**  

- After resolving shots, the opponent chooses a Flyer to Dogfight, alternating until all desired Dogfights are resolved.  
- Flyers that shoot during Dogfight phase can still shoot during their Shooting phase but must choose ground targets then.  

### Leaving Combat Airspace  

- Flyers can move off the battlefield edge, termed as **Leaving Combat Airspace**, due to minimum move exceptions.  
- At the end of their next Movement phase, roll a D6 to attempt re-entry:  
  - On a 1 or 2, delayed and does not arrive this turn (roll again next turn).  
  - On a 3+, the Flyer arrives on the board touching any battlefield edge facing any direction and moves directly forward up to 6" (no further turn).  
- Flyers arriving this way are assumed to have moved their maximum distance for that movement.  
- Any Flyer still off the board by game end counts as destroyed for victory conditions.  

---

## Death from the Skies Stratagems  

### Evasive Manoeuvres  
- Use when one of your Flyers is targeted by an enemy Flyer in a Dogfight.  
- Re-roll all failed saving throws this phase for that Flyer.  
- Subtract 1 from all hit rolls made against it until the end of the turn.  
- Cost: 1 Command Point (CP)  

### Refuel, Rearm, Repair  
- Use as soon as one of your Flyers Leaves Combat Airspace.  
- Spend 1 CP: the aircraft automatically re-enters combat airspace at the end of your next Movement phase (no dice roll needed).  
- Spend 2 CPs: re-enters and regains any limited-use weapons (bombs, etc.).  
- Spend 3 CPs: re-enters, regains limited-use weapons, and regains D3 wounds.  

---

## Death From The Skies Tactical Strike  

A window of opportunity has arisen for your bombers and ground-attack craft to strike strategically vital ground targets. The Attacker must strike fast as the Defender scrambles fighters to intercept.  

### The Armies  

- Players choose who is the **Attacker** and who is the **Defender**.  
- Both select a Battle-forged army including at least one **Air Wing Detachment**.  
- Defenders should include some **Fortifications** for shelter.  
- Attacker's Power Level should be higher than the Defender's.  

### The Battlefield  

- Create a battlefield large enough to accommodate both armies with suitable terrain.  
- Defender’s deployment zone should have defensible terrain such as **ruins** for shelter.  
- Defender sets up 5 **Objective Markers** denoting Attacker’s **Ground Objectives**.  
- Objectives can be placed anywhere not in terrain or on Fortifications with Wounds, at least 6" apart.  

### Deployment  

- Defender deploys their army within their zone first.  
- Attacker sets up their army within their deployment zone afterwards.  

### Ground Objective  

- Attacker must target and destroy the Ground Objectives.  
- If on a Fortification, objective is destroyed when Fortification is destroyed.  
- Underground targets (not on terrain) have **Toughness 6**, **Save 4+**, and **10 Wounds**.  
- Ground Objectives are hit automatically in fights (no hit rolls).  

### Bunker Busters  

- Attacker adds +1 to all hit and wound rolls made by their Flyers targeting Ground Objectives.  

### First Turn  

- The Attacker has the first turn.  

### Battle Length  

- Game lasts for 6 battle rounds.  

### Victory Conditions  

- **4 or more** Ground Objectives destroyed: Attacker wins a **major victory**.  
- **2 or fewer** destroyed: Defender wins a **major victory**.  
- **3** destroyed with Attacker's Power Level at least 10 higher: Defender wins a **minor victory**.  
- Otherwise, the battle is a **draw**.  

---

## Multiplayer Battles  

Rules for **Warhammer 40,000** are designed for battles between two players but can be adapted for multiplayer with three or more participants. Each player strives separately to defeat all opponents.  

### General Setup  

- Multiplayer battles can have as many sides as players.  
- All other players’ models are enemy models to each player.  

### Missions  

- Best played with missions designed for multiplayer, e.g., **Carnage**.  
- Many two-player missions can be modified for multiplayer with guidelines:  

### The Armies  

- At least three players required.  
- Each selects an army independently.  

### Battle Rounds  

- Each battle round split into three or more turns (one per player).  
- At the start of every round, players roll off for turn order.  
- Highest roller chooses which player goes first.  
- After a player’s turn, remaining players roll off for next turn order.  
- This repeats until all players have had a turn, then the round ends.  

### Psychic Phase  

- Only one player may attempt to resist a successfully manifested **psychic power**.  
- If multiple players wish to resist, the active player chooses who may attempt.  

### Charge Phase  

- After a player has moved all charging models, other players can attempt **Heroic Interventions**.  
- The order of Heroic Interventions is decided by the player whose turn it is.  

---

*Blessed is the mind too small for doubt.*  
*Thought for the day: Only in death does duty end.*  
*Thought for the day: An open mind is like a fortress with its gate unbarred and unguarded.*  
*A weapon cannot substitute for zeal.*

## Heroic Intervention

An **enemy CHARACTER** can only perform a **Heroic Intervention** if it is within **3"** of a model controlled by the player whose turn it is.

## Fight Phase

- Any unit that has models within **1"** of an enemy unit can **Fight** in this phase.
- Models can attack any enemy models, not just those belonging to the player whose turn is taking place.
- Units that charged this turn **Fight first** as normal.
- Then, the player whose turn it is chooses an order for all players (including themselves) to select a unit to **Fight** with, before the next player chooses a unit.
- Continue going around in the same order until all eligible units that you want to Fight have done so.
- If one player completes all of their units’ Fights first, or they don’t have any units that can Fight, the other players complete all of their remaining Fights, one unit after another, in the same order.
- No unit can **Fight** more than once in each Fight phase.

## Morale Phase

- In the Morale phase, all players must take **Morale tests** for units from their army that have had models slain during the turn.
- The player whose turn it is tests first and then decides the order in which the other players will take their Morale tests.

## Multiplayer Stratagem

### Bribe Stratagem

- In multiplayer missions, each player can use **Command Points (CPs)** to use the following Stratagem:
  
  - You can use this Stratagem at any time to give any number of your remaining CPs to another player to bargain for a temporary **ceasefire**, **alliance**, **betrayal**, etc.

## Hints & Tips

- In a battle fought between three or more opponents, each general must be **cunning**.
- You must be able to set foes against each other, form temporary alliances, and know when to betray someone before they betray you.
- A successful general must be willing to use **underhand ploys** and tactics to win a battle!

---

## Multiplayer Battle: Carnage

### Overview

- Several armies converge on the same battlefield, each determined to capture it for themselves.
- Make whatever truces you must and betray whomever you wish, but be careful — when the battle is over, there can be **only one victor**.

### The Armies

- You will need **three or four players**.
- Each must select a **Battle-forged army**.

### The Battlefield

- Create a battlefield and set up terrain large enough to accommodate up to four armies.
- Place a single **objective marker** in the centre of the battlefield.

### Deployment

- The battlefield is divided into **quarters**.
- Players roll off; the winner chooses one quarter as their **deployment zone**.
- Remaining players roll off, selecting the remaining quarters in turn.
- Players alternate deploying units starting with the first player who chose their deployment zone.
- Models must be set up in their own deployment zone, more than **9"** from the centre of the battlefield.
- Continue deploying units until all armies are set up.

### Power Level and Ranking

- After deployment, add together the **Power Ratings** of all units in each army to determine their **Power Level**.
- Rank armies from highest to lowest Power Level.
- If two have the same Power Level, roll off to decide the higher rank.

### First Turn

- The player with the **lowest rank** chooses who has the first turn during the first battle round.
- The player with the second lowest rank chooses who has the second turn, and so on.

### Battle Length

- The game lasts for **5 battle rounds**.

### Victory Conditions

- If one player’s army has slain all foes, they win a **major victory**.
- Otherwise, the player with the most **victory points** wins a major victory.
- If two or more players are tied for the highest victory points, the player with the **lowest rank** wins a **minor victory**.

### Victory Points

- **Dominate the Field**: At the end of each battle round, the objective marker is worth 1 victory point to the player who controls it.
- A player controls the objective if they have more models within **3"** of the centre of the marker than any enemy models.

---

## Campaigns

### Introduction

- Campaigns add meaning to victories and defeats by telling a story that unfolds with every new engagement.
- The results of each battle affect the next one in a series of linked games.
- Campaigns develop the **narrative** of your army, with characters gaining reputations, rivalries, and history.

### Benefits of Campaigns

- Provides a clear structure and greater significance for every battle.
- Armies gain **battle honours**, and commanders hone their skills over time.
- Friendly rivalries develop, giving opportunities to capitalize on victories or seek retribution for defeats.

### Types of Campaigns

#### Tree Campaigns

- A series of linked games where the outcome of each battle affects the conditions for the next.
- Example chain of battles:
  
  - **Patrol** (Defender vs. Attacker)
  - **Ambush!**
  - **Sabotage**
  - **Blitz**
  - **Meat Grinder**
  - **Rescue**

- Winning or losing a battle determines the next mission and its unique bonuses or penalties.

#### Matrix Campaigns

- Require forward planning with each battle influenced by players’ secret choices.
- Players select a strategy from a list before each battle.
- The matrix of choices determines the mission and attacker/defender roles.
- Can be reused or modified throughout the campaign with additional bonuses or penalties.

#### Map Campaigns

- Use a geographical setting that evolves over time.
- Each player starts with territory on a grid or Realm of Battle board.
- Territory is taken or lost based on battle results.
- Additional rules can cover supply lines, reinforcements, or natural disasters.

### The Next Step

- Beginners should start with small campaigns with manageable objectives like capturing an outpost.
- Experienced players can dive into epic narrative campaigns involving creative talents and expansive battlefield setups.
- Campaigns encourage multiplayer battles with alliances and expanding armies.

### Matrix Campaign Example

| Warlord A's Choice | Advance             | Hold                      | Reconnoitre             | Flank                  | Reinforce              |
|--------------------|---------------------|---------------------------|-------------------------|------------------------|------------------------|
| **Advance**        | Retrieval Mission (pg 218) | Blitz (pg 202)<br>(Warlord B Attacker) | Patrol (pg 200)<br>(Warlord B Attacker) | Ambush! (pg 198)<br>(Warlord A Attacker) | No Mercy (pg 219)      |
| **Hold**           | Blitz (pg 202)<br>(Warlord A Attacker) | Deadlock (pg 235)        | Cleanse and Capture (pg 230) | Meat Grinder (pg 196)<br>(Warlord B Attacker) | Meat Grinder (pg 196)<br>(Warlord A Attacker) |
| **Reconnoitre**    | Patrol (pg 200)<br>(Warlord A Attacker) | Cleanse and Capture (pg 230) | Patrol (pg 200)<br>(choose Attacker randomly) | The Scouring (pg 220)   | Sabotage (pg 204)<br>(Warlord B Attacker) |
| **Flank**          | Ambush! (pg 198)<br>(Warlord B Attacker) | Meat Grinder (pg 196)<br>(Warlord A Attacker) | The Scouring (pg 220)   | Cloak and Shadows (pg 234) | Ambush!               |

- For matrix campaigns, players simultaneously reveal choices and cross-reference the matrix to determine the mission and roles.

- "Thought for the day: Only in death does duty end."
- "We must be unsleeping in vigilance, swift in judgement, merciless in deed."

## 273  
So does the cycle of **eternal strife** continue. The grinding wheels of **conflict crush the bodies of men** and the **souls of gods** until all that is left is dust. Even those who fall do not know **peace**, for as one battle ends, another begins, and then another.  

To hope for a better world is to embrace **futility and despair**. In this world, in this cosmos, in this reality and the next, a single stark truth abides: **There is only war**.  

**FAITH WITHOUT DEEDS IS WORTHLESS.**

---

## APPENDIX

### DAEMONS  
That there are **Daemons** abroad in the universe, and the link that these entities have with the **warp**, is not a commonly known or understood phenomenon within the broader community of the **Imperium**.  

There are various reasons for this. Quite apart from the rarity of encounters with the denizens of the warp, the **hierarchy of the Imperium** has always sought to suppress such knowledge. What little awareness exists amongst the peoples of the Imperium is never openly or officially acknowledged. Tales of the warp, and its unpleasant inhabitants, are dismissed as scaremongering or mere superstition.  

The Imperium, or at least its more senior agents, is quite determined to prevent the spread of **daemonic infestation**. It is known amongst the **cognoscenti** that the ways of the Daemon are **deceitful and devious** and that they have subtle ways to infiltrate human societies and influence the human mind.  

Many are the strange, twisted cults and secretive covens of Daemon worshippers that have inveigled themselves into the worlds of the Imperium throughout the course of its long history. Wherever possible, these cults are **unearthed and eradicated**, but not without great cost of lives, property and sanity.  

There is also the very real threat of **possession**, which, although very rare, is nonetheless feared above all other outcomes. A Daemon with such a foothold in **realspace** is both difficult to identify, at least in the early stages of possession, and a deadly and dangerous foe.  

Furthermore, the Daemon is always intent on spreading its taint by establishing **cult worship** and encouraging yet more possessions. Unchecked, such a creature can wreak untold damage in both the **physical and metaphysical spheres**.  

However, the primary motivation for keeping knowledge of Daemons secret is to ensure that the greater population is not catastrophically disturbed by such revelations and driven to **madness, despair and mass civil unrest** through the knowing of them.  

There is a world of difference between understanding that there are vile, antipathetic **alien species** at large in the universe and knowing that one’s **immortal soul** is at risk from predation by unholy daemonic entities from a **hellish dimension** a mere thought away from our own.  

Also, as dangerous as warp travel may be perceived to be, if the general populace were to realise that it was, in fact, through a realm inhabited by Daemons, it is unlikely that anyone would willingly submit themselves to such a means of transport or trust any of the **astropathic messages** sent through it. The resultant anarchy would be threat enough to completely destabilise an already strained Imperium.  

Thus, only the most **stout-hearted and iron-willed** are permitted to know and retain knowledge of the Daemons and their masters, the **Dark Gods**. The bearers of this knowledge are few, and they share this information reluctantly.  

The **Inquisition**, their erstwhile allies, the **Grey Knights**, and a few others are among the tiny number of humans who are allowed to know of the Daemons’ existence. Most others who come into contact with them are culled to prevent both the promulgation of knowledge and the possible spread of daemonic taint.  

If they are of sufficient value to the Imperium, they are instead **mind-wiped** to erase all memories of the encounter.  

---

### ASTROPATHIC COMMUNICATION  
A brief treatise on the basics of **Astropathic transmission** (Imp. Ref. 0253870007/SA).  

There are many methods of communication within a single planetary orbit and even within compact star systems, ranging from the mundane to the esoteric. However, the majority of the Imperium’s colonised worlds are so far apart from other star systems that other means are required to stay in contact with the wider Imperium. To pass messages over such great interstellar distances requires the skills and powers of an **Astropath**.  

Astropaths are the most common sanctioned **psykers** in the Imperium, having escaped the cruel fate that awaits those without the strength of mind to control their powers, or the will and determination to survive the Imperium’s strict training regimes.  

All major organisations of the **Adeptus Terra**, from the bureaucratic branches of the **Administratum** to the furtive offices of the **Inquisition**, use Astropaths to communicate with each other across the vast distances of the galaxy. These psykers can be found working alongside starship captains, rogue traders, planetary governors and officers from all branches of the military.  

The **Adeptus Ministorum** makes extensive use of Astropaths, and has built vast amphidomes and psi-comm spires that rise high over every shrine world, aiding their spiritual broadcasts and creating an interlocking transmission web that at least partially connects many dioceses and parishes, though the most powerful can even reach some of the far missionaries on the edges of the Imperium.  

It is said that the **Emperor**, the greatest of all psychic minds, once held full telepathic conversations with **Malcador the Hero**, himself a mighty telepath. Though they were at opposite ends of the known galaxy, there was no time delay to speak of, and they may as well have been in the same room.  

Although human psykers of such extreme potency no longer stride among the stars, so long as the **warp** is relatively calm, the most powerful Astropaths can single-handedly send messages across several star systems with some accuracy. If all goes well, telepathic communications travel quickly through the warp, crossing many thousands of light years, becoming fainter and fainter, before eventually fading out altogether.  

Still, such communications vary widely based on the **mental strength** of the sender, the ability of the receiver to absorb such incoming messages and, perhaps most of all, the unpredictable nature of the warp itself.  

When the galactic distance required of a transmission is so great that a single Astropath proves insufficient, it is common for them to work in relays, sending messages to various beacons, hubs and **Imperial sub-stations** to pass along.  

It is also possible to boost a message by using an **Astropath Choir** – a group working in synchronicity to broadcast or receive complex messages over unimaginable distances.  

It is too complicated and variable to list all of the methods and processes involved in Astropath communications, but the following generalisations should help even a novice understand some of the difficulties of the medium.  

There are, after all, dozens of types of **Trance Broadcasts** alone, to mention nothing of **Station Reception**, **Astral Projection** or the nearly infinite styles of **Divination** practised by Astropaths within (and beyond) the purview of **Imperial Sanction**.  

Using mesmeric chants to enter a deep trance, a typical Astropath forms the message within his mind and sends it through the warp. The progress of the message is rather like a stone dropped into a pool, as it creates a series of ripples that extend outwards through the immaterium. Some psychics are able to project the message so that it travels only in a desired direction, but even then, some echoes are likely to lap outwards.  

Once projected, a message hurtles through the warp until its energy is lost and it fades away, typically a gradual process, but the immaterium is anything but predictable.  

Communications of this kind have many restrictions; they are brief in length, perhaps comprising only a few images or sentences depending on how the Astropath works (psychics are as likely to work in abstract pictures and emotions as they are words).  

As with all things, the very chaos of the warp can alter the form of a message, if only rarely its intent. Unless powered by a mighty source, longer or more complex messages risk getting unravelled in the ripples of the warp, arriving in a jumbled order and risking further, if not complete, distortion.  

**Warp interference** is common, as messages can be delayed, muddled or contaminated by any number of fluctuations, such as shifts in warp tides or the intermingling of multiple telepathic signals.  

**Raging warp storms** can redirect or simply swallow and destroy messages, blocking communiqués for centuries.  

Any Astropath can pick up **Trance Broadcasts**, although in general it can be said that more discipline is needed to receive messages than to send them.  

With outgoing messages, an Astropath can concentrate on the clarity of thought, on the message itself, pushing such deliberations deep into the warp. Astropaths in such a trance and actively receiving incoming messages are particularly vulnerable – their minds must open to the eternal noise of that erratic and highly dangerous realm.  

Not only must an Astropath attempt to sift out the senseless static of passing currents, they must also contend with the residue of ancient messages that sometimes (for no logical reason) drift endlessly, not losing power but continuing to call from some distant past, faint waves of energy lapping across the void.  

The repercussive **warp-waves** of major events or cataclysms can also be picked up, sometimes unintentionally, sending more sensitive Astropaths into fits or burning out their minds altogether with the onslaught.  

Ominously, some telepathic impulses attract unwanted attention – mischievous **warp entities** that attempt to alter messages, making them misleading or obscene, redirecting them to the wrong recipient, or perhaps even attaching themselves to the mental transmissions, piggybacking on the message to its final destination.  

Although rare, it is possible for **Daemons** themselves to become aware of and attracted to the psychic signals hurtling through their realm. On occasion, they will even trace them back to their source, searching for a way to establish a claw-hold in realspace.  

An Astropath who wishes to send a singular message to a specific location – whether it is a particular spacecraft, planet, hive or even an individual – must be able to concentrate his mind to a degree that is unimaginable to a normal human.  

These messages are launched into the warp not as ripples extending outwards in all directions, but as a single bolt of **pure thought**. The recipient must be prepared to receive such a powerful transmission, though it is still possible for those in **Sweeping Trance Reception** to pick up snippets of such messages if they happen to pass through their area of their psychic awareness on the way to their destination.  

Success of this kind is linked more to **random chance** than any degree of skill or accuracy on the part of the recipient.  

The need for interstellar communication is enormous, and the **Scholastica Psykana** is constantly bombarded with requests for sanctioned Astropaths.  

They are a common sight in the more civilised sectors of the Imperium, easily distinguished by their **green robes** and sightless, sunken eye sockets.  

---

**EXCUSES ARE THE REFUGE OF THE WEAK.**

## Astropaths and Soul Binding

Although only released for duty once they have cleared all **sanctioning tests** and the holy ritual known as the **Soul Binding**, in which they face the psychic might of the **Emperor himself**, the nature of their occupation puts them in nearly constant danger. There have been documented cases of **Astropaths becoming corrupted** (see crossfile, datascroll Ref. 0062132005).

## High Lords of Terra

### Overview

The **High Lords of Terra** are the governing body of the **Imperium**, tasked with interpreting the **Emperor’s will** and enacting his rule across the largest empire in the galaxy. On their command, the armies of the Imperium move; only their edict can approve a **Space Marine Founding**, and on their orders the **Black Fleet** sails and their grim tithes are collected.

### Formation and Origins

The **Senatorum Imperialis** has roots in ruling bodies formed before the birth of the Imperium. At the beginning of the age, the **Emperor** himself ruled but formed a council of advisors comprised of key individuals such as the **Fabricator General of Mars**, the **Paternova of the Navigator Houses**, and **Malcador the Sigillite**, perhaps the Emperor’s greatest ally during the **Unification Wars of Terra**.

When the Emperor left Terra to lead the **Great Crusade**, he left **Malcador** as regent. During the Great Crusade, the Emperor discovered the lost **Primarchs** and relied on his battle council.

### The Council of Terra

After the decisive victory at the **Battle of Ullanor**, the Emperor left military matters to **Horus**, his newly appointed **Warmaster**, and returned to Terra. He formed the **Council of Terra**, formalizing the role of his advisors, initially starting with a half-dozen men.

This council became the governing body managing the complex bureaucracy of the new empire. Under **Malcador**, the **Adeptus Administratum** was born and new branches formed beneath it.

### Military and Political Tensions

The council coexisted with the **Primarchs**, who headed military branches under the Warmaster. This caused resentment among some Primarchs, which arguably contributed to several becoming corrupted by the **Ruinous Powers**.

### After the Horus Heresy

Following the **Horus Heresy**, the Emperor was interred upon the **Golden Throne** and could no longer rule directly. His final instructions concerned the governance of the Imperium.

With Malcador gone, **Roboute Guilliman**, Primarch of the **Ultramarines**, established the **Senatorum Imperialis**, now known as the **High Lords of Terra**. He became the **Lord Commander of the Imperium**, a title replacing **Warmaster**.

### Structure of the High Lords of Terra

The ruling council's number was set at twelve, fluctuating over time but typically returning to this number. Each seat is held by leaders from the most powerful Imperium organizations.

A complex web of **tradition**, **skulduggery**, **promises**, and **threats** binds the High Lords together, deciding officeholders. Some offices are so vital that their chiefs almost always occupy seats on the council.

### Permanent Seats

The following offices are almost invariably represented on the High Lords due to their importance:

- **Lord Commander of the Imperium**, Roboute Guilliman  
- **Master of the Administratum**  
- **Fabricator General of the Adeptus Mechanicus**  
- **Paternoval Envoy of the Navigators**  
- **Inquisitorial Representative**  
- **Master of the Adeptus Astra Telepathica**  
- **Ecclesiarch of the Adeptus Ministorum**  
- **Grand Master of the Officio Assassinorum**  
- **Master of the Astronomican**

These nine posts are virtually sacrosanct, and they have rarely been left empty without successors from the same organizations.

### Notable Details on Representation

- The **Inquisitorial Representative** seat is held by whoever the Inquisition sends for each session, not by a specific Inquisitor.  
- The **Paternoval Envoy** is held by the current envoy of the **Paternova** family of Navigators. The Paternova himself never leaves the **Palace of Navigators**.  

### Additional Seats

The remaining three seats are typically filled by officials such as:

- **Lord Commander of Segmentum Solar**  
- **Lord Commander Militant of the Astra Militarum**  
- **Lord High Admiral of the Imperial Navy**  
- **Cardinal(s) of the Holy Synod of Terra**  
- **Abbess Sanctorum of the Adepta Sororitas**  
- **Captain-General of the Adeptus Custodes**  
- **Grand Provost Marshal of the Adeptus Arbites**  
- **Chancellor of the Estate Imperium**  
- **Speaker for the Chartist Captains**

### Space Marines and the High Lords

Few members of the **Adeptus Astartes** have served as High Lords despite their importance. This was likely intentional by Guilliman, who believed Space Marines' duty was to serve, not rule, Mankind—as per his **Codex Astartes**.

### History and Challenges

The High Lords have undergone many changes, including:

- Adding the **Ecclesiarch** after the **Imperial Cult** became the sole religion in early **M32**.  
- Being wiped out by assassination in an event called **“the Beheading”** on orders of a slighted **Grand Master of the Officio Assassinorum**.  
- Dissolution by the Ecclesiarch during the civil war known as the **Age of Apostasy**.  

Despite these power struggles, the High Lords of Terra continue interpreting the **Will of the Emperor** and governing the largest empire in the galaxy.

## Excerpts on Warp Travel

### Notes of Sharim Calypso

**Sharim Calypso**, Adjutant advisor to the **Imperial Navy**, records observations in Ref. MCS17-82h.57c.

The **Questio Logisticus** branch of the **Adeptus Administratum** tracks median travel via common **warp routes**. Though only two millennia of data exist, it confirms the danger of warp travel.

The **Proxxian traders** operate in the **Nephilim Sector**, transporting forced labour from the hive world of **Proxx** to mining colonies on **Hephastian** about three times a Terran year. This short distance requires fleet travel through the **immaterium**.

### Warp Route Observations

- The route is highly unpredictable despite a “semi-fluctuating” stable classification.  
- Typical voyages range from one to six weeks.  
- Extreme voyages have lasted from two minutes to 1,200 years.  
- About 22% of expeditions have not arrived, though many may still be en route.  
- Longer journeys increase the risks drastically.

### Conclusion on Warp Travel

Further computations offer little new insight. The old Navigator maxim, "**Trust in the Emperor’s Light**," remains the only truism about warp travel.

## STC Systems

### Definition and Purpose

Created at the peak of the **Age of Technology**, the **Standard Template Construct (STC)** system enabled all human colonies to build anything needed—air-purifiers, military weapons, habitation buildings, and plasma reactors.

The system calculates the most efficient way to construct requested items based on local materials and manufacturing means.

### User Accessibility

STCs were designed so even the least accomplished users could fabricate vehicles, buildings, or weapons. These systems represented humanity’s zenith of technical knowledge.

Every human colony had at least one STC system, though many colonists used only the more rudimentary templates, rarely attempting the advanced constructs.

### Decline and Loss

Over time, most STC machines were:

- Lost or destroyed in battle or natural disasters.  
- Corrupted due to failing databanks or jury-rigged maintenance.  
- Worn out after thousands of years of use.

The gradual disappearance of STC systems marked a significant loss of technological heritage for humanity.

## STC Systems and the Age of Strife

Those **lucky planets** that maintained even a **partially working STC (Standard Template Construct) system** grew to guard it jealously as the **Age of Technology** slipped into the anarchic madness of the **Age of Strife**. Soon, the galaxy-wide realm of Man was fractured, each world cut off from all but its closest neighbours.

The madness, warfare, warp-spawned invasions, and the great backlash against technology ensured that few of the great works of the previous era survived. **Today, there are no surviving STC systems.**

It was common practice, beginning in the Age of Technology, for colonies to produce **hard copies** of many of the more standard designs. Over the years, these have been copied repeatedly with varying levels of accuracy. Now, any copy is a **rarefied item**, especially those carrying **first-generation printout information**.

During the **Great Crusade** and later the **Forging**, thousands of previously colonised planets were reclaimed for Humanity. Many **STC reproductions** were found, and it is rumoured that some partially working systems were unearthed.

These long-lost treasures were mostly discovered buried amidst the ruins of regressed worlds but occasionally found in locked vaults, guarded by those who no longer understood the name or purpose of STC. Such findings are greedily collected by the **Adeptus Mechanicus**, who study, hoard, worship, and copy them at their secretive forge worlds.

## Characteristics and Legacy of STC Designs

The **STC system** was pivotal in human development, resulting in many worlds utilising similar designs and machinery. Although millennia have wrought changes, many humans still adhere religiously to old designs intended to cope with the unpredictable nature of colonies.

STC designs were typically:

- Big and brutish
- Hard to damage
- Easy to repair

Examples of **recovered STC technology** still in use include:

- **Rhino Armoured Personnel Carrier**
- **Land Raider**
- Atmospheric pumps that keep air breathable in large hive-blocks

The Adeptus Mechanicus still searches for undiscovered templates or a fully functioning STC system. Until then, secrets remain lost, such as:

- The trident-shaped **Proteus Cannon of Mars**
- Force field generators guarding the **Palace of Xerxes**

These marvels' workings remain beyond even the most adept Tech-Priests.

## Abhumans

**Abhumans** are evolved from human stock but altered or mutated to varying degrees. Unlike true mutants, they:

- Conform to recognizable physical standards
- Breed true
- Are no more prone than humans to further mutation

There are billions of abhumans in the Imperium, tolerated and exploited similarly to the general population. They rarely reach positions of authority and often face derision, fear, or prejudice.

Many abhumans are recruited into the **Administratum** and its subdivisions, such as the **Imperial Guard** and the **Imperial Fleet**. In the Imperial Guard, they serve in dedicated, segregated squads or companies.

The **Adeptus Terra** officially recognises **seventy-three stable abhuman strains**. Of these:

- Forty-six types are extinct
- No records of twelve strains have been received for over a generation
- Fifteen strains remain with varied status and contested classification by the **Tithes Chamber Notaries, sub. Planetary Census (Abhumans)**

### Noteworthy Abhuman Strains

The most contentious group is the **Ogryn** (**Homo sapiens gigantus**) complex, officially seven types, including:

- Alpha
- Theta
- Type IV
- Type VIIa
- H.S. gigantus gigantus
- H.S. gigantus cranopus
- Grey Ogryns

Many experts doubt their classification, pending revision.

Other classified abhuman races include:

- **Ratlings (Homo sapiens minimus)**
- **Squats (Homo sapiens rotundus)**
- **Beastmen (Homo sapiens variatus)**
- **Troths (Homo sapiens verdantus)**
- **Longshanks (Homo sapiens elongatus)**
- **Pelagers (Homo sapiens oceanus)**
- **Felinids (Homo sapiens hirsutus)**
- **Neandors (Homo sapiens hyannothus)**

**Beastmen** face severe persecution and are on the **Register of Proscribed Citizens (Class A-G worlds)** by the **Adeptus Arbites**, forbidding their settlement on or transportation to more than 300,000 worlds and military conscription.

- Troths, Felinids, and Neandors are endemic to worlds Verdant, Carlos McConnell, and Hyannoth IV, respectively.
- Remaining abhuman races are variously distributed across the Imperium.

In some regions, they live in large colonies or populate entire worlds; in others, they are scarce or virtually unknown.

## Black Ships

The great fleet of **Black Ships** belongs to the **Adeptus Astra Telepathica**. Independent from the Imperial Navy, they are the **second-largest fleet** in the galaxy with many thousands of ships.

Only the highest-ranking **adepts** within Astra Telepathica know the fleet’s true scale and operation scope. New ships are constantly commissioned to replace losses and expand the fleet.

Each year, more Imperium planets are visited and stripped of their **psykers**, who are transported to Terra.

### Crews and Operations

- Captains and senior officers are senior adepts of the Adeptus Astra Telepathica.
- Crews are indentured workers from Imperial worlds near Terra, recruited under ancient contracts in exchange for exemption from Imperial Tithes.
- All crew undergo rigorous testing for latent psychic abilities and regular mind-scrubbing to remove taint or infection.
- Navigators working for the fleet are exclusively members of the **Granicus, Ptolemy, and MacPherson Navigator Houses** serving the Astra Telepathica.
- **Inquisitors** have secured **Rights of Passage** aboard Black Ships, travelling freely and overseeing difficult psyker incarcerations.
- Occasionally, Space Marines, Sisters of Battle, or high-ranking Adeptus Terra officials are permitted aboard by captain’s discretion.

### Conditions on Black Ships

Black Ships are harsh environments for psykers:

- Psychically sensitive crew stay on shielded upper decks away from containment holds.
- The holds employ numerous devices to confuse or disrupt psychic abilities.
- A troop of adepts focuses psychic energies into an **Occluding Sphere**—a metaphysical device disrupting nearby psykers' concentration and talents.
- Holds are filled with loud, discordant noise and dim lighting, frequently interrupted with strobing lights.
- Captives’ food and drink are laced with sedatives.
- Psykers are regularly moved between holds to maintain compliance.
- The most dangerous psykers are kept in isolated cells deep within the holds.

Each day, dozens of Black Ships arrive at Terra, disgorging thousands of psykers who proceed through processing, grading, and distribution to institutions according to the Tithe.

## Combat Life Saver

### Lesson 243.77fIVs: How to Field Dress a Las Wound

**Laser weapons** are easy to produce and maintain, making them some of the most common weapons in the galaxy. They do not fire projectiles or slugs but instead emit a **high-energy pulse**.

- The beam’s strength varies by the weapon size and power source rating.
- The largest weapons, like **lancestrike batteries** on Imperial Navy spacecraft, can sear away entire hab-blocks, leaving huge craters.
- More commonly, smaller weapons like **laspistols** can vaporise a foe’s face, penetrating skull and brain, causing instant death.

A **las-pulse** causes:

- A **cauterised hole** surrounded by blister-burns
- An initial **flash-burn effect** from heat vaporising the surface area upon impact
- The flash resembles explosive wounds but differs significantly in treatment

The beam’s ongoing projection penetrates internal organs and can sever limbs, causing extensive damage.

### Steps to Treat a Las Wound:

1. **Approach**  
   Do not treat until removing the victim from the source. Las weapons produce a narrow, amplified beam, often in short bursts. If the beam persists, it is dangerous to approach as exposure will create more casualties.

2. **Expose**  
   Identify the impact site and assess the extent of the flash burn.

## Burn Treatment Guidelines

- **Lift away any clothing** covering the **burnt area**, without pulling material over the burns.
- **Leave in place** any material that has been **seared into the burn area**.
- If the victim is wearing **armour**, be aware that some materials **absorb heat**, leaving the area dangerous to touch.
- In a **hazardous environment** (such as chem-zones, rad-sites, or other dangerous areas), **do not cut away any protective covering** – apply the dressing directly **over it**.

### III) Evaluate

- Find the **penetration level** of the beam.
- Has the beam passed through the victim causing an **exit wound**?
- Check as soon as possible, since **extreme heat cauterises the wound**, leaving minimal bleeding.
- **Rapid swelling** will begin around the area almost immediately, making later diagnosis more difficult.
- If the **las wound** is only a **glancing hit** on a limb or shows no signs of striking a **vital organ**, proceed with **Field Dressing Type I**.
- If you suspect the las wound has penetrated a **vital organ**, go straight to **Type II**.

### IV) Field Dressing (Type I)

- Using the **cleanest material available**, place the cloth lightly over the burn, covering the entirety of the wound.
- If the victim is able, they may **hold the dressing in place**.
- Use strips to **bind in place** (wrapping around limbs or torso) and tie tightly enough to avoid slipping.
- **Do not break blisters or apply ointments** to flash burns.

### V) Field Dressing (Type II)

- **Cover the wound as quickly and completely as possible**.
- This is **cosmetic**, to hide the **lethal wound** from comrades and may also allow the victim some **false comfort**.
- The swelling that follows is bound to cause **catastrophic bodily failures**.
- **Death is effectively inevitable**, and redistribution of resources can commence immediately.

---

## Servitors and Servo-Skulls

### Duty to the Emperor beyond death

- **Servitors** and **servo-skulls** represent the lowest forms of servitude in the Imperium, continuing to serve even after death.

### Servitors

- **Basest form of biomechanical life** – task-adapted slaves.
- Mechanical components designed so the whole performs a **single laborious function**.
- Mindless machines of living flesh and metal that **obey programming without question**.
- A **servitor’s mind is essentially blank**, retaining only rudimentary instincts.
- Make up the bulk of the **Martian population**, working tirelessly across the Imperium.
- Adapted to work in **hostile environments** where unmodified humans would perish.
- Vary tremendously: 
  - Mechanical legs or arms for lifting
  - Computer terminals sprouting from bodies
  - Weapon-toting gun servitors
  - Heavy mining cyborgs
  - Holomats and living holographic recorders with bulging vid-lens optic receptors.
- Seen accompanying senior **Tech-Priests** on the battlefield, serving as **servants and guardians**, operating dangerous machinery or weaponry.

### Origins and Punishment

- Many servitors are adapted from artificially cultured drone bodies.
- Others are the remains of humans who have committed **terrible crimes**.
- The most severe punishment for criminals is to be turned into **servitors**, not death.
- The malefactor is **mind-wiped, augmented, and reprogrammed** to perform tedious functions.
- Ex-convict servitors wear a **brass plate** on their body proclaiming their crime as a warning.

### Servo-Skulls

- Fate of some who die in honoured service to the Emperor is to continue labor as a **servo-skull**.
- Made from **polished human craniums**, closely associated with the **Adeptus Mechanicus**.
- Seen assisting high-ranking **officers and officials** throughout the Imperium.
- Modified to facilitate **communications** or **archiving**.
- Equipped with:
  - Pict-recorders
  - Loud-hailers
  - Scrivening devices
  - Weapons
  - Simple manipulator pincers
  - Illumination emitters
  - Sensors or surgical tools, depending on needs
- Feature a tiny **gravity repulsor array** allowing them to float.
- Often sport **opulent, protective metal coatings** making them extremely durable.
- Often the last witness on battlefields, floating over ash and debris to attest to the **valour or cowardice** of those who died.
